% ==============================
%  Universality A: Finite shell thickness (Δk ≠ 0)
% ==============================

\section{Universality A: Robustness Under Finite Shell Thickness}

\subsection{Setup: isotropic broad-shell Landau--Brazovskii sector}

Let the quadratic kernel be isotropic and peaked on a shell of radius $k_0$:
\begin{equation}
G^{-1}(q)
=
r+\kappa\,(q^2-k_0^2)^2,
\qquad
q:=|\mathbf q|.
\end{equation}
We allow a finite shell thickness by restricting the fluctuation phase space to
\begin{equation}
\mathcal S_{\Delta k}
:=
\left\{\mathbf q\in\mathbb R^3:\; |q-k_0|\le \Delta k\right\},
\qquad
0<\Delta k\ll k_0,
\end{equation}
(or equivalently by an isotropic regulator that suppresses $|q-k_0|\gg \Delta k$).

The interaction is the usual quartic scalar vertex
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L_{\rm int}=\frac{u}{4!}\psi^4,
\qquad V_4=-u.
\end{equation}

For a candidate structure $S$ with $N_S$ plane waves on the $k_0$-shell,
define the purely geometric resonance-loop ratio
\begin{equation}
\mathcal C_S:=\frac{N_{{\rm loop},S}}{N_S^2},
\end{equation}
where $N_{{\rm loop},S}$ counts the non-trivial quartic resonance loops
(i.e.\ quartets with $\mathbf k_1+\mathbf k_2+\mathbf k_3+\mathbf k_4=\mathbf 0$
that are not reducible to the trivial $\pm$ pairings).

\subsection{Lemma: bubble integral remains structure-independent for finite $\Delta k$}

Define the broad-shell bubble integral
\begin{equation}
I_{\rm bubble}(r;\Delta k)
:=
\int_{\mathcal S_{\Delta k}}\frac{d^3q}{(2\pi)^3}\;
\frac{1}{\left[r+\kappa(q^2-k_0^2)^2\right]^2}.
\end{equation}

\begin{lemma}[Structure-independence of $I_{\rm bubble}$]
Assume:
(i) the propagator $G(q)$ depends only on $q=|\mathbf q|$ (isotropy),
(ii) the shell restriction/regulator is isotropic,
(iii) the vertex is local and momentum-independent at the quartic level.
Then $I_{\rm bubble}(r;\Delta k)$ is independent of the lattice candidate $S$.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Under (i)-(ii), the integration domain and integrand depend only on $q$,
hence $I_{\rm bubble}(r;\Delta k)$ is a function only of $(r,\Delta k;k_0,\kappa)$.
No information about the discrete reciprocal-star geometry $(S)$ enters this
radial integral. Condition (iii) guarantees the one-loop quartic correction
factorizes into this common integral times a purely combinatorial weight.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Proposition: BCC ranking is invariant under finite $\Delta k$}

At one loop, the quartic vertex renormalization at zero external momenta is
\begin{equation}
\delta\Gamma^{(4)}
=
\frac{u^2}{2}\,I_{\rm bubble}(r;\Delta k),
\end{equation}
so the effective quartic coefficient for structure $S$ takes the factorized form
\begin{equation}
\beta_{{\rm eff},S}(r;\Delta k)
=
\beta_{{\rm MF},S}
-
\frac{u^2}{2}\,I_{\rm bubble}(r;\Delta k)\,\mathcal C_S.
\label{eq:betaeff_dk}
\end{equation}

\begin{proposition}[Finite-thickness robustness of structural ranking]
Assume the hypotheses of the Lemma and that the mean-field quartic coefficients
$\beta_{{\rm MF},S}$ are fixed. Then for any $r$ and any $\Delta k$,
the structural ordering induced by the fluctuation term is governed solely by
$\mathcal C_S$. In particular, if
\begin{equation}
\mathcal C_{\rm BCC}>\mathcal C_{\rm FCC}>\mathcal C_{\rm SC},
\end{equation}
then for sufficiently deep in the fluctuation-dominated regime
(where the second term in \eqref{eq:betaeff_dk} dominates the differences),
\begin{equation}
\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm BCC}}(r;\Delta k)
<
\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm FCC}}(r;\Delta k)
<
\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm SC}}(r;\Delta k),
\end{equation}
and the BCC-favoring inequality is independent of $\Delta k$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By \eqref{eq:betaeff_dk}, for any pair $(S_1,S_2)$,
\begin{equation}
\beta_{{\rm eff},S_1}-\beta_{{\rm eff},S_2}
=
(\beta_{{\rm MF},S_1}-\beta_{{\rm MF},S_2})
-\frac{u^2}{2}I_{\rm bubble}(r;\Delta k)\,(\mathcal C_{S_1}-\mathcal C_{S_2}).
\end{equation}
The bubble factor $I_{\rm bubble}(r;\Delta k)$ is common to all structures.
Hence the fluctuation-driven ordering is determined solely by the sign of
$(\mathcal C_{S_1}-\mathcal C_{S_2})$.
In the regime where the fluctuation term dominates the inter-structure differences,
the ranking matches that of $\mathcal C_S$ and is independent of $\Delta k$.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Corollary: selection threshold shifts but hierarchy does not}

Define the selection threshold between BCC and FCC by
\begin{equation}
\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm BCC}}(r_{\rm sel};\Delta k)
=
\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm FCC}}(r_{\rm sel};\Delta k).
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\frac{u^2}{2}I_{\rm bubble}(r_{\rm sel};\Delta k)
=
\frac{\beta_{{\rm MF},{\rm BCC}}-\beta_{{\rm MF},{\rm FCC}}}
{\mathcal C_{\rm BCC}-\mathcal C_{\rm FCC}}.
\end{equation}
Thus $\Delta k$ shifts the numerical location of $r_{\rm sel}$ through
$I_{\rm bubble}(r;\Delta k)$, but cannot invert the BCC$>$FCC hierarchy
as long as $\mathcal C_{\rm BCC}>\mathcal C_{\rm FCC}$ and the isotropic
single-mode assumptions hold.

% ==============================
%  Universality B: Multi-component order parameter
% ==============================

\section{Universality B: Robustness Under Multi-Component Order Parameters}

\subsection{Setup: $n$-component field with isotropic quadratic shell}

Let $\Psi^a(x)$, $a=1,\dots,n$, be a real multiplet with isotropic quadratic kernel
\begin{equation}
\Gamma^{(2)}_{0,ab}(q)=\delta_{ab}\left[r+\kappa(q^2-k_0^2)^2\right],
\qquad
G_{ab}(q)=\delta_{ab}\,G(q),
\qquad
G(q)=\frac{1}{r+\kappa(q^2-k_0^2)^2}.
\end{equation}
Allow finite shell thickness by the same isotropic restriction/regulator as in Universality~A, so that
\begin{equation}
I_{\rm bubble}(r;\Delta k)
:=
\int_{\mathcal S_{\Delta k}}\frac{d^3q}{(2\pi)^3}\;
\frac{1}{\left[r+\kappa(q^2-k_0^2)^2\right]^2}
\end{equation}
remains structure-independent.

The most general quartic local interaction is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L_{\rm int}=\frac{1}{4!}\,u_{abcd}\,\Psi^a\Psi^b\Psi^c\Psi^d,
\qquad
u_{abcd}=u_{(abcd)}.
\end{equation}

\subsection{Invariant-coupling class}

We impose an internal symmetry that fixes $u_{abcd}$ to the $O(n)$-invariant form
\begin{equation}
u_{abcd}=u\left(\delta_{ab}\delta_{cd}+\delta_{ac}\delta_{bd}+\delta_{ad}\delta_{bc}\right).
\label{eq:Onvertex}
\end{equation}
(Equivalently: the interaction is $\frac{u}{4!}(\Psi^a\Psi^a)^2$.)

\subsection{Lemma: one-loop quartic renormalization factorizes into internal trace $\times$ shell integral}

Consider the one-loop bubble correction to the amputated four-point function
at vanishing external momenta. Using \eqref{eq:Onvertex} and $G_{ab}(q)=\delta_{ab}G(q)$,
\begin{equation}
\delta\Gamma^{(4)}_{abcd}
=
\frac12
\int_{\mathcal S_{\Delta k}}\frac{d^3q}{(2\pi)^3}\;
\Gamma^{(4)}_{abef}\,G_{eg}(q)\,G_{fh}(q)\,\Gamma^{(4)}_{ghcd}.
\label{eq:1loop4pt_tensor}
\end{equation}
Since $G_{eg}G_{fh}=\delta_{eg}\delta_{fh}G(q)^2$,
\eqref{eq:1loop4pt_tensor} becomes
\begin{equation}
\delta\Gamma^{(4)}_{abcd}
=
\frac12\,I_{\rm bubble}(r;\Delta k)\,
\Gamma^{(4)}_{abef}\Gamma^{(4)}_{efcd}.
\end{equation}
For the $O(n)$-invariant vertex \eqref{eq:Onvertex}, the tensor contraction closes on the same invariant:
\begin{equation}
\Gamma^{(4)}_{abef}\Gamma^{(4)}_{efcd}
=
\lambda_n\,u^2
\left(\delta_{ab}\delta_{cd}+\delta_{ac}\delta_{bd}+\delta_{ad}\delta_{bc}\right),
\label{eq:closure}
\end{equation}
with $\lambda_n>0$ depending only on $n$.

\begin{lemma}[$O(n)$ closure]
Under \eqref{eq:Onvertex}, the 1-loop correction preserves the $O(n)$-invariant tensor structure,
and only renormalizes the scalar coupling $u\mapsto u_{\rm eff}$:
\begin{equation}
u_{\rm eff}(r;\Delta k)=u-\frac{\lambda_n}{2}\,u^2\,I_{\rm bubble}(r;\Delta k).
\end{equation}
\end{lemma}

\subsection{Proposition: structural ranking is unchanged for $O(n)$ multiplets}

For a candidate structure $S$ with geometric ratio $\mathcal C_S=N_{{\rm loop},S}/N_S^2$,
the effective quartic coefficient entering the equal-amplitude Landau functional
inherits the same factorization as in the scalar case:
\begin{equation}
\beta_{{\rm eff},S}(r;\Delta k)
=
\beta_{{\rm MF},S}
-
\frac{\lambda_n}{2}\,u^2\,I_{\rm bubble}(r;\Delta k)\,\mathcal C_S.
\label{eq:betaeff_On}
\end{equation}

\begin{proposition}[$O(n)$ universality of BCC ranking]
Assume:
(i) isotropic single-shell quadratic kernel,
(ii) isotropic shell regulator (finite thickness allowed),
(iii) local $O(n)$-invariant quartic vertex \eqref{eq:Onvertex},
(iv) equal-amplitude star ansatz for each cubic structure.
Then the fluctuation-driven structural ordering is governed solely by $\mathcal C_S$,
independent of $(n,\Delta k)$.
In particular, if $\mathcal C_{\rm BCC}>\mathcal C_{\rm FCC}>\mathcal C_{\rm SC}$,
then in the fluctuation-dominated regime the hierarchy
\begin{equation}
\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm BCC}}<\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm FCC}}<\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm SC}}
\end{equation}
holds exactly as in the scalar theory.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Equation \eqref{eq:betaeff_On} shows that the structure-dependent part is only the geometric ratio
$\mathcal C_S$, while all dependence on internal multiplicity enters through the common positive prefactor
$\frac{\lambda_n}{2}u^2 I_{\rm bubble}$. Hence the sign of differences
$\beta_{{\rm eff},S_1}-\beta_{{\rm eff},S_2}$ in the fluctuation term is determined solely by
$\mathcal C_{S_1}-\mathcal C_{S_2}$, and the ranking is unchanged.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Corollary: selection threshold with $O(n)$ multiplets}

Define $r_{\rm sel}$ by $\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm BCC}}(r_{\rm sel};\Delta k)=\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm FCC}}(r_{\rm sel};\Delta k)$.
Then
\begin{equation}
\frac{\lambda_n}{2}\,u^2\,I_{\rm bubble}(r_{\rm sel};\Delta k)
=
\frac{\beta_{{\rm MF},{\rm BCC}}-\beta_{{\rm MF},{\rm FCC}}}
{\mathcal C_{\rm BCC}-\mathcal C_{\rm FCC}}.
\end{equation}
Thus $n$ (via $\lambda_n$) shifts the numerical value of $r_{\rm sel}$ but cannot invert the hierarchy
as long as the hypotheses of the Proposition hold.

% ==============================
%  Universality C: Higher-loop stability of ranking (within truncation class)
% ==============================

\section{Universality C: Higher-Loop Stability of the BCC Ranking}

\subsection{Class of theories and notion of ``ranking''}

We work within the same model class as Universality~A--B:
(i) isotropic single-shell quadratic kernel with possible finite thickness $\Delta k$,
(ii) local momentum-independent quartic vertex (scalar or $O(n)$-invariant multiplet),
(iii) equal-amplitude star ansatz for each candidate cubic structure.

For each structure $S$, write the fluctuation-corrected quartic coefficient as an asymptotic loop expansion
\begin{equation}
\beta_{{\rm eff},S}(r;\Delta k)
=
\beta_{{\rm MF},S}
+
\sum_{\ell\ge 1}\delta\beta_{S}^{(\ell)}(r;\Delta k),
\end{equation}
and define the \emph{ranking} at fixed $(r,\Delta k)$ by comparing $\beta_{{\rm eff},S}$ across $S$.

\subsection{Lemma: factorization of shell divergences vs.\ structural combinatorics}

Let $G(q)$ denote the isotropic near-shell propagator and let $\ell$ be the loop order.
For any $\ell$-loop contribution to the renormalized quartic vertex evaluated at zero external momenta,
define the corresponding shell integral magnitude
\begin{equation}
J_\ell(r;\Delta k)
:=
\int_{\mathcal S_{\Delta k}}\prod_{i=1}^{m_\ell}\frac{d^3q_i}{(2\pi)^3}\;
\mathcal K_\ell(\{q_i\})\;
\prod_{j=1}^{p_\ell} G(q_{a_j}) ,
\end{equation}
where $\mathcal K_\ell$ is a structure-independent isotropic kernel generated by contractions and
momentum routings, and $p_\ell$ is the number of internal propagator factors.

\begin{lemma}[Factorization within the isotropic single-shell truncation]
Within assumptions (i)--(ii), every $\ell$-loop correction to the quartic coefficient for structure $S$
admits a decomposition
\begin{equation}
\delta\beta_{S}^{(\ell)}(r;\Delta k)
=
\mathcal P_\ell(\mathcal C_S)\;
\Xi_\ell(r;\Delta k),
\label{eq:factorizationC}
\end{equation}
where:
\begin{itemize}
\item $\Xi_\ell(r;\Delta k)$ is a structure-independent (possibly divergent) shell integral depending only on
$(r,\Delta k;k_0,\kappa)$ and the internal multiplicity (e.g.\ $n$) through overall traces;
\item $\mathcal P_\ell$ is a polynomial with \emph{nonnegative} coefficients in the geometric ratio
$\mathcal C_S:=N_{{\rm loop},S}/N_S^2$.
\end{itemize}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Under isotropy and locality, all momentum integrals depend only on magnitudes and relative angles
through scalar products, and the regulator/domain $\mathcal S_{\Delta k}$ is common to all structures.
Hence the loop integrals producing $\Xi_\ell$ are identical across $S$ up to purely discrete sums over
allowed star wavevectors $\{\mathbf k_i\}$ that satisfy the resonance constraints enforced at each vertex.
Each quartic vertex contraction contributes a factor selecting a resonance quartet; counting such resonant
quartets produces the weight $N_{{\rm loop},S}$, while normalization by the number of mode choices yields
$N_S^2$, leading to the basic ratio $\mathcal C_S$.
At higher loops, multiple quartic resonance constraints appear; the total number of admissible discrete
assignments is a sum over products of such counts, which yields a polynomial $\mathcal P_\ell(\mathcal C_S)$
with nonnegative coefficients. The remaining continuous shell integrals are common and collected into
$\Xi_\ell(r;\Delta k)$.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Proposition: hierarchy cannot invert without adding new structural weights}

\begin{proposition}[Higher-loop non-inversion criterion]
Assume:
(i)--(iii) as above, and additionally that there exists a fluctuation-dominated regime in which
\begin{equation}
\left|\beta_{{\rm MF},S_1}-\beta_{{\rm MF},S_2}\right|
\ll
\left|\sum_{\ell\ge 1}\left(\delta\beta_{S_1}^{(\ell)}-\delta\beta_{S_2}^{(\ell)}\right)\right|
\quad \text{for the structures compared.}
\end{equation}
If, for all $\ell\ge 1$, the polynomials $\mathcal P_\ell$ in \eqref{eq:factorizationC}
are \emph{monotone increasing} functions of $\mathcal C_S$ on the relevant range of $\mathcal C_S$,
then the structural ranking induced by fluctuations is fixed by $\mathcal C_S$ and cannot be inverted
by any finite resummation of higher loops.
In particular, if $\mathcal C_{\rm BCC}>\mathcal C_{\rm FCC}>\mathcal C_{\rm SC}$, then in the
fluctuation-dominated regime
\begin{equation}
\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm BCC}}(r;\Delta k)
<
\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm FCC}}(r;\Delta k)
<
\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm SC}}(r;\Delta k)
\end{equation}
persists to all loop orders within the truncation class.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Lemma~\eqref{eq:factorizationC},
\begin{equation}
\beta_{{\rm eff},S}
=
\beta_{{\rm MF},S}
+
\sum_{\ell\ge 1}\mathcal P_\ell(\mathcal C_S)\,\Xi_\ell.
\end{equation}
For any pair $(S_1,S_2)$,
\begin{equation}
\begin{align} \begin{split}
\beta_{{\rm eff},S_1}-\beta_{{\rm eff},S_2}
=
(\beta_{{\rm MF},S_1}-\beta_{{\rm MF},S_2})
\\ +
\sum_{\ell\ge 1}\left[\mathcal P_\ell(\mathcal C_{S_1})-\mathcal P_\ell(\mathcal C_{S_2})\right]\Xi_\ell .
\end{split} \end{align}
\end{equation}

If each $\mathcal P_\ell$ is monotone increasing and $\mathcal C_{S_1}>\mathcal C_{S_2}$, then
$\mathcal P_\ell(\mathcal C_{S_1})-\mathcal P_\ell(\mathcal C_{S_2})>0$ for all $\ell$.
Thus the sign of the fluctuation contribution to the difference is fixed and cannot be reversed by adding
higher-loop terms; higher loops can only shift magnitudes (and hence the numerical location of selection
thresholds) through the common factors $\Xi_\ell(r;\Delta k)$.
In the fluctuation-dominated regime, the mean-field difference is subleading and cannot flip the sign.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Remark: how inversion can occur (outside the present universality class)}

The non-inversion statement relies crucially on the absence of new structure-specific weights beyond
$\mathcal C_S$. Inversion can occur only if one introduces additional ingredients that generate genuinely
new discrete geometric functionals, e.g.:
\begin{equation}
\begin{align} \begin{split}
\text{multi-shell couplings},
\\ \text{anisotropic/nonlocal quartic kernels}, 
\\ \text{explicit lattice pinning fields}, 
\\ \text{strongly momentum-dependent vertices}.
\end{split} \end{align}
\end{equation}
Such extensions lie outside the isotropic single-shell local truncation class considered here.

% ==============================
%  Universality D: Two-shell / multi-shell robustness (next step)
% ==============================

\section{Universality D: Robustness Under Weak Multi-Shell Coupling}

\subsection{Two-shell quadratic sector and mode decomposition}

Let the quadratic kernel admit two nearby soft shells at radii $k_0$ and $k_1$,
with $0<|k_1-k_0|\ll k_0$, and (possibly) finite thicknesses $\Delta k_0,\Delta k_1$.
Decompose the order parameter into shell components
\begin{equation}
\psi(x)=\psi_0(x)+\psi_1(x),
\end{equation}
where in momentum space
\begin{equation}
{\rm supp}\,\psi_a(\mathbf q)\subset \mathcal S^{(a)}_{\Delta k_a}
:=
\{\mathbf q:\; ||\mathbf q|-k_a|\le \Delta k_a\},
\qquad a\in\{0,1\}.
\end{equation}

Assume isotropic propagators on each shell:
\begin{equation}
G_a(q)=\frac{1}{r_a+\kappa_a(q^2-k_a^2)^2},
\qquad a\in\{0,1\}.
\end{equation}

\subsection{Local quartic interaction and shell-resolved couplings}

Take a local quartic interaction:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L_{\rm int}=\frac{u}{4!}\psi^4
=
\frac{1}{4!}\sum_{a,b,c,d\in\{0,1\}}
u_{abcd}\,\psi_a\psi_b\psi_c\psi_d,
\end{equation}
with the \emph{shell-resolved} couplings induced by locality satisfying
\begin{equation}
u_{abcd}=u\quad \text{for all }a,b,c,d,
\end{equation}
up to possible small renormalizations from integrating out hard modes.

\subsection{Shell-resolved equal-amplitude ansatz for a given structure}

For each structure $S$ (e.g.\ BCC/FCC/SC), assume the dominant pattern is on the
primary shell $k_0$ and allow subleading admixture on $k_1$:
\begin{equation}
\psi_0(x)=A\sum_{i=1}^{N_S}\cos(\mathbf k_i\cdot x),
\qquad |\mathbf k_i|=k_0,
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\psi_1(x)=B\sum_{j=1}^{M_S}\cos(\mathbf p_j\cdot x),
\qquad |\mathbf p_j|=k_1,
\end{equation}
with equal amplitudes within each shell orbit.

Define the primary-shell geometric ratio
\begin{equation}
\mathcal C_S^{(0)}:=\frac{N^{(0)}_{{\rm loop},S}}{N_S^2},
\end{equation}

counting nontrivial resonance quartets \emph{entirely on shell $k_0$}
(i.e.\ $\mathbf k_{i_1}+\mathbf k_{i_2}+\mathbf k_{i_3}+\mathbf k_{i_4}=0$).

Similarly define the mixed-shell resonance weight
\begin{equation}
\mathcal D_S^{(01)}:=\frac{N^{(01)}_{{\rm loop},S}}{N_S^2},
\end{equation}
counting quartets involving two $k_0$-modes and two $k_1$-modes that satisfy
$\mathbf k_{i_1}+\mathbf k_{i_2}+\mathbf p_{j_1}+\mathbf p_{j_2}=0$.

\subsection{One-loop effective quartic coefficients with two shells}

At one loop, the zero-momentum quartic renormalization splits into shell channels.
Introduce three bubble integrals (all structure-independent under isotropy):
\begin{align}
I_{00}(r_0;\Delta k_0)
&:=
\int_{\mathcal S^{(0)}_{\Delta k_0}}\frac{d^3q}{(2\pi)^3}\;
G_0(q)^2,\\
I_{11}(r_1;\Delta k_1)
&:=
\int_{\mathcal S^{(1)}_{\Delta k_1}}\frac{d^3q}{(2\pi)^3}\;
G_1(q)^2,\\
I_{01}(r_0,r_1;\Delta k_0,\Delta k_1)
&:=
\int_{\mathcal S^{(0)}_{\Delta k_0}}\frac{d^3q}{(2\pi)^3}\;
G_0(q)G_1(q)\,\chi_{01}(q),
\end{align}
where $\chi_{01}$ is an isotropic overlap/regulator factor (possibly unity if both shells are
handled with a joint isotropic regulator).

The effective quartic coefficient on the \emph{primary} shell $k_0$
takes the factorized form
\begin{equation}
\beta_{{\rm eff},S}^{(0)}
=
\beta_{{\rm MF},S}^{(0)}
-\frac{u^2}{2}\left[
I_{00}\,\mathcal C_S^{(0)}
+
I_{01}\,\mathcal D_S^{(01)}
\right],
\label{eq:betaeff_twoshell}
\end{equation}
and similarly for the secondary shell.

\subsection{Lemma: structure-independence of the two-shell bubble integrals}

\begin{lemma}[Structure-independence]
Assume:
(i) $G_a(q)$ depends only on $q=|\mathbf q|$ for each shell,
(ii) the regulator/domains $\mathcal S^{(a)}_{\Delta k_a}$ are isotropic,
(iii) the quartic vertex is local (momentum-independent).
Then $I_{00}, I_{11}, I_{01}$ are independent of the lattice structure $S$.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Same as Universality~A: under isotropy, the integrands and domains depend only on $q$.
No discrete star-geometry information enters the continuous integrals.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Proposition: weak multi-shell coupling does not invert BCC ranking}

\begin{proposition}[Non-inversion under weak shell mixing]
Assume the hypotheses of the Lemma and that the structural ordering on the primary shell
satisfies
\begin{equation}
\mathcal C_{\rm BCC}^{(0)}>\mathcal C_{\rm FCC}^{(0)}>\mathcal C_{\rm SC}^{(0)}.
\end{equation}
Assume furthermore that the mixed-shell resonance contribution is parametrically weak:
\begin{equation}
I_{01}\,\sup_S |\mathcal D_S^{(01)}|
\le \epsilon\; I_{00}\,\inf_{S\in\{\rm BCC,FCC\}} |\mathcal C_S^{(0)}|,
\qquad 0<\epsilon\ll 1.
\label{eq:weakmix}
\end{equation}
Then in the fluctuation-dominated regime, the BCC$>$FCC ranking on the primary shell persists:
\begin{equation}
\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm BCC}}^{(0)} < \beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm FCC}}^{(0)},
\end{equation}
and cannot be inverted by two-shell mixing satisfying \eqref{eq:weakmix}.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
From \eqref{eq:betaeff_twoshell},
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
    

\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm BCC}}^{(0)}-\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm FCC}}^{(0)}
&=
\left(\beta_{{\rm MF},{\rm BCC}}^{(0)}-\beta_{{\rm MF},{\rm FCC}}^{(0)}\right)
\\ -\frac{u^2}{2}\Big[
I_{00}\left(\mathcal C_{\rm BCC}^{(0)}-\mathcal C_{\rm FCC}^{(0)}\right)
+
I_{01}\left(\mathcal D_{\rm BCC}^{(01)}-\mathcal D_{\rm FCC}^{(01)}\right)
\Big].

\end{split}
\end{align}
In the fluctuation-dominated regime the mean-field difference is subleading.
Since $\mathcal C_{\rm BCC}^{(0)}-\mathcal C_{\rm FCC}^{(0)}>0$,
the leading term favors BCC.
The mixed term can at most reduce the magnitude of the difference.
Imposing \eqref{eq:weakmix} guarantees the mixed contribution cannot change the sign,
hence the BCC$>$FCC hierarchy persists.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Remark: what must be computed next}

To \emph{complete} Universality~D one must:
(i) compute/upper-bound $\sup_S|\mathcal D_S^{(01)}|$ for the relevant candidate structures,
(ii) evaluate $I_{01}/I_{00}$ in the relevant parameter regime,
thereby verifying \eqref{eq:weakmix} (or deriving an alternative sufficient condition).

% ==============================
%  Universality D (continued): estimating I01/I00 and completing the criterion
% ==============================

\subsection{Asymptotic estimates: $I_{00}$ and an upper bound on $I_{01}$}

Define the shell separation
\begin{equation}
\Delta := |k_1^2-k_0^2|>0,
\qquad
\Delta \ll k_0^2,
\end{equation}
and assume the deep Brazovskii regime on the primary shell:
\begin{equation}
r_0 \to 0^+,
\qquad
0<\Delta k_0 \ll k_0,
\qquad
\kappa_0>0.
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Primary-shell bubble.}
The standard near-shell evaluation gives
\begin{equation}
\begin{align}
\begin{split}

I_{00}(r_0;\Delta k_0)
=
\int_{\mathcal S^{(0)}_{\Delta k_0}}\frac{d^3q}{(2\pi)^3}\;
\frac{1}{\left[r_0+\kappa_0(q^2-k_0^2)^2\right]^2}
\\ \sim
\frac{1}{8\pi}\frac{k_0}{\sqrt{\kappa_0}}\;r_0^{-3/2}.
\label{eq:I00_asymp}

\end{split}
\end{align}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Cross-shell bubble: general bound.}
For any isotropic overlap factor satisfying $0\le \chi_{01}(q)\le 1$,
Cauchy--Schwarz yields
\begin{equation}
I_{01}(r_0,r_1;\Delta k_0,\Delta k_1)
\le
\left[I_{00}(r_0;\Delta k_0)\right]^{1/2}
\left[I_{11}(r_1;\Delta k_1)\right]^{1/2}.
\label{eq:I01_CS}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Cross-shell bubble: separation-suppressed estimate.}
If the shells are separated ($\Delta>0$), then on $\mathcal S^{(0)}_{\Delta k_0}$ we have
\begin{equation}
|q^2-k_1^2|
=
|(q^2-k_0^2)-(k_1^2-k_0^2)|
\ge
\Delta - |q^2-k_0^2|.
\end{equation}
For $|q-k_0|\le \Delta k_0$ and $\Delta k_0 \ll \Delta/k_0$, this implies
\begin{equation}
|q^2-k_1^2|
\ge
\frac{\Delta}{2},
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
\begin{split} 
$G_1(q)$
=
\frac{1}{r_1+\kappa_1(q^2-k_1^2)^2}
\\ \le
\frac{1}{\kappa_1(\Delta/2)^2}
=
\frac{4}{\kappa_1\Delta^2}.
\label{eq:G1_bound_on_shell0}
\end{split}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\begin{align} \begin{split}
I_{01} =
\int_{\mathcal S^{(0)}_{\Delta k_0}}\frac{d^3q}{(2\pi)^3}\;G_0(q)G_1(q)\chi_{01}(q)
\\ \le
\frac{4}{\kappa_1\Delta^2}
\int_{\mathcal S^{(0)}_{\Delta k_0}}\frac{d^3q}{(2\pi)^3}\;G_0(q).
\end{split} \end{align} 
\end{equation}
The remaining integral scales as
\begin{equation}
\int_{\mathcal S^{(0)}_{\Delta k_0}}\frac{d^3q}{(2\pi)^3}\;G_0(q)
\sim
\frac{1}{4\pi}\frac{k_0}{\sqrt{\kappa_0}}\;r_0^{-1/2},
\end{equation}
so we obtain the separation-suppressed bound
\begin{equation}
I_{01}(r_0,r_1;\Delta k_0,\Delta k_1)
\;\lesssim\;
\frac{1}{\pi}\;
\frac{k_0}{\sqrt{\kappa_0}}\;
\frac{1}{\kappa_1\Delta^2}\;
r_0^{-1/2}.
\label{eq:I01_sep}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Ratio estimate.}
Combining \eqref{eq:I00_asymp} and \eqref{eq:I01_sep},
\begin{equation}
\frac{I_{01}}{I_{00}}
\;\lesssim\;
8\;
\frac{\sqrt{\kappa_0}}{\kappa_1\Delta^2}\;
r_0,
\qquad
(r_0\to 0^+),
\label{eq:I01_over_I00}
\end{equation}
so \emph{cross-shell mixing is parametrically suppressed} in the deep Brazovskii regime
at fixed $\Delta>0$.

\subsection{Completion of Universality D: a sufficient non-inversion condition}

Recall \eqref{eq:betaeff_twoshell}:
\begin{equation}
\beta_{{\rm eff},S}^{(0)}
=
\beta_{{\rm MF},S}^{(0)}
-\frac{u^2}{2}\left[
I_{00}\,\mathcal C_S^{(0)}
+
I_{01}\,\mathcal D_S^{(01)}
\right].
\end{equation}
Define the geometric gaps
\begin{equation}
\Delta\mathcal C_{BF}:=
\mathcal C_{\rm BCC}^{(0)}-\mathcal C_{\rm FCC}^{(0)} > 0,
\qquad
\Delta\mathcal D_{BF}:=
\mathcal D_{\rm BCC}^{(01)}-\mathcal D_{\rm FCC}^{(01)}.
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[Two-shell non-inversion in the deep Brazovskii regime]
Assume isotropy, locality, and single-star equal-amplitude ansatz on each shell.
Assume $\Delta\mathcal C_{BF}>0$ and shell separation $\Delta>0$.
Then for sufficiently small $r_0>0$,
\begin{equation}
\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm BCC}}^{(0)} < \beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm FCC}}^{(0)}
\end{equation}
holds provided the following \emph{sufficient} condition is met:
\begin{equation}
\frac{I_{01}}{I_{00}}\;|\Delta\mathcal D_{BF}|
<
\Delta\mathcal C_{BF}.
\label{eq:noninvert_condition_final}
\end{equation}
Using \eqref{eq:I01_over_I00}, a concrete sufficient condition is
\begin{equation}
8\;
\frac{\sqrt{\kappa_0}}{\kappa_1\Delta^2}\;
r_0\;
|\Delta\mathcal D_{BF}|
<
\Delta\mathcal C_{BF},
\qquad
(r_0\to 0^+).
\label{eq:noninvert_condition_r0}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Compute the difference:
\begin{equation}
\begin{align} \begin{split}
\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm BCC}}^{(0)}-\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm FCC}}^{(0)}
=
(\beta_{{\rm MF},{\rm BCC}}^{(0)}-\beta_{{\rm MF},{\rm FCC}}^{(0)})
\\ -\frac{u^2}{2}\left[
I_{00}\Delta\mathcal C_{BF}+I_{01}\Delta\mathcal D_{BF}
\right].
\end{split} \end{align}
\end{equation}
In the fluctuation-dominated regime, the mean-field difference is subleading.
Thus the sign is controlled by the bracket.
Since $I_{00}>0$ and $\Delta\mathcal C_{BF}>0$, the leading term favors BCC.
The mixed term can only flip the sign if $I_{01}|\Delta\mathcal D_{BF}|\ge I_{00}\Delta\mathcal C_{BF}$.
Therefore \eqref{eq:noninvert_condition_final} is sufficient for non-inversion.
Equation \eqref{eq:noninvert_condition_r0} follows from the ratio bound \eqref{eq:I01_over_I00}.
\end{proof}

\subsection{What remains to \emph{fully close} Universality D}

To turn the sufficient condition \eqref{eq:noninvert_condition_final} into a completely explicit theorem,
one must provide:
\begin{equation}
\begin{align} \begin{split}
\text{(i) an explicit evaluation or bound for }\Delta\mathcal D_{BF},
\\ \text{(ii) the regime of validity for }\Delta k_0\ll \Delta/k_0.
\end{split} \end{align}
\end{equation}
Item (i) is purely combinatorial (mixed-shell resonance counting) once the secondary-shell star
$\{\mathbf p_j\}$ is specified.

% ==============================
%  Universality D (continued): bounding the mixed-shell combinatorics ΔD_BF
% ==============================

\subsection{Mixed-shell resonance counting: a universal upper bound}

We now bound the mixed-shell combinatorial weight
\begin{equation}
\mathcal D_S^{(01)}:=\frac{N^{(01)}_{{\rm loop},S}}{N_S^2},
\end{equation}
where $N^{(01)}_{{\rm loop},S}$ counts (nontrivial) quartets of the form
\begin{equation}
\mathbf k_{i_1}+\mathbf k_{i_2}+\mathbf p_{j_1}+\mathbf p_{j_2}=\mathbf 0,
\qquad
|\mathbf k_{i_\alpha}|=k_0,\;\;|\mathbf p_{j_\beta}|=k_1,
\end{equation}
with $\{\mathbf k_i\}_{i=1}^{N_S}$ the primary-shell star for structure $S$ and
$\{\mathbf p_j\}_{j=1}^{M_S}$ the secondary-shell star (not assumed identical across $S$).

\paragraph{Counting convention.}
For definiteness, let $N^{(01)}_{{\rm loop},S}$ count \emph{ordered} pairs
$((i_1,i_2),(j_1,j_2))$ satisfying the resonance constraint.
(Any unordered convention differs only by an overall constant factor that cancels in
the non-inversion criterion after redefinition of $\mathcal D_S^{(01)}$.)

\begin{lemma}[Universal bound on mixed-shell resonance loops]
For any two stars $\{\mathbf k_i\}_{i=1}^{N_S}$ and $\{\mathbf p_j\}_{j=1}^{M_S}$,
\begin{equation}
N^{(01)}_{{\rm loop},S}\le N_S^2\,M_S.
\label{eq:mixed_bound1}
\end{equation}
Consequently,
\begin{equation}
0\le \mathcal D_S^{(01)}\le M_S.
\label{eq:mixed_bound2}
\end{equation}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Fix an ordered pair $(i_1,i_2)$ on the primary shell, and fix $j_1$ on the secondary shell.
Then the resonance condition uniquely determines the fourth wavevector:
\begin{equation}
\mathbf p_{j_2}=-(\mathbf k_{i_1}+\mathbf k_{i_2}+\mathbf p_{j_1}).
\end{equation}
Hence for each choice of $(i_1,i_2,j_1)$ there is \emph{at most one} index $j_2$
that can satisfy the resonance, and it may fail to lie in the discrete star.
Therefore the number of solutions for fixed $(i_1,i_2)$ is at most $M_S$, and summing over
the $N_S^2$ ordered primary pairs gives \eqref{eq:mixed_bound1}.
Dividing by $N_S^2$ gives \eqref{eq:mixed_bound2}.
\end{proof}

\subsection{A structure-independent sufficient condition using the bound}

Recall the sufficient non-inversion criterion \eqref{eq:noninvert_condition_final}:
\begin{equation}
\frac{I_{01}}{I_{00}}\;|\Delta\mathcal D_{BF}|<\Delta\mathcal C_{BF},
\qquad
\Delta\mathcal C_{BF}:=\mathcal C_{\rm BCC}^{(0)}-\mathcal C_{\rm FCC}^{(0)}.
\end{equation}
Using the triangle inequality and \eqref{eq:mixed_bound2},
\begin{equation}
\begin{align} \begin{split}
|\Delta\mathcal D_{BF}|
=
|\mathcal D_{\rm BCC}^{(01)}-\mathcal D_{\rm FCC}^{(01)}|
\\ \le
\mathcal D_{\rm BCC}^{(01)}+\mathcal D_{\rm FCC}^{(01)}
\le
M_{\rm BCC}+M_{\rm FCC}.
\label{eq:DeltaD_bound}
\end{split} \end{align}
\end{equation}
Therefore a fully explicit (though conservative) sufficient condition is
\begin{equation}
\frac{I_{01}}{I_{00}}\,(M_{\rm BCC}+M_{\rm FCC})
<
\Delta\mathcal C_{BF}.
\label{eq:noninvert_condition_conservative}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Completion with separation-suppressed estimate}

Using the ratio estimate \eqref{eq:I01_over_I00} from the previous subsection,
\begin{equation}
\frac{I_{01}}{I_{00}}
\;\lesssim\;
8\;
\frac{\sqrt{\kappa_0}}{\kappa_1\Delta^2}\;
r_0,
\end{equation}
a concrete sufficient condition ensuring the BCC$>$FCC hierarchy survives two-shell mixing is:
\begin{equation}
8\;
\frac{\sqrt{\kappa_0}}{\kappa_1\Delta^2}\;
r_0\,
(M_{\rm BCC}+M_{\rm FCC})
<
\Delta\mathcal C_{BF}.
\label{eq:noninvert_condition_final_explicit}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Interpretation (formal).}
Equation \eqref{eq:noninvert_condition_final_explicit} shows that for fixed shell separation $\Delta>0$
and fixed discrete secondary-shell star sizes $M_{\rm BCC},M_{\rm FCC}$,
the cross-shell contribution is parametrically suppressed as $r_0\to 0^+$, hence cannot invert the
primary-shell geometric hierarchy whenever $\Delta\mathcal C_{BF}>0$.

\subsection{Optional strengthening: equal secondary-shell orbit sizes}

If the secondary-shell construction uses the same orbit size $M$ across the cubic candidates,
\begin{equation}
M_{\rm BCC}=M_{\rm FCC}=M,
\end{equation}
then \eqref{eq:noninvert_condition_final_explicit} simplifies to
\begin{equation}
16\;
\frac{\sqrt{\kappa_0}}{\kappa_1\Delta^2}\;
r_0\,M
<
\Delta\mathcal C_{BF}.
\end{equation}

\subsection{Status of Universality D}

Within the isotropic local truncation class, Universality~D is now closed at the level of a
\emph{sufficient} (non-optimized) theorem:
\begin{itemize}
\item the mixed-shell bubble contribution is structure-independent and separation-suppressed;
\item the mixed-shell combinatorics admits a universal bound independent of the detailed star geometry;
\item together, these yield an explicit inequality \eqref{eq:noninvert_condition_final_explicit}
guaranteeing that two-shell mixing cannot invert the BCC$>$FCC hierarchy.
\end{itemize}
Sharper (less conservative) results follow by computing $\mathcal D_S^{(01)}$ explicitly for the chosen
secondary-shell stars, but are not required for a rigorous sufficient non-inversion theorem.

% ==============================
%  Universality D (continued): SHARP mixed-shell combinatorics via length-ratio obstruction
% ==============================

\subsection{Sharp closure of Universality D via a discrete length-ratio obstruction}

We now sharpen the mixed-shell combinatorics beyond the crude bound
$0\le \mathcal D_S^{(01)}\le M_S$ by using a necessary \emph{metric} condition for mixed-shell
resonances.

Let the primary-shell star for structure $S$ be the finite set of directions
\begin{equation}
U_S:=\{\hat{\mathbf k}_i\}_{i=1}^{N_S}\subset S^2,
\qquad
\mathbf k_i=k_0\hat{\mathbf k}_i,
\end{equation}
and let the secondary-shell star be another finite set of directions
\begin{equation}
V:=\{\hat{\mathbf p}_j\}_{j=1}^{M}\subset S^2,
\qquad
\mathbf p_j=k_1\hat{\mathbf p}_j,
\end{equation}
taken \emph{common} across candidates (i.e.\ $V$ does not depend on $S$), which is the natural
setting for a universality statement.

Define the (finite) chord-length sets of \emph{pair sums}
\begin{equation}
\begin{align} \begin{split}
\mathcal L(U_S):=\Big\{\,\|\hat{\mathbf k}+\hat{\mathbf k}'\|\;:\;\hat{\mathbf k},\hat{\mathbf k}'\in U_S\,\Big\},
\qquad
\\ \mathcal L(V):=\Big\{\,\|\hat{\mathbf p}+\hat{\mathbf p}'\|\;:\;\hat{\mathbf p},\hat{\mathbf p}'\in V\,\Big\}.
\end{split} \end{align}
\end{equation}
Note that $0\in \mathcal L(\cdot)$ always (from $\hat{\mathbf v}+\!(-\hat{\mathbf v})=0$ if both are present).

\subsection{Lemma: necessary length-ratio condition for a mixed-shell resonance}

A mixed-shell quartet requires
\begin{equation}
\begin{align} \begin{split}
\mathbf k_{i_1}+\mathbf k_{i_2}+\mathbf p_{j_1}+\mathbf p_{j_2}=\mathbf 0
\\ \quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
k_0(\hat{\mathbf k}_{i_1}+\hat{\mathbf k}_{i_2})=-k_1(\hat{\mathbf p}_{j_1}+\hat{\mathbf p}_{j_2}).
\label{eq:mixed_resonance_unit}
\end{split} \end{align}
\end{equation}

\begin{lemma}[Length-ratio obstruction]
If \eqref{eq:mixed_resonance_unit} holds and both pair-sums are nonzero, then necessarily
\begin{equation}
\frac{k_1}{k_0}=\frac{\|\hat{\mathbf k}_{i_1}+\hat{\mathbf k}_{i_2}\|}{\|\hat{\mathbf p}_{j_1}+\hat{\mathbf p}_{j_2}\|}
\in
\frac{\mathcal L(U_S)\setminus\{0\}}{\mathcal L(V)\setminus\{0\}}.
\label{eq:length_ratio_condition}
\end{equation}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Taking norms in \eqref{eq:mixed_resonance_unit} and assuming neither side is zero yields
$k_0\|\hat{\mathbf k}_{i_1}+\hat{\mathbf k}_{i_2}\|
=
k_1\|\hat{\mathbf p}_{j_1}+\hat{\mathbf p}_{j_2}\|$,
hence \eqref{eq:length_ratio_condition}.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Definition: nontrivial mixed-shell loops}

We define $N^{(01)}_{{\rm loop},S}$ to count only \emph{nontrivial} mixed loops, i.e.\ solutions to
\eqref{eq:mixed_resonance_unit} with
\begin{equation}
\hat{\mathbf k}_{i_1}+\hat{\mathbf k}_{i_2}\neq \mathbf 0
\quad\text{and}\quad
\hat{\mathbf p}_{j_1}+\hat{\mathbf p}_{j_2}\neq \mathbf 0.
\end{equation}
(Trivial $\pm$-pairings on each shell are excluded because they produce only structure-independent
self-renormalizations and do not contribute to structural ranking.)

\subsection{Theorem: generic absence of nontrivial mixed resonances (hence $\mathcal D_S^{(01)}=0$)}

\begin{theorem}[Generic vanishing of the mixed-shell combinatorics]
Fix finite direction sets $U_S$ (for each candidate structure $S$) and a common finite $V$.
If the shell-radius ratio satisfies
\begin{equation}
\frac{k_1}{k_0}\notin
\bigcup_{S\in\{\rm BCC,FCC,SC\}}
\frac{\mathcal L(U_S)\setminus\{0\}}{\mathcal L(V)\setminus\{0\}},
\label{eq:generic_ratio_exclusion}
\end{equation}
then there exist \emph{no} nontrivial mixed-shell resonances for any $S$.
Consequently,
\begin{equation}
N^{(01)}_{{\rm loop},S}=0,
\qquad
\mathcal D_S^{(01)}=0,
\qquad
\Delta\mathcal D_{BF}=0,
\end{equation}
and the two-shell effective quartic coefficient reduces to
\begin{equation}
\beta_{{\rm eff},S}^{(0)}
=
\beta_{{\rm MF},S}^{(0)}
-\frac{u^2}{2}I_{00}(r_0;\Delta k_0)\,\mathcal C_S^{(0)},
\end{equation}
so the BCC$>$FCC ranking is \emph{identical} to the single-shell theory, with no additional condition.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Under \eqref{eq:generic_ratio_exclusion}, the necessary condition
\eqref{eq:length_ratio_condition} cannot be satisfied for any nonzero pair-sums, hence no nontrivial mixed
resonances exist. By definition of $N^{(01)}_{{\rm loop},S}$, this implies $N^{(01)}_{{\rm loop},S}=0$ and
thus $\mathcal D_S^{(01)}=0$. Substituting into \eqref{eq:betaeff_twoshell} gives the reduced form.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Corollary: Universality D is fully closed for generic $(k_1/k_0)$}

\begin{corollary}[Unconditional non-inversion for generic ratios]
For fixed discrete stars $U_S$ and a common $V$, the exceptional set of ratios
\begin{equation}
\mathfrak E :=
\bigcup_{S}
\frac{\mathcal L(U_S)\setminus\{0\}}{\mathcal L(V)\setminus\{0\}}
\end{equation}
is finite, hence measure-zero in $\mathbb R_{>0}$.
For all $k_1/k_0\notin \mathfrak E$, mixed-shell loops vanish and BCC ranking is unchanged
without needing the small-mixing inequality \eqref{eq:noninvert_condition_final_explicit}.
\end{corollary}

\subsection{Remark: the resonant (nongeneric) case}

If $k_1/k_0\in \mathfrak E$, nontrivial mixed resonances may exist and one must revert to the
previous sufficient-condition theorem (bounded by $I_{01}/I_{00}$) or compute $\mathcal D_S^{(01)}$
explicitly for that specific ratio and choice of $V$.

% ==============================
%  Universality E: Resonant two-shell case (k1/k0 in exceptional set)
% ==============================

\section{Universality E: The Resonant Two-Shell Case}

\subsection{Problem statement}

Assume the shell ratio lies in the exceptional (finite) set
\begin{equation}
\frac{k_1}{k_0}\in \mathfrak E,
\qquad
\mathfrak E :=
\bigcup_{S\in\{\rm BCC,FCC,SC\}}
\frac{\mathcal L(U_S)\setminus\{0\}}{\mathcal L(V)\setminus\{0\}},
\end{equation}
so that nontrivial mixed-shell resonances \emph{may} exist.

Recall the primary-shell effective quartic coefficient:
\begin{equation}
\beta_{{\rm eff},S}^{(0)}
=
\beta_{{\rm MF},S}^{(0)}
-\frac{u^2}{2}\left[
I_{00}\,\mathcal C_S^{(0)}
+
I_{01}\,\mathcal D_S^{(01)}
\right].
\label{eq:E_betaeff}
\end{equation}
Universality~E consists in obtaining a \emph{sharp} control of
$\Delta \mathcal D_{BF}:=\mathcal D_{\rm BCC}^{(01)}-\mathcal D_{\rm FCC}^{(01)}$
for the resonant ratios, and proving that mixed-shell terms cannot invert the hierarchy.

\subsection{Reduction to a discrete representation problem}

Write the mixed-shell resonance constraint as
\begin{equation}
k_0(\hat{\mathbf k}_{i_1}+\hat{\mathbf k}_{i_2})
=
-k_1(\hat{\mathbf p}_{j_1}+\hat{\mathbf p}_{j_2}).
\label{eq:E_vec}
\end{equation}
Define the discrete pair-sum sets
\begin{equation}
\Sigma(U_S):=\{\hat{\mathbf k}+\hat{\mathbf k}':\hat{\mathbf k},\hat{\mathbf k}'\in U_S,\ \hat{\mathbf k}+\hat{\mathbf k}'\neq 0\},
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\Sigma(V):=\{\hat{\mathbf p}+\hat{\mathbf p}':\hat{\mathbf p},\hat{\mathbf p}'\in V,\ \hat{\mathbf p}+\hat{\mathbf p}'\neq 0\}.
\end{equation}
Then \eqref{eq:E_vec} is equivalent to the existence of
\begin{equation}
\mathbf s\in \Sigma(U_S),\qquad \mathbf t\in \Sigma(V)
\quad\text{such that}\quad
k_0\,\mathbf s=-k_1\,\mathbf t.
\label{eq:E_match}
\end{equation}

Hence mixed resonances exist if and only if the scaled set $k_0\Sigma(U_S)$ intersects $-k_1\Sigma(V)$.

\subsection{Definition of multiplicity weights}

For any nonzero vector $\mathbf v\in \mathbb R^3$, define multiplicities
\begin{equation}
m_S(\mathbf v):=\#\{(i_1,i_2):\hat{\mathbf k}_{i_1}+\hat{\mathbf k}_{i_2}=\mathbf v\},
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
n(\mathbf v):=\#\{(j_1,j_2):\hat{\mathbf p}_{j_1}+\hat{\mathbf p}_{j_2}=\mathbf v\}.
\end{equation}
Then the number of mixed loops is
\begin{equation}
N^{(01)}_{{\rm loop},S}
=
\sum_{\mathbf v\neq 0}
m_S(\mathbf v)\,
n\!\left(-\frac{k_0}{k_1}\mathbf v\right),
\label{eq:E_Nloop_conv}
\end{equation}
with the convention that $n(\mathbf w)=0$ if $\mathbf w\notin \Sigma(V)$.

Therefore,
\begin{equation}
\mathcal D_S^{(01)}
=
\frac{1}{N_S^2}
\sum_{\mathbf v\neq 0}
m_S(\mathbf v)\,
n\!\left(-\frac{k_0}{k_1}\mathbf v\right).
\label{eq:E_D_def}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Lemma: uniform upper bound in terms of maximal pair-sum multiplicities}

Define
\begin{equation}
\begin{align} \begin{split}
m_S^{\max}:=\max_{\mathbf v\neq 0} m_S(\mathbf v),
\qquad
n^{\max}:=\max_{\mathbf v\neq 0} n(\mathbf v),
\\ \qquad
|\Sigma(U_S)|:=\#\Sigma(U_S).
\end{split} \end{align}
\end{equation}

\begin{lemma}[Resonant bound]
For any resonant ratio $k_1/k_0$, one has
\begin{equation}
\mathcal D_S^{(01)}
\le
\frac{|\Sigma(U_S)|}{N_S^2}\,m_S^{\max}\,n^{\max}.
\label{eq:E_bound}
\end{equation}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
From \eqref{eq:E_D_def},
\begin{equation}
\begin{align} \begin{split}
\mathcal D_S^{(01)}
\le
\frac{1}{N_S^2}
\sum_{\mathbf v\neq 0}
m_S^{\max}\,n^{\max}\,\mathbf 1\!\left[-\frac{k_0}{k_1}\mathbf v\in \Sigma(V)\right]
\\ \le
\frac{|\Sigma(U_S)|}{N_S^2}\,m_S^{\max}\,n^{\max}.
\end{split} \end{align}
\end{equation}
\end{proof}

\subsection{Proposition: sufficient non-inversion criterion in the resonant case}

Let $\Delta\mathcal C_{BF}:=\mathcal C_{\rm BCC}^{(0)}-\mathcal C_{\rm FCC}^{(0)}>0$.
Using \eqref{eq:E_betaeff}, the BCC$>$FCC condition is
\begin{equation}
I_{00}\Delta\mathcal C_{BF}+I_{01}\Delta\mathcal D_{BF}>0.
\end{equation}
A sufficient (conservative) condition is
\begin{equation}
\frac{I_{01}}{I_{00}}
\left(
\mathcal D_{\rm BCC}^{(01)}+\mathcal D_{\rm FCC}^{(01)}
\right)
<
\Delta\mathcal C_{BF}.
\label{eq:E_suff}
\end{equation}

By Lemma~\eqref{eq:E_bound}, one obtains a fully explicit sufficient condition:
\begin{equation}
\frac{I_{01}}{I_{00}}\,
n^{\max}
\left[
\frac{|\Sigma(U_{\rm BCC})|}{N_{\rm BCC}^2}m_{\rm BCC}^{\max}
+
\frac{|\Sigma(U_{\rm FCC})|}{N_{\rm FCC}^2}m_{\rm FCC}^{\max}
\right]
<
\Delta\mathcal C_{BF}.
\label{eq:E_suff_explicit}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Remark: what remains to \emph{fully close} Universality E}

To make \eqref{eq:E_suff_explicit} operational, one must:
\begin{itemize}
\item Fix a concrete secondary-shell star $V$ (hence compute $n^{\max}$);
\item Compute $|\Sigma(U_S)|$ and $m_S^{\max}$ for $S\in\{\rm BCC,FCC\}$ (purely discrete, closed-form);
\item Evaluate $I_{01}/I_{00}$ in the regime of interest (already bounded by separation-suppression when $\Delta>0$).
\end{itemize}
The above converts the resonant-case problem into finite combinatorics plus a single ratio of isotropic integrals.

% ==============================
%  Universality E (continued): explicit evaluation of |Sigma(U_S)| and m_S^{max}
%  for the standard cubic stars (SC, FCC=<111>, BCC=<110>)
% ==============================

\subsection{Explicit multiplicity data for the standard cubic stars}

We take the standard reciprocal-star direction sets:
\begin{align}
U_{\rm SC} &:= \{\pm \hat{\mathbf e}_x,\pm \hat{\mathbf e}_y,\pm \hat{\mathbf e}_z\}, \qquad N_{\rm SC}=6,\\
U_{\rm FCC} &:= \left\{\frac{1}{\sqrt3}(\pm1,\pm1,\pm1)\right\}, \qquad N_{\rm FCC}=8,\\
U_{\rm BCC} &:= \left\{\frac{1}{\sqrt2}(\pm1,\pm1,0)\ \text{and perms}\right\}, \qquad N_{\rm BCC}=12.
\end{align}

Recall
\begin{equation}
\Sigma(U_S):=\{\hat{\mathbf k}+\hat{\mathbf k}':\hat{\mathbf k},\hat{\mathbf k}'\in U_S,\ \hat{\mathbf k}+\hat{\mathbf k}'\neq 0\},
\qquad
m_S(\mathbf v):=\#\{(i_1,i_2):\hat{\mathbf k}_{i_1}+\hat{\mathbf k}_{i_2}=\mathbf v\},
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
m_S^{\max}:=\max_{\mathbf v\neq 0} m_S(\mathbf v),
\qquad
|\Sigma(U_S)|:=\#\Sigma(U_S).
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Result (ordered-pair convention).}
For the above stars one obtains:
\begin{align}
|\Sigma(U_{\rm SC})| &= 18, & m_{\rm SC}^{\max} &= 2,\\
|\Sigma(U_{\rm FCC})| &= 26, & m_{\rm FCC}^{\max} &= 4,\\
|\Sigma(U_{\rm BCC})| &= 54, & m_{\rm BCC}^{\max} &= 4.
\end{align}

Hence the resonant-case bound (Lemma~\eqref{eq:E_bound}) becomes:
\begin{align}
\mathcal D_{\rm FCC}^{(01)}
&\le
\frac{|\Sigma(U_{\rm FCC})|}{N_{\rm FCC}^2}\,m_{\rm FCC}^{\max}\,n^{\max}
=
\frac{26}{8^2}\cdot 4\,n^{\max}
=
\frac{13}{8}\,n^{\max},\\
\mathcal D_{\rm BCC}^{(01)}
&\le
\frac{|\Sigma(U_{\rm BCC})|}{N_{\rm BCC}^2}\,m_{\rm BCC}^{\max}\,n^{\max}
=
\frac{54}{12^2}\cdot 4\,n^{\max}
=
\frac{3}{2}\,n^{\max}.
\end{align}

Therefore,
\begin{equation}
\mathcal D_{\rm BCC}^{(01)}+\mathcal D_{\rm FCC}^{(01)}
\le
\left(\frac{3}{2}+\frac{13}{8}\right)n^{\max}
=
\frac{25}{8}\,n^{\max}.
\label{eq:Dbf_plus_bound_sharp}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Fully explicit resonant-case non-inversion condition}

Using \eqref{eq:E_suff} and \eqref{eq:Dbf_plus_bound_sharp}, a sufficient resonant-case criterion is
\begin{equation}
\frac{I_{01}}{I_{00}}\cdot \frac{25}{8}\,n^{\max}
<
\Delta\mathcal C_{BF},
\qquad
\Delta\mathcal C_{BF}:=\mathcal C_{\rm BCC}^{(0)}-\mathcal C_{\rm FCC}^{(0)} >0.
\label{eq:E_noninvert_sharp_final}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{If the secondary star equals a standard cubic star.}
If the secondary-shell direction set $V$ is taken as one of the standard cubic stars, then
\begin{align}
V=U_{\rm SC}:&\quad n^{\max}=2,\\
V=U_{\rm FCC}:&\quad n^{\max}=4,\\
V=U_{\rm BCC}:&\quad n^{\max}=4,
\end{align}
so \eqref{eq:E_noninvert_sharp_final} becomes explicitly
\begin{equation}
\frac{I_{01}}{I_{00}}\cdot
\begin{cases}
\frac{25}{4} & (V=U_{\rm SC}),\\[4pt]
\frac{25}{2} & (V=U_{\rm FCC}\ \text{or}\ U_{\rm BCC}),
\end{cases}
\;<\;
\Delta\mathcal C_{BF}.
\end{equation}

% ==============================
%  Universality E (continued): plug-in ΔC_BF and obtain final explicit r0-condition
% ==============================

\subsection{Evaluating $\Delta\mathcal C_{BF}$ for the cubic stars}

For the standard cubic stars used throughout (SC: $N=6$, FCC: $N=8$, BCC: $N=12$),
the geometric ratios entering the one-loop quartic correction are
\begin{equation}
\mathcal C_S^{(0)}=\frac{N^{(0)}_{{\rm loop},S}}{N_S^2},
\end{equation}
with the explicit values (from the resonance-loop counting on the primary shell)
\begin{equation}
\mathcal C_{\rm BCC}^{(0)}=\frac{1}{6},\qquad
\mathcal C_{\rm FCC}^{(0)}=\frac{1}{8},\qquad
\mathcal C_{\rm SC}^{(0)}=0.
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\Delta\mathcal C_{BF}:=\mathcal C_{\rm BCC}^{(0)}-\mathcal C_{\rm FCC}^{(0)}
=\frac{1}{24}.
\label{eq:DeltaC_BF_value}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Final resonant-case inequality in terms of $I_{01}/I_{00}$}

Insert \eqref{eq:DeltaC_BF_value} into \eqref{eq:E_noninvert_sharp_final}:
\begin{equation}
\frac{I_{01}}{I_{00}}\cdot \frac{25}{8}\,n^{\max}
<
\frac{1}{24}.
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\frac{I_{01}}{I_{00}}
<
\frac{1}{75\,n^{\max}}.
\label{eq:Iratio_threshold_resonant}
\end{equation}

If the secondary-shell direction set $V$ is itself a standard cubic star, then
\begin{equation}
n^{\max}=
\begin{cases}
2, & V=U_{\rm SC},\\
4, & V=U_{\rm FCC}\ \text{or}\ U_{\rm BCC},
\end{cases}
\end{equation}
and \eqref{eq:Iratio_threshold_resonant} becomes
\begin{equation}
\frac{I_{01}}{I_{00}}
<
\begin{cases}
\frac{1}{150}, & (V=U_{\rm SC}),\\[4pt]
\frac{1}{300}, & (V=U_{\rm FCC}\ \text{or}\ U_{\rm BCC}).
\end{cases}
\label{eq:Iratio_threshold_resonant_numeric}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Final resonant-case inequality in terms of shell separation and $r_0$}

Using the separation-suppressed estimate (deep Brazovskii regime with $\Delta=|k_1^2-k_0^2|>0$ and
$\Delta k_0\ll \Delta/k_0$):
\begin{equation}
\frac{I_{01}}{I_{00}}
\;\lesssim\;
8\;
\frac{\sqrt{\kappa_0}}{\kappa_1\Delta^2}\;
r_0,
\label{eq:Iratio_bound_repeat}
\end{equation}
a concrete sufficient condition ensuring \eqref{eq:Iratio_threshold_resonant} is
\begin{equation}
8\;
\frac{\sqrt{\kappa_0}}{\kappa_1\Delta^2}\;
r_0
<
\frac{1}{75\,n^{\max}}.
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
r_0
<
\frac{1}{600\,n^{\max}}
\frac{\kappa_1\Delta^2}{\sqrt{\kappa_0}}.
\label{eq:r0_final_resonant_condition}
\end{equation}

For the standard cubic secondary stars:
\begin{equation}
r_0
<
\begin{cases}
\displaystyle \frac{1}{1200}\frac{\kappa_1\Delta^2}{\sqrt{\kappa_0}},
& (V=U_{\rm SC}),\\[10pt]
\displaystyle \frac{1}{2400}\frac{\kappa_1\Delta^2}{\sqrt{\kappa_0}},
& (V=U_{\rm FCC}\ \text{or}\ U_{\rm BCC}).
\end{cases}
\label{eq:r0_final_resonant_condition_numeric}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Theorem: Universality D is closed for generic and resonant ratios}

\begin{theorem}[Two-shell universality of the BCC ranking]
Consider an isotropic two-shell Landau--Brazovskii theory with local quartic interaction and
equal-amplitude star ansatz on each shell.
Let the primary-shell cubic stars be $U_{\rm BCC},U_{\rm FCC},U_{\rm SC}$ as above.

\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{Generic ratio:} If $k_1/k_0\notin\mathfrak E$, then all nontrivial mixed-shell
resonance loops vanish and the BCC$>$FCC hierarchy is identical to the single-shell theory.

\item \textbf{Resonant ratio:} If $k_1/k_0\in\mathfrak E$, then the BCC$>$FCC hierarchy still persists
provided the cross-shell bubble ratio satisfies \eqref{eq:Iratio_threshold_resonant}, or
sufficiently, the explicit deep-Brazovskii condition \eqref{eq:r0_final_resonant_condition}.
\end{itemize}
\end{theorem}

% ==============================
%  Universality F: Strong multi-shell overlap (Δ → 0), mode mixing, and reduction
% ==============================

\section{Universality F: Strong Multi-Shell Overlap ($\Delta\to 0$) and Mode-Reduction}

\subsection{Setup: two strongly coupled shell components with a quadratic mixing matrix}

Let $\phi_a(x)$, $a\in\{0,1\}$, denote two coarse-grained components supported near a common soft radius
$k_0$ (allowing strong overlap). The quadratic action is taken as the most general \emph{isotropic} form
consistent with rotational symmetry:
\begin{equation}
S_2
=
\frac12
\int_{\mathbf q}
\phi_a(\mathbf q)\,
\mathcal M_{ab}(q)\,
\phi_b(-\mathbf q),
\qquad
\int_{\mathbf q}:=\int \frac{d^3q}{(2\pi)^3},
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M(q)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
r_0+\kappa_0(q^2-k_0^2)^2 & \mu \\
\mu & r_1+\kappa_1(q^2-k_0^2)^2
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad q:=|\mathbf q|.
\label{eq:MF_matrix}
\end{equation}
Here $\mu$ parametrizes \emph{strong} inter-shell mixing (no smallness assumption), and the two shells
have merged into a single isotropic soft band around $k_0$.

The interaction is local quartic (scalar for definiteness):
\begin{equation}
S_4=\int d^3x\;\frac{u}{4!}\,(\phi_0+\phi_1)^4.
\label{eq:MF_quartic}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Diagonalization into eigenmodes}

For each $q$, diagonalize $\mathcal M(q)$ by an orthogonal matrix $O(q)\in SO(2)$:
\begin{equation}
O(q)^{\mathsf T}\mathcal M(q)O(q)=\mathrm{diag}\big(\lambda_-(q),\lambda_+(q)\big),
\end{equation}
and define eigenmodes
\begin{equation}
\begin{pmatrix}
\varphi_-(\mathbf q)\\
\varphi_+(\mathbf q)
\end{pmatrix}
=
O(q)^{\mathsf T}
\begin{pmatrix}
\phi_0(\mathbf q)\\
\phi_1(\mathbf q)
\end{pmatrix}.
\end{equation}
Explicitly,
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\pm(q)
=
\frac12\left(A(q)+B(q)\right)\pm \frac12\sqrt{\left(A(q)-B(q)\right)^2+4\mu^2},
\label{eq:lambda_pm}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
A(q)=r_0+\kappa_0(q^2-k_0^2)^2,\qquad B(q)=r_1+\kappa_1(q^2-k_0^2)^2.
\end{equation}

\subsection{Assumption: a single soft eigenmode dominates}

\begin{assumption}[Single-soft-mode regime]
There exists a neighborhood $\mathcal B$ of the soft band around $q\simeq k_0$ such that
\begin{equation}
\begin{align} \begin{split}
\lambda_-(q)\to 0^+ \ \text{as control parameters vary},
\qquad
\\ \lambda_+(q)\ge \Delta_+>0 \ \ \forall q\in\mathcal B,
\label{eq:gap_assumption}
\end{split} \end{align}
\end{equation}
for some $q$-independent gap $\Delta_+$.
\end{assumption}

\subsection{Lemma: integrating out the gapped mode yields a single-mode isotropic Brazovskii theory}

\begin{lemma}[Mode reduction]
Under \eqref{eq:gap_assumption}, the gapped eigenmode $\varphi_+$ can be integrated out perturbatively
in $u$ to produce an effective action for $\varphi_-$
\begin{equation}
\begin{align} \begin{split}
S_{\rm eff}[\varphi_-]
=
\frac12\int_{\mathbf q}\varphi_-(\mathbf q)\lambda_-(q)\varphi_-(-\mathbf q)
\\ +
\int d^3x\;\frac{u_{\rm eff}}{4!}\,\varphi_-^4
+\text{(higher operators)},
\label{eq:Seff_minus}
\end{split} \end{align}
\end{equation}
where:
\begin{itemize}
\item $\lambda_-(q)$ is isotropic and has the Brazovskii form near $k_0$:
$\lambda_-(q)=r_{\rm eff}+\kappa_{\rm eff}(q^2-k_0^2)^2+O\!\left((q^2-k_0^2)^3\right)$;
\item $u_{\rm eff}=u\cdot \alpha^4+O(u^2)$ with $\alpha$ the (bounded) projection coefficient of
$\phi_0+\phi_1$ onto $\varphi_-$ on the band $\mathcal B$;
\item the induced higher operators are either higher-derivative or higher-point and are suppressed by
powers of $\Delta_+^{-1}$.
\end{itemize}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Since $\lambda_+(q)\ge \Delta_+>0$ on $\mathcal B$, the $\varphi_+$ propagator is uniformly bounded,
so the functional integral over $\varphi_+$ is analytic in $u$ and generates a local derivative expansion.
Rotational symmetry ensures isotropy of all induced kernels. The leading contribution to the quartic term
is the projection of $(\phi_0+\phi_1)^4$ onto $\varphi_-^4$, giving $u_{\rm eff}=u\alpha^4+O(u^2)$.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Proposition: BCC selection persists in the strong-overlap regime}

Let $S$ denote a candidate cubic structure and impose the equal-amplitude star ansatz on the \emph{soft}
eigenmode:
\begin{equation}
\varphi_-(x)=A\sum_{i=1}^{N_S}\cos(\mathbf k_i\cdot x),
\qquad |\mathbf k_i|=k_0.
\end{equation}

\begin{proposition}[Universality in the strong-overlap regime]
Under the hypotheses of Lemma~\eqref{eq:Seff_minus} (in particular, isotropy and a gapped $\varphi_+$),
the fluctuation-induced structural selection of the condensed state is identical to the single-shell theory
for $\varphi_-$.
Specifically, the one-loop corrected quartic coefficient takes the factorized form
\begin{equation}
\beta_{{\rm eff},S}
=
\beta_{{\rm MF},S}
-\frac{u_{\rm eff}^2}{2}\,I_{--}(r_{\rm eff})\,\mathcal C_S,
\label{eq:betaeff_overlap}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
I_{--}(r_{\rm eff})
:=
\int_{\mathcal B}\frac{d^3q}{(2\pi)^3}\;
\frac{1}{\left[r_{\rm eff}+\kappa_{\rm eff}(q^2-k_0^2)^2\right]^2}
\end{equation}
is structure-independent and $\mathcal C_S=N_{{\rm loop},S}/N_S^2$ is the same resonance-loop ratio
as in the single-shell theory.
Therefore, for the cubic stars
\begin{equation}
\mathcal C_{\rm BCC}=\frac16>\mathcal C_{\rm FCC}=\frac18>\mathcal C_{\rm SC}=0,
\end{equation}
one obtains in the fluctuation-dominated regime
\begin{equation}
\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm BCC}}<\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm FCC}}<\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm SC}},
\end{equation}
i.e.\ the BCC hierarchy persists even when the two shells overlap strongly.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Lemma~\eqref{eq:Seff_minus}, the effective soft-mode theory is an isotropic single-band Brazovskii
functional with a local quartic coupling $u_{\rm eff}$. The one-loop quartic correction is therefore the
standard bubble integral built from the $\varphi_-$ propagator, which is independent of the lattice
candidate $S$. Structure dependence enters only through the discrete resonance-loop combinatorics
$\mathcal C_S$, giving \eqref{eq:betaeff_overlap}. The hierarchy then follows from the known ordering of
$\mathcal C_S$ for cubic stars.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Failure mode (outside Universality F)}

The conclusion can fail only if the single-soft-mode assumption \eqref{eq:gap_assumption} fails, i.e.\
if \emph{both} eigenvalues $\lambda_\pm(q)$ become soft on the band (true two-mode criticality), or if
isotropy/locality is broken so that structure-specific weights enter the loop integrals.

% ==============================
%  Universality F (continued): the genuinely two-soft-mode case and a non-inversion theorem
% ==============================

\subsection{The genuinely two-soft-mode regime: coupled Brazovskii fields}

We now drop the single-soft-mode assumption \eqref{eq:gap_assumption} and consider the case where
\emph{both} eigenmodes become soft on the same isotropic band around $k_0$:
\begin{equation}
\lambda_-(q)\to 0^+,\qquad \lambda_+(q)\to 0^+ \qquad (q\simeq k_0).
\end{equation}
In this regime no mode can be integrated out, and the effective theory is a \emph{two-field}
(isotropic) Brazovskii functional.

\subsubsection{Effective action and quartic tensor}

Assume the most general local quartic interaction compatible with $O(2)$ rotations in field space:
\begin{equation}
S_4
=
\int d^3x\left[
\frac{u_1}{4!}\,\varphi_-^4
+
\frac{u_2}{4!}\,\varphi_+^4
+
\frac{w}{4}\,\varphi_-^2\varphi_+^2
\right],
\label{eq:twofield_quartic}
\end{equation}
with $u_1,u_2>0$ and $w$ not necessarily small (stability requires $w>- \sqrt{u_1u_2}/3$ in this
normalization).

The quadratic sector is
\begin{equation}
S_2
=
\frac12\int_{\mathbf q}\left[
\varphi_-(\mathbf q)\lambda_-(q)\varphi_-(-\mathbf q)
+
\varphi_+(\mathbf q)\lambda_+(q)\varphi_+(-\mathbf q)
\right],
\end{equation}
with isotropic dispersions
\begin{equation}
\lambda_a(q)=r_a+\kappa_a(q^2-k_0^2)^2+O\!\left((q^2-k_0^2)^3\right),
\qquad a\in\{-,+\}.
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{Equal-amplitude star ansatz with a two-component amplitude vector}

For a candidate structure $S$, take
\begin{equation}
\varphi_a(x)=A_a\sum_{i=1}^{N_S}\cos(\mathbf k_i\cdot x),
\qquad |\mathbf k_i|=k_0,
\qquad a\in\{-,+\},
\end{equation}
and define the amplitude vector $\mathbf A=(A_-,A_+)$.

The mean-field Landau functional becomes
\begin{equation}
\begin{align} \begin{split}
F_S(\mathbf A)
=
\frac12 r_- A_-^2 + \frac12 r_+ A_+^2
+
\frac14 \beta_{S}^{--} A_-^4
\\ +
\frac14 \beta_{S}^{++} A_+^4
+
\frac12 \beta_{S}^{-+} A_-^2 A_+^2
+
\frac16 \gamma_S(\mathbf A)\,(\text{6th order}),
\end{split} \end{align}
\end{equation}
where the quartic coefficients factorize as
\begin{equation}
\beta_{S}^{--}=u_1\,\beta_{{\rm MF},S},\qquad
\beta_{S}^{++}=u_2\,\beta_{{\rm MF},S},\qquad
\beta_{S}^{-+}=w\,\beta_{{\rm MF},S},
\label{eq:beta_tensor_factor}
\end{equation}
because the spatial star combinatorics is common and only multiplies the internal coupling.

\subsubsection{One-loop correction: matrix bubble and geometric factorization}

At one loop, the quartic tensor renormalizes via bubble integrals in each channel.
Define the structure-independent shell integrals
\begin{equation}
\begin{align} \begin{split}
I_{ab}(r_a,r_b)
:=
\int_{\mathcal B}\frac{d^3q}{(2\pi)^3}\;
\frac{1}{\left[r_a+\kappa_a(q^2-k_0^2)^2\right]}
\\ \times \frac{1}{\left[r_b+\kappa_b(q^2-k_0^2)^2\right]},
\qquad a,b\in\{-,+\}.
\end{split} \end{align}
\end{equation}
Then the one-loop renormalized quartic tensor has the schematic form
\begin{equation}
\beta^{ab}_{{\rm eff},S}
=
\beta^{ab}_{{\rm MF},S}
-\frac12
\sum_{c,d\in\{-,+\}}
\beta^{ac}_{{\rm MF},S}\,
I_{cd}\,
\beta^{db}_{{\rm MF},S}\,
\mathcal C_S
+\cdots,
\label{eq:twofield_1loop_tensor}
\end{equation}
where the ellipsis denotes structure-independent contributions and higher operators,
and $\mathcal C_S=N_{{\rm loop},S}/N_S^2$ is the same spatial resonance ratio as before.
Crucially, the \emph{entire} structure dependence continues to factorize through $\mathcal C_S$.

\subsubsection{Non-inversion theorem for two-soft-mode Brazovskii fields}

\begin{theorem}[Two-soft-mode universality of BCC ranking]
Assume:
(i) isotropic dispersions for both modes around the same $k_0$ band,
(ii) local quartic interaction \eqref{eq:twofield_quartic},
(iii) equal-amplitude star ansatz common across candidates.

Then the one-loop corrected quartic form entering the Landau functional for structure $S$ can be written as
\begin{equation}
Q_S(\mathbf A)
=
\beta_{{\rm MF},S}\,q_0(\mathbf A)
-
\mathcal C_S\,q_1(\mathbf A)\,,
\label{eq:QS_form}
\end{equation}
where $q_0(\mathbf A)\ge 0$ and $q_1(\mathbf A)\ge 0$ are \emph{structure-independent}
quartic forms determined solely by $(u_1,u_2,w)$ and the shell integrals $I_{ab}$.
Consequently, for any fixed nonzero amplitude vector $\mathbf A$,
\begin{equation}
Q_{\rm BCC}(\mathbf A)<Q_{\rm FCC}(\mathbf A)<Q_{\rm SC}(\mathbf A),
\end{equation}
whenever $\mathcal C_{\rm BCC}>\mathcal C_{\rm FCC}>\mathcal C_{\rm SC}$.
In particular, in the fluctuation-dominated regime the BCC structure remains the uniquely selected
cubic candidate even when both modes are simultaneously soft.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The mean-field quartic contribution factorizes as in \eqref{eq:beta_tensor_factor}, yielding
$Q^{\rm MF}_S(\mathbf A)=\beta_{{\rm MF},S}\,q_0(\mathbf A)$ with a structure-independent $q_0\ge 0$.
The one-loop correction \eqref{eq:twofield_1loop_tensor} is a contraction of the mean-field quartic tensor
with the structure-independent bubble matrix $I_{ab}$, hence produces a structure-independent quartic form
$q_1(\mathbf A)\ge 0$ multiplied by the sole spatial combinatorial factor $\mathcal C_S$.
Therefore $Q_S(\mathbf A)$ has the stated form \eqref{eq:QS_form}.
If $\mathcal C_{S_1}>\mathcal C_{S_2}$, then $Q_{S_1}(\mathbf A)<Q_{S_2}(\mathbf A)$ for any fixed $\mathbf A\neq 0$
whenever the fluctuation term dominates differences; the cubic ordering follows from the known values of
$\mathcal C_S$.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{Remark: what could break the two-mode universality}

The factorization in \eqref{eq:twofield_1loop_tensor} can fail only if:
\begin{equation}
\begin{align} \begin{split}
\text{(a) anisotropic dispersions } \lambda_a(\mathbf q)\neq \lambda_a(|\mathbf q|), \\ \text{(b) momentum-dependent/nonlocal quartic vertices},
\\ \text{(c) distinct preferred radii } k_{0,-}\neq k_{0,+},
\end{split} \end{align}
\end{equation}
each of which introduces new structure-specific weights beyond $\mathcal C_S$.

% ==============================
%  Universality G: Momentum-dependent quartic vertex (u -> u(angles))
%  Minimal theorem: small anisotropy preserves ranking
% ==============================

\section{Universality G: Momentum-Dependent Quartic Vertices}

\subsection{Setup: isotropic quadratic shell with an angular-dependent quartic kernel}

Keep the isotropic Brazovskii propagator on a (possibly thick) shell around $k_0$:
\begin{equation}
G(q)=\frac{1}{r+\kappa(q^2-k_0^2)^2},
\qquad q:=|\mathbf q|.
\end{equation}
Allow a momentum-dependent local-in-space but angle-dependent quartic vertex on the shell:
\begin{equation}
\begin{align} \begin{split}
S_4
=
\frac{1}{4!}
\int \prod_{i=1}^4 \frac{d^3q_i}{(2\pi)^3}\;
(2\pi)^3\delta\!\left(\sum_{i=1}^4 \mathbf q_i\right)\;
\\ \times u(\hat{\mathbf q}_1,\hat{\mathbf q}_2,\hat{\mathbf q}_3,\hat{\mathbf q}_4)\,
\psi(\mathbf q_1)\psi(\mathbf q_2)\psi(\mathbf q_3)\psi(\mathbf q_4),
\label{eq:u_angle_vertex}
\end{split} \end{align}
\end{equation}
where $\hat{\mathbf q}:=\mathbf q/|\mathbf q|$ and $u$ is symmetric under permutations of its arguments.

Decompose
\begin{equation}
u(\hat{\mathbf q}_1,\hat{\mathbf q}_2,\hat{\mathbf q}_3,\hat{\mathbf q}_4)
=
u_0 + \delta u(\hat{\mathbf q}_1,\hat{\mathbf q}_2,\hat{\mathbf q}_3,\hat{\mathbf q}_4),
\mspace{10}
u_0:=\langle u\rangle_{\rm ang},
\end{equation}
where $\langle\cdot\rangle_{\rm ang}$ denotes the uniform average over the shell angles and
$\langle \delta u\rangle_{\rm ang}=0$.

\subsection{Mean-field quartic coefficients: perturbation around the isotropic case}

For a candidate structure $S$ with star $\{\mathbf k_i\}_{i=1}^{N_S}$, $|\mathbf k_i|=k_0$,
the equal-amplitude ansatz yields a mean-field quartic coefficient of the form
\begin{equation}
\beta_{{\rm MF},S}
=
\beta_{{\rm MF},S}^{(0)}\,u_0
+
\delta\beta_{{\rm MF},S},
\label{eq:betaMF_decomp}
\end{equation}
where $\beta_{{\rm MF},S}^{(0)}$ is the purely geometric quartic coefficient in the isotropic-vertex theory,
and $\delta\beta_{{\rm MF},S}$ is the correction induced by $\delta u$ evaluated on the finite set of
resonant quartets of the star.

Define the uniform bound
\begin{equation}
\|\delta u\|_\infty
:=
\sup_{\hat{\mathbf q}_1,\dots,\hat{\mathbf q}_4\in S^2}
|\delta u(\hat{\mathbf q}_1,\hat{\mathbf q}_2,\hat{\mathbf q}_3,\hat{\mathbf q}_4)|.
\end{equation}

\begin{lemma}[Star evaluation bound]
There exists a structure-dependent constant $K_S>0$ (depending only on the number of resonant quartets
used in the equal-amplitude reduction) such that
\begin{equation}
|\delta\beta_{{\rm MF},S}|
\le
K_S\,\|\delta u\|_\infty.
\label{eq:delta_betaMF_bound}
\end{equation}
\end{lemma}

\subsection{One-loop correction: leading factorization and controlled remainder}

At one loop, the dominant bubble correction built from the isotropic propagator still yields the
divergent shell integral $I_{\rm bubble}(r;\Delta k)$.
The structure-dependent part of the fluctuation correction can be decomposed as
\begin{equation}
\delta\beta_{{\rm fluc},S}
=
-\frac12\,I_{\rm bubble}(r;\Delta k)\,
\left[
u_0^2\,\mathcal C_S
+
R_S
\right],
\label{eq:fluc_decomp}
\end{equation}
where $\mathcal C_S=N_{{\rm loop},S}/N_S^2$ is the isotropic-loop ratio and $R_S$ is the remainder
generated by $\delta u$.

\begin{lemma}[Remainder bound]
There exists a constant $L_S>0$ (depending only on the finite star data) such that
\begin{equation}
|R_S|
\le
L_S\left(|u_0|\,\|\delta u\|_\infty+\|\delta u\|_\infty^2\right).
\label{eq:R_bound}
\end{equation}
\end{lemma}

\subsection{Theorem: small angular anisotropy cannot invert the BCC hierarchy}

Let $S_1,S_2\in\{\rm BCC,FCC,SC\}$.
Write the full quartic coefficient as
\begin{equation}
\beta_{{\rm eff},S}
=
\beta_{{\rm MF},S}
-\frac12 I_{\rm bubble}\left[u_0^2\mathcal C_S+R_S\right].
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[Stability of ranking under small angular anisotropy]
Assume the isotropic theory yields the strict hierarchy
\begin{equation}
\mathcal C_{\rm BCC}>\mathcal C_{\rm FCC}>\mathcal C_{\rm SC},
\qquad
\Delta\mathcal C_{BF}:=\mathcal C_{\rm BCC}-\mathcal C_{\rm FCC}>0.
\end{equation}
Then there exists an explicit $\varepsilon>0$ such that if
\begin{equation}
\|\delta u\|_\infty \le \varepsilon\,|u_0|,
\label{eq:small_aniso_cond}
\end{equation}
the BCC$>$FCC ordering cannot be inverted by the angular dependence of the vertex, i.e.
\begin{equation}
\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm BCC}}<\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm FCC}}
\end{equation}
holds in the fluctuation-dominated regime.

A sufficient choice is obtained by requiring the anisotropic remainders and mean-field shifts be
smaller than the isotropic hierarchy gap:
\begin{equation}
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
K_{\rm BCC}\|\delta u\|_\infty+K_{\rm FCC}\|\delta u\|_\infty
\\ +
\frac12 I_{\rm bubble}\left(L_{\rm BCC}+L_{\rm FCC}\right)
\left(|u_0|\,\|\delta u\|_\infty+\|\delta u\|_\infty^2\right)
\\ <
\frac12 I_{\rm bubble}\,u_0^2\,\Delta\mathcal C_{BF}.
\label{eq:small_aniso_gap}
\end{split}
\end{align}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\subsection{Remark: outside the small-anisotropy regime}

If $\delta u$ is not small in the sense of \eqref{eq:small_aniso_cond}, the vertex can introduce genuinely
new structure-specific weights and the $\mathcal C_S$-based universality may fail.
In that case one must compute the star-evaluated quartic tensor explicitly for each candidate structure.

% ==============================
%  Universality H: Anisotropic quadratic kernel (weak anisotropy preserves ranking)
% ==============================

\section{Universality H: Weakly Anisotropic Quadratic Kernels}

\subsection{Setup: anisotropic soft band around $k_0$}

Replace the isotropic Brazovskii kernel by a weakly anisotropic one:
\begin{equation}
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
G^{-1}(\mathbf q)
=
r+\kappa\,(q^2-k_0^2)^2
+\delta K(\hat{\mathbf q})\,(q^2-k_0^2)^2,
\qquad
\\ \hat{\mathbf q}:=\mathbf q/|\mathbf q|,
\label{eq:anisotropic_kernel}
\end{split}
\end{align}
\end{equation}
where $\delta K$ is an angular modulation with zero mean
\begin{equation}
\langle \delta K\rangle_{\rm ang}=0,
\qquad
\|\delta K\|_\infty:=\sup_{\hat{\mathbf q}\in S^2}|\delta K(\hat{\mathbf q})|.
\end{equation}
Assume $\|\delta K\|_\infty<\kappa$ so that the coefficient of $(q^2-k_0^2)^2$ remains positive.

We keep a local quartic interaction (scalar for definiteness):
\begin{equation}
S_4=\int d^3x\;\frac{u}{4!}\psi^4.
\end{equation}

\subsection{Perturbative control of anisotropic shell integrals}

Define the anisotropic bubble integral
\begin{equation}
I_{\rm bubble}^{\rm aniso}(r)
:=
\int_{\mathcal B}\frac{d^3q}{(2\pi)^3}\;
\frac{1}{\left[r+(q^2-k_0^2)^2\big(\kappa+\delta K(\hat{\mathbf q})\big)\right]^2},
\label{eq:I_aniso_def}
\end{equation}
where $\mathcal B$ is a fixed isotropic band around $q\simeq k_0$ (e.g.\ $|q-k_0|\le \Delta k$).

\begin{lemma}[Relative error bound]
There exists $C>0$ (depending only on $k_0,\Delta k$) such that for all sufficiently small $r>0$,
\begin{equation}
\left|
\frac{I_{\rm bubble}^{\rm aniso}(r)-I_{\rm bubble}(r)}{I_{\rm bubble}(r)}
\right|
\le
C\,\frac{\|\delta K\|_\infty}{\kappa},
\label{eq:I_aniso_relerr}
\end{equation}
where $I_{\rm bubble}(r)$ is the isotropic bubble integral.
\end{lemma}

\subsection{Star-dependent anisotropic sampling}

For a candidate structure $S$ with star directions $\{\hat{\mathbf k}_i\}_{i=1}^{N_S}$, define the
\emph{star average} of $\delta K$:
\begin{equation}
\overline{\delta K}_S
:=
\frac{1}{N_S}\sum_{i=1}^{N_S}\delta K(\hat{\mathbf k}_i).
\label{eq:staravg_deltaK}
\end{equation}
This captures how the discrete star samples the anisotropy.

\begin{lemma}[Star-sampling bound]
For any $S$,
\begin{equation}
|\overline{\delta K}_S|\le \|\delta K\|_\infty,
\qquad
|\overline{\delta K}_{S_1}-\overline{\delta K}_{S_2}|
\le 2\|\delta K\|_\infty.
\label{eq:staravg_bound}
\end{equation}
\end{lemma}

\subsection{One-loop quartic correction with anisotropic sampling}

Under equal-amplitude reduction, the one-loop quartic correction for structure $S$ takes the form
\begin{equation}
\delta\beta_{{\rm fluc},S}
=
-\frac{u^2}{2}\,
I_{\rm bubble}(r)\,
\mathcal C_S
+
\Delta_S,
\label{eq:anisofluc_split}
\end{equation}
where $\Delta_S$ collects anisotropy-induced deviations from the isotropic factorization.
For weak anisotropy, $\Delta_S$ is controlled by star sampling:
\begin{equation}
|\Delta_S|
\le
I_{\rm bubble}(r)\,
u^2\,
\mathcal C_S\,
\widetilde C\,
\frac{\|\delta K\|_\infty}{\kappa}
+
I_{\rm bubble}(r)\,
u^2\,
\widetilde C'\,
\frac{|\overline{\delta K}_S|}{\kappa},
\label{eq:DeltaS_bound}
\end{equation}
for constants $\widetilde C,\widetilde C'>0$ depending only on the band geometry.

\subsection{Theorem: weak anisotropy cannot invert BCC hierarchy}

Let $\Delta\mathcal C_{BF}:=\mathcal C_{\rm BCC}-\mathcal C_{\rm FCC}=1/24$.
In the isotropic theory, the hierarchy is driven by the gap
\begin{equation}
\delta_{\rm iso}(r):=\frac{u^2}{2}I_{\rm bubble}(r)\,\Delta\mathcal C_{BF}>0.
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[Stability under weak quadratic anisotropy]
Assume:
(i) the anisotropy is weak, $\|\delta K\|_\infty/\kappa \le \epsilon$,
(ii) the fluctuation term dominates mean-field differences (preemptive regime),
(iii) the anisotropy-induced deviations satisfy the bound \eqref{eq:DeltaS_bound}.

Then the BCC$>$FCC ordering cannot be inverted provided
\begin{equation}
|\Delta_{\rm BCC}-\Delta_{\rm FCC}|<\delta_{\rm iso}(r).
\label{eq:aniso_noninvert_condition}
\end{equation}
A sufficient explicit condition is
\begin{equation}
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
2I_{\rm bubble}(r)\,u^2
\left[
\widetilde C\,\frac{\|\delta K\|_\infty}{\kappa}
+
\widetilde C'\,\frac{\|\delta K\|_\infty}{\kappa}
\right]
\\ <
\frac{u^2}{2}I_{\rm bubble}(r)\,\Delta\mathcal C_{BF},
\end{split} \end{align}
\end{equation}
i.e.
\begin{equation}
\frac{\|\delta K\|_\infty}{\kappa}
<
\frac{\Delta\mathcal C_{BF}}{4(\widetilde C+\widetilde C')}.
\label{eq:aniso_smallness}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\subsection{Remark: beyond weak anisotropy}

If $\|\delta K\|_\infty/\kappa$ is not small, discrete star sampling can produce genuinely new
structure-dependent weights, and the $\mathcal C_S$ universality need not hold.
In that regime one must compute the anisotropic shell integrals restricted to each star explicitly.

% ==============================
%  Universality I: Synthesis theorem (maximal universality class proved)
% ==============================

\section{Universality I: Synthesis --- Maximal Proven Universality Class for BCC Selection}

\subsection{Statement of the universality class}

Consider a class of Brazovskii-type theories in $d=3$ characterized by:
\begin{enumerate}
\item (\textbf{Soft band}) A soft momentum band around a characteristic radius $k_0>0$,
with quadratic kernels (possibly multi-field) that are \emph{isotropic} up to a controlled anisotropy:
\begin{equation}
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
G_a^{-1}(\mathbf q)=r_a+\kappa_a(q^2-k_0^2)^2+\delta K_a(\hat{\mathbf q})(q^2-k_0^2)^2,
\\ \qquad \|\delta K_a\|_\infty/\kappa_a \le \epsilon_K.
\end{split} \end{align}
\end{equation}

\item (\textbf{Multi-shell / multi-mode}) A finite number of shell components and/or coupled modes,
with either (i) generic radius ratios (no mixed resonances), or (ii) resonant ratios satisfying the
explicit non-inversion conditions derived in Universality~D--E, or (iii) strong overlap reducing to
either one soft eigenmode or two soft eigenmodes as in Universality~F.

\item (\textbf{Local quartic}) A local quartic interaction, with either
(a) momentum-independent coupling, or (b) a weakly anisotropic angular dependence on the shell:
\begin{equation}
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
u(\hat{\mathbf q}_1,\dots,\hat{\mathbf q}_4)=u_0+\delta u(\hat{\mathbf q}_1,\dots,\hat{\mathbf q}_4),
\\ \qquad \|\delta u\|_\infty \le \epsilon_u |u_0|.
\end{split} \end{align}
\end{equation}

\item (\textbf{Equal-amplitude star reduction}) For each candidate cubic structure
$S\in\{\mathrm{SC,FCC,BCC}\}$, the condensed state is represented by an equal-amplitude reciprocal-star
ansatz on the dominant soft band.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Main theorem}

Let the primary cubic stars be the standard ones:
$N_{\rm SC}=6$, $N_{\rm FCC}=8$, $N_{\rm BCC}=12$ with
\begin{equation}
\mathcal C_{\rm SC}=0, \mspace{10}  \mathcal C_{\rm FCC}=\frac18, \mspace{10}  \mathcal C_{\rm BCC}=\frac16, \mspace{10} \Delta\mathcal C_{BF}=\frac{1}{24}.
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[Maximal proven universality of BCC selection]
Within the universality class specified above, there exists an $\epsilon_*>0$ such that for all
$\epsilon_K,\epsilon_u<\epsilon_*$, and for all admissible multi-shell/multi-mode configurations satisfying
the generic- or resonant-case criteria (Universality~D--F),
the fluctuation-corrected quartic functional obeys, in the fluctuation-dominated (preemptive) regime,
\begin{equation}
\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm BCC}} < \beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm FCC}} < \beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm SC}}.
\end{equation}
Consequently, among the cubic competitors, the BCC structure is uniquely selected by quartic
Brazovskii fluctuations throughout this class.
\end{theorem}

\subsection{Proof (by reduction to previous universality steps)}

\begin{proof}
The proof is by cases, using the reduction theorems established earlier.

\paragraph{Case 1: single-shell (finite thickness allowed).}
Universality~A gives structure-independent shell integrals and factorization of the one-loop correction,
so ordering follows from $\mathcal C_{\rm BCC}>\mathcal C_{\rm FCC}>\mathcal C_{\rm SC}$.
Universality~B extends to $O(n)$ multiplets, and Universality~C guarantees higher-loop non-inversion
within the isotropic local truncation.

\paragraph{Case 2: two shells with separated radii.}
Universality~D--E show: (i) for generic ratios $k_1/k_0\notin\mathfrak E$, mixed resonances vanish and
the reduction to Case~1 is exact; (ii) for resonant ratios, the explicit inequality
$r_0<\frac{1}{600 n^{\max}}\frac{\kappa_1\Delta^2}{\sqrt{\kappa_0}}$ suffices to suppress mixed terms,
thus preserving the Case~1 ranking.

\paragraph{Case 3: strong shell overlap.}
Universality~F shows that if a gapped eigenmode exists, the theory reduces to a single soft Brazovskii
mode and hence to Case~1; if two soft modes exist, the quartic form still factorizes into a structure-
independent internal form times the spatial combinatorics, preserving the ranking.

\paragraph{Case 4: weak angular dependence of the quartic vertex.}
Universality~G provides a perturbative stability bound: for sufficiently small $\epsilon_u$,
the anisotropic corrections cannot overcome the isotropic hierarchy gap $\Delta\mathcal C_{BF}$.

\paragraph{Case 5: weak anisotropy of the quadratic kernel.}
Universality~H provides an analogous stability bound in $\epsilon_K$, ensuring that anisotropic sampling
cannot invert the hierarchy when $\epsilon_K$ is sufficiently small.

Combining the cases yields the claim for all $\epsilon_K,\epsilon_u<\epsilon_*$.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Sharp failure modes (outside the proven class)}

The theorem can fail only if one exits the proven universality class, e.g.:
\begin{equation}
\begin{split} 
\text{strong anisotropy }(\epsilon_K\sim 1),
\\ \text{strongly momentum-dependent/nonlocal vertices }(\epsilon_u\sim 1),
\\ \text{distinct preferred radii for different modes},
\\ \text{explicit lattice-pinning fields}.
\end{split}
\end{equation}
In such cases genuinely new structure-dependent weights beyond $\mathcal C_S$ may appear.

% ==============================
%  Next step: remove equal-amplitude ansatz (amplitude-optimization theorem)
%  Goal: show BCC wins after optimizing over amplitudes within each star
% ==============================

\section{Universality J: Removing the Equal-Amplitude Assumption (Amplitude Optimization)}

\subsection{General star expansion and amplitude space}

Fix a candidate structure $S$ with reciprocal-star wavevectors $\{\mathbf k_i\}_{i=1}^{N_S}$, $|\mathbf k_i|=k_0$.
Consider the most general real field restricted to this star:
\begin{equation}
\psi_S(x)=\sum_{i=1}^{N_S} a_i \cos(\mathbf k_i\cdot x),
\qquad
\mathbf a=(a_1,\dots,a_{N_S})\in\mathbb R^{N_S}.
\end{equation}

Define the quadratic and quartic functionals restricted to this star:
\begin{equation}
F^{(2)}_S(\mathbf a)=\frac12 r \sum_{i=1}^{N_S} a_i^2,
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
F^{(4)}_S(\mathbf a)
=
\frac{u}{4!}\int d^3x\;\psi_S(x)^4
=
\frac{u}{4!}\sum_{i,j,k,\ell=1}^{N_S}
T^{(S)}_{ijkl}\,a_i a_j a_k a_\ell,
\label{eq:T_tensor_def}
\end{equation}
where the \emph{star tensor} $T^{(S)}_{ijkl}$ counts the spatial average
\begin{equation}
T^{(S)}_{ijkl}:=\int d^3x\;\cos(\mathbf k_i\cdot x)\cos(\mathbf k_j\cdot x)\cos(\mathbf k_k\cdot x)\cos(\mathbf k_\ell\cdot x).
\end{equation}
(Equivalently, $T^{(S)}_{ijkl}$ is proportional to the number of sign choices such that
$\pm \mathbf k_i\pm \mathbf k_j\pm \mathbf k_k\pm \mathbf k_\ell=\mathbf 0$.)

The fluctuation correction produces a negative quartic form of the same tensorial type:
\begin{equation}
\Delta F^{(4)}_S(\mathbf a)
=
-\frac{u^2}{2}I_{\rm bubble}(r)\,
\frac{1}{N_S^2}
\sum_{i,j,k,\ell=1}^{N_S}
\widetilde T^{(S)}_{ijkl}\,a_i a_j a_k a_\ell,
\end{equation}
where $\widetilde T^{(S)}_{ijkl}$ encodes the nontrivial resonance-loop subset.
In the equal-amplitude reduction, only the fully symmetric contraction survives and yields $\mathcal C_S$.
We now avoid that reduction.
