\subsection{Normalized amplitude optimization problem}

Impose a normalization $\sum_i a_i^2=1$ (overall scale is fixed by minimizing including $r$ and $A^6$ terms).
Define the normalized quartic forms
\begin{equation}
\begin{align} \begin{split}
\mathcal Q^{\rm MF}_S(\mathbf a):=
\sum_{i,j,k,\ell} T^{(S)}_{ijkl}\,a_i a_j a_k a_\ell,
\\ \qquad
\mathcal Q^{\rm fluc}_S(\mathbf a):=
\sum_{i,j,k,\ell} \widetilde T^{(S)}_{ijkl}\,a_i a_j a_k a_\ell.
\end{split} \end{align}
\end{equation}
The effective quartic functional at fixed $(r,u)$ is then
\begin{equation}
\mathcal Q^{\rm eff}_S(\mathbf a)
=
u\,\mathcal Q^{\rm MF}_S(\mathbf a)
-
u^2 I_{\rm bubble}(r)\,\frac{1}{N_S^2}\,\mathcal Q^{\rm fluc}_S(\mathbf a).
\end{equation}

The structure selection is governed by the minimized value
\begin{equation}
\mathcal Q^{\rm eff,*}_S := \min_{\mathbf a\in\mathbb R^{N_S},\,\sum a_i^2=1}\mathcal Q^{\rm eff}_S(\mathbf a).
\label{eq:Qstar_def}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Key lemma: group-averaging yields an $O_h$-invariant minimizer}

Let $G_S$ be the symmetry group of the star (a subgroup of $O_h$ acting by permuting indices).
For any amplitude vector $\mathbf a$, define its group average
\begin{equation}
\bar{\mathbf a}:=\frac{1}{|G_S|}\sum_{g\in G_S} g\cdot \mathbf a.
\end{equation}

\begin{lemma}[Symmetry reduction]
Assume:
(i) the tensors $T^{(S)}_{ijkl}$ and $\widetilde T^{(S)}_{ijkl}$ are invariant under $G_S$ index permutations,
(ii) $\mathcal Q^{\rm eff}_S$ is convex along group orbits (true for the quartic forms arising from averages).
Then any minimizer of \eqref{eq:Qstar_def} can be chosen $G_S$-invariant, i.e.\ proportional to the
equal-amplitude vector $\mathbf 1=(1,1,\dots,1)$.
\end{lemma}

\subsection{Proposition: equal-amplitude is globally optimal in the fluctuation-dominated regime}

\begin{proposition}[Equal-amplitude optimality]
In the fluctuation-dominated regime (where the negative fluctuation term dominates the inter-structure differences),
the minimizer of $\mathcal Q^{\rm eff}_S$ under $\sum a_i^2=1$ is the $G_S$-invariant vector.
Consequently,
\begin{equation}
\mathcal Q^{\rm eff,*}_S
=
u\,\mathcal Q^{\rm MF}_S(\mathbf 1/\sqrt{N_S})
-
u^2 I_{\rm bubble}(r)\,\mathcal C_S,
\end{equation}
and the BCC ranking is unchanged by allowing arbitrary amplitude distortions within the star.
\end{proposition}

\subsection{Status}

Universality~J reduces structural selection to an explicit constrained minimization.
To \emph{fully close} this step rigorously, one must verify the convexity/invariance hypothesis
for the specific tensors $T^{(S)}$ and $\widetilde T^{(S)}$ (finite-dimensional, checkable),
or provide a direct inequality showing that $\mathcal Q^{\rm fluc}_S$ is maximized at equal amplitudes,
hence $\mathcal Q^{\rm eff}_S$ minimized there.

% ==============================
%  Universality J (continued): rigorous equal-amplitude optimality
%  Key: rewrite fluctuation quartic as sum of squares and apply Cauchy--Schwarz
% ==============================

\subsection{Exact square-sum representation of the fluctuation quartic form}

Fix a star $S$ with wavevectors $\{\mathbf k_i\}_{i=1}^{N_S}$, $|\mathbf k_i|=k_0$.
For any amplitude vector $\mathbf a\in\mathbb R^{N_S}$ define the bilinear ``pair-field''
\begin{equation}
B(\mathbf q;\mathbf a):=\sum_{i,j=1}^{N_S} a_i a_j\;\delta_{\mathbf q,\mathbf k_i+\mathbf k_j},
\end{equation}
where $\delta_{\mathbf q,\mathbf p}$ is the Kronecker delta on the discrete set of pair-sums
$\mathbf q\in\{\mathbf k_i+\mathbf k_j\}$.

Let $\mathcal P_S$ denote the set of \emph{nontrivial} pair-sums (excluding $\mathbf q=\mathbf 0$ from $\pm$ pairings):
\begin{equation}
\mathcal P_S := \{\mathbf q\neq \mathbf 0:\exists i,j\ \text{s.t.}\ \mathbf q=\mathbf k_i+\mathbf k_j\}.
\end{equation}

\begin{lemma}[Square-sum form of the resonant quartic]
Under the standard 1-loop Brazovskii contraction on a single shell, the structure-dependent (resonant)
fluctuation quartic form can be written exactly as
\begin{equation}
\mathcal Q^{\rm fluc}_S(\mathbf a)
=
\sum_{\mathbf q\in\mathcal P_S} \left|B(\mathbf q;\mathbf a)\right|^2.
\label{eq:Qfluc_square_sum}
\end{equation}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
A nontrivial resonance loop is a quartet $(i,j,k,\ell)$ with
$\mathbf k_i+\mathbf k_j+\mathbf k_k+\mathbf k_\ell=\mathbf 0$ not reducible to trivial $\pm$ pairings.
Equivalently, it is a match of two nonzero pair-sums:
\begin{equation}
\mathbf k_i+\mathbf k_j = -(\mathbf k_k+\mathbf k_\ell)=:\mathbf q\neq \mathbf 0.
\end{equation}
Summing the amplitude weight $a_i a_j a_k a_\ell$ over all such quartets groups naturally by $\mathbf q$,
yielding precisely the square of the sum over pairs producing that $\mathbf q$.
This gives \eqref{eq:Qfluc_square_sum}.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Cauchy--Schwarz maximization at fixed $\ell^2$ norm}

Impose the normalization
\begin{equation}
\|\mathbf a\|_2^2=\sum_{i=1}^{N_S}a_i^2=1.
\end{equation}
For each $\mathbf q\in\mathcal P_S$, let
\begin{equation}
P_S(\mathbf q):=\{(i,j):\mathbf k_i+\mathbf k_j=\mathbf q\}
\end{equation}
be the set of ordered index pairs yielding $\mathbf q$, with cardinality
\begin{equation}
M_S(\mathbf q):=|P_S(\mathbf q)|.
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
B(\mathbf q;\mathbf a)=\sum_{(i,j)\in P_S(\mathbf q)} a_i a_j.
\end{equation}

\begin{lemma}[Uniform upper bound for each channel]
For each fixed $\mathbf q\in\mathcal P_S$,
\begin{equation}
\left|B(\mathbf q;\mathbf a)\right|^2
\le
M_S(\mathbf q)\sum_{(i,j)\in P_S(\mathbf q)} a_i^2 a_j^2,
\label{eq:channel_CS}
\end{equation}
with equality if and only if $a_i a_j$ is constant on $P_S(\mathbf q)$.
\end{lemma}

Apply Cauchy--Schwarz to the finite sum over $P_S(\mathbf q)$:

\begin{equation}
\begin{split}
%Apply Cauchy--Schwarz to the finite sum over $P_S(\mathbf q)$:
%\[
\left(\sum_{(i,j)\in P_S(\mathbf q)} a_i a_j\right)^2
\le
\left(\sum_{(i,j)\in P_S(\mathbf q)} 1\right)
\left(\sum_{(i,j)\in P_S(\mathbf q)} a_i^2 a_j^2\right)
\\ =
M_S(\mathbf q)\sum_{(i,j)\in P_S(\mathbf q)} a_i^2 a_j^2.
%\]
\end{split}
\end{equation}


Summing \eqref{eq:channel_CS} over $\mathbf q\in\mathcal P_S$ yields

\begin{equation}
\mathcal Q^{\rm fluc}_S(\mathbf a)
=
\sum_{\mathbf q\in\mathcal P_S}|B(\mathbf q;\mathbf a)|^2
\le
\sum_{\mathbf q\in\mathcal P_S} M_S(\mathbf q)
\sum_{(i,j)\in P_S(\mathbf q)} a_i^2 a_j^2.
\label{eq:Qfluc_bound1}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Transitivity closes the bound: cubic stars force equal amplitudes}

For the standard cubic stars (SC/FCC/BCC), the octahedral group $O_h$ acts transitively on star indices,
and also transitively on each orbit of nonzero pair-sums. Consequently:

\begin{assumption}[Orbit-regularity of cubic stars]
For each cubic star $S\in\{\mathrm{SC,FCC,BCC}\}$, the multiplicity $M_S(\mathbf q)$ is constant on
$\mathcal P_S$:
\begin{equation}
M_S(\mathbf q)\equiv M_S
\qquad \forall \mathbf q\in\mathcal P_S.
\label{eq:orbit_regular}
\end{equation}
\end{assumption}
(This is a finite check; it holds for the standard SC/FCC/BCC stars.)

Under \eqref{eq:orbit_regular}, \eqref{eq:Qfluc_bound1} simplifies:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal Q^{\rm fluc}_S(\mathbf a)
\le
M_S
\sum_{\mathbf q\in\mathcal P_S}
\sum_{(i,j)\in P_S(\mathbf q)} a_i^2 a_j^2
=
M_S
\sum_{(i,j)\in \mathcal I_S} a_i^2 a_j^2,
\label{eq:Qfluc_bound2}
\end{equation}
where $\mathcal I_S:=\bigcup_{\mathbf q\in\mathcal P_S}P_S(\mathbf q)$ is the set of ordered pairs that
participate in nontrivial pair-sums.

By symmetry of the cubic stars, each index $i$ appears in the same number $d_S$ of ordered pairs in
$\mathcal I_S$, hence
\begin{equation}
\sum_{(i,j)\in \mathcal I_S} a_i^2 a_j^2
=
\sum_{i=1}^{N_S} a_i^2 \left(\sum_{j\in \mathcal N_S(i)} a_j^2\right),
\qquad |\mathcal N_S(i)|\equiv d_S,
\end{equation}
with $\mathcal N_S(i)$ the neighbor-set induced by $\mathcal I_S$.

\begin{lemma}[Maximizer of the quadratic form on the simplex]
Let $x_i:=a_i^2\ge 0$ with $\sum_i x_i=1$. If the induced neighbor graph is regular (degree $d_S$) and
vertex-transitive (true for SC/FCC/BCC stars), then the functional
\begin{equation}
\Phi_S(\mathbf x):=\sum_{(i,j)\in \mathcal I_S} x_i x_j
\end{equation}
is maximized over the simplex at the uniform point $x_i\equiv 1/N_S$.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
$\Phi_S(\mathbf x)=\mathbf x^{\mathsf T}A_S\mathbf x$ where $A_S$ is the adjacency matrix of a regular
vertex-transitive graph. By Perron--Frobenius, the top eigenvector of $A_S$ is strictly positive and,
by transitivity, is proportional to the uniform vector $\mathbf 1$. The Rayleigh quotient is maximized
by this eigenvector subject to $\|\mathbf x\|_2=1$; restricting to the simplex yields the same maximizer.
\end{proof}

Combining this with \eqref{eq:Qfluc_bound2} gives:

\begin{theorem}[Equal-amplitude maximizes the fluctuation gain]
For each cubic star $S\in\{\mathrm{SC,FCC,BCC}\}$, among all amplitude vectors $\mathbf a$ with
$\sum_i a_i^2=1$, the fluctuation quartic
\begin{equation}
\mathcal Q^{\rm fluc}_S(\mathbf a)=\sum_{\mathbf q\in\mathcal P_S}\left|B(\mathbf q;\mathbf a)\right|^2
\end{equation}
is maximized by the equal-amplitude configuration
\begin{equation}
a_i\equiv \pm \frac{1}{\sqrt{N_S}}.
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\subsection{Corollary: amplitude optimization cannot defeat BCC}

In the fluctuation-dominated regime, the effective quartic functional has the schematic form
\begin{equation}
\mathcal Q^{\rm eff}_S(\mathbf a)
=
u\,\mathcal Q^{\rm MF}_S(\mathbf a)
-
u^2 I_{\rm bubble}(r)\,\frac{1}{N_S^2}\,\mathcal Q^{\rm fluc}_S(\mathbf a).
\end{equation}
Since the second term is \emph{negative} and dominates inter-structure differences, minimizing
$\mathcal Q^{\rm eff}_S$ at fixed $\|\mathbf a\|_2=1$ is achieved by maximizing $\mathcal Q^{\rm fluc}_S$,
hence at equal amplitude.

Therefore,
\begin{equation}
\begin{align} \begin{split}
\mathcal Q^{\rm eff,*}_S
=
\mathcal Q^{\rm eff}_S(\mathbf a_{\rm eq})
=
u\,\mathcal Q^{\rm MF}_S(\mathbf a_{\rm eq})
-
u^2 I_{\rm bubble}(r)\,\mathcal C_S,
\\ \qquad
\mathbf a_{\rm eq}=\frac{1}{\sqrt{N_S}}(1,\dots,1),
\end{split} \end{align}
\end{equation}
and the BCC$>$FCC$>$SC hierarchy derived under equal amplitudes is unchanged by allowing arbitrary
intra-star amplitude distortions.

% ==============================
%  Universality K: removing star-restriction (arbitrary superpositions on the shell)
%  Goal: show the minimizing configuration lies on a single cubic star (closure)
% ==============================

\section{Universality K: Beyond a Single Star --- Variational Reduction on the Full Shell}

\subsection{Full-shell variational problem}

Let $\psi(\mathbf q)$ be supported on an isotropic soft band $\mathcal B$ around $|\mathbf q|=k_0$.
Consider the (fluctuation-dominated) quartic effective functional at fixed quadratic norm:
\begin{equation}
\|\psi\|_2^2:=\int_{\mathcal B}\frac{d^3q}{(2\pi)^3}\,|\psi(\mathbf q)|^2 = 1.
\end{equation}
Define the resonant pair-field on the shell
\begin{equation}
B(\mathbf Q):=\int_{\mathcal B}\frac{d^3q}{(2\pi)^3}\;\psi(\mathbf q)\psi(\mathbf Q-\mathbf q),
\end{equation}
and note that the 1-loop Brazovskii quartic correction can be written as a sum/integral of squares:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal Q^{\rm fluc}[\psi]=\int d^3Q\;|B(\mathbf Q)|^2,
\label{eq:fullshell_square}
\end{equation}
restricted effectively to nontrivial $\mathbf Q$ supported by the band convolution.

The structural selection problem becomes the maximization of $\mathcal Q^{\rm fluc}[\psi]$ under
$\|\psi\|_2=1$ (since the fluctuation term enters with a negative sign in the free energy).

\subsection{Lemma: maximizers are finitely-supported extremals}

\begin{lemma}[Concentration of extremals]
Assume:
(i) $\mathcal B$ is thin (or regulated) so that all wavevectors have $|\mathbf q|\simeq k_0$,
(ii) the interaction kernel is local and isotropic.
Then any maximizer of \eqref{eq:fullshell_square} under $\|\psi\|_2=1$ can be taken to be supported on a
finite set of wavevectors $\{\mathbf k_i\}_{i=1}^N$ on the shell, i.e.
\begin{equation}
\psi(\mathbf q)=\sum_{i=1}^N a_i\,(2\pi)^3\delta(\mathbf q-\mathbf k_i),
\qquad |\mathbf k_i|=k_0,
\end{equation}
for some $N<\infty$.
\end{lemma}

\subsection{Reduction to discrete star optimization}

Under the finite-support form, \eqref{eq:fullshell_square} reduces to
\begin{equation}
\mathcal Q^{\rm fluc}(\{\mathbf k_i\},\mathbf a)
=
\sum_{\mathbf Q\neq 0}
\left|\sum_{i,j:\,\mathbf k_i+\mathbf k_j=\mathbf Q} a_i a_j\right|^2,
\end{equation}
with the normalization $\sum_i a_i^2=1$.

Define the discrete loop ratio for the configuration:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal C(\{\mathbf k_i\}):=\frac{N_{\rm loop}}{N^2},
\end{equation}
where $N_{\rm loop}$ counts nontrivial resonance quartets among the chosen wavevectors.

\subsection{Theorem: cubic extremals reduce to standard stars}

Restrict attention to \emph{cubic-symmetric} extremals: those whose support set is invariant under the
octahedral group $O_h$. Then the smallest nontrivial such invariant sets on the shell are precisely
the standard cubic stars:
\begin{equation}
U_{\rm SC},\qquad U_{\rm FCC},\qquad U_{\rm BCC}.
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[Reduction to cubic stars]
Among all cubic-symmetric finite-support configurations on the shell (with $\|\psi\|_2=1$),
the fluctuation functional $\mathcal Q^{\rm fluc}$ is maximized by one of the standard cubic stars
with equal amplitudes.
\end{theorem}

\subsection{Corollary: global cubic minimizer is BCC}

Since the fluctuation selection among cubic stars obeys
\begin{equation}
\mathcal C_{\rm BCC}>\mathcal C_{\rm FCC}>\mathcal C_{\rm SC},
\end{equation}
it follows that within the cubic-symmetric sector, the global minimizer of the fluctuation-dominated
free energy is the BCC star.

\subsection{Status}

Universality~K completes the removal of \emph{intra-star} assumptions (Universality~J) and begins the
removal of the \emph{single-star restriction}. To fully close the \emph{global} problem without assuming
cubic symmetry, one must analyze whether non-cubic support sets can beat the cubic stars in maximizing
\eqref{eq:fullshell_square}. This is a separate extremal problem on the sphere.

% ==============================
%  Universality K (continued): no non-cubic set can beat cubic stars
%  Strategy: show maximal resonance density is attained by BCC under isotropic constraints
%  (rigorous within the class of finite-support configurations with fixed N)
% ==============================

\subsection{Global comparison against non-cubic configurations (finite-support class)}

We now remove the \emph{cubic-symmetry} restriction and compare arbitrary finite-support configurations
on the shell against the cubic stars.

\subsubsection{Finite-support class and resonance density}

Consider a finite support set $K:=\{\mathbf k_i\}_{i=1}^N$ on the shell $|\mathbf k|=k_0$, and amplitudes
$\mathbf a\in\mathbb R^N$ with $\sum_{i=1}^N a_i^2=1$.

Define the set of nontrivial pair-sums
\begin{equation}
\mathcal P(K):=\{\mathbf Q\neq 0:\exists i,j\ \text{s.t. }\mathbf Q=\mathbf k_i+\mathbf k_j\},
\end{equation}
and the pair-multiplicity
\begin{equation}
M_K(\mathbf Q):=\#\{(i,j):\mathbf k_i+\mathbf k_j=\mathbf Q\}.
\end{equation}

Then the fluctuation functional is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal Q^{\rm fluc}(K,\mathbf a)
=
\sum_{\mathbf Q\in \mathcal P(K)}\left|\sum_{(i,j):\,\mathbf k_i+\mathbf k_j=\mathbf Q} a_i a_j\right|^2.
\label{eq:Qfluc_K}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{Universal upper bound at fixed $N$}

\begin{lemma}[Cauchy--Schwarz global bound]
For any $(K,\mathbf a)$ with $\sum_i a_i^2=1$,
\begin{equation}
\mathcal Q^{\rm fluc}(K,\mathbf a)
\le
\sum_{\mathbf Q\in \mathcal P(K)} M_K(\mathbf Q)\,
\sum_{(i,j):\,\mathbf k_i+\mathbf k_j=\mathbf Q} a_i^2 a_j^2.
\label{eq:global_CS1}
\end{equation}
Moreover,
\begin{equation}
\sum_{\mathbf Q\in \mathcal P(K)}
\sum_{(i,j):\,\mathbf k_i+\mathbf k_j=\mathbf Q} a_i^2 a_j^2
\le
\left(\sum_{i=1}^N a_i^2\right)^2
=1,
\label{eq:global_CS2}
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
\mathcal Q^{\rm fluc}(K,\mathbf a)
\le
\max_{\mathbf Q\in\mathcal P(K)} M_K(\mathbf Q).
\label{eq:global_bound_Mmax}
\end{equation}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Equation \eqref{eq:global_CS1} is channel-wise Cauchy--Schwarz as in \eqref{eq:channel_CS}.
For \eqref{eq:global_CS2}, note that each ordered pair $(i,j)$ contributes to exactly one $\mathbf Q=\mathbf k_i+\mathbf k_j$,
and the full sum over $(i,j)$ gives $(\sum_i a_i^2)(\sum_j a_j^2)=1$.
Then \eqref{eq:global_bound_Mmax} follows by taking the maximum multiplicity.
\end{proof}

Thus maximizing $\mathcal Q^{\rm fluc}$ requires producing a configuration $K$ with a large
pair-sum multiplicity $M_K(\mathbf Q)$ for some nonzero $\mathbf Q$.

\subsubsection{Geometric constraint: pair-sum multiplicity on a sphere}

Fix $\mathbf Q\neq 0$. The constraint $\mathbf k_i+\mathbf k_j=\mathbf Q$ implies
\begin{equation}
\mathbf k_j = \mathbf Q - \mathbf k_i,
\qquad |\mathbf k_i|=|\mathbf k_j|=k_0,
\end{equation}
which is possible if and only if $\mathbf k_i$ lies on the intersection circle
\begin{equation}
|\mathbf k|=k_0
\quad \cap \quad
|\mathbf Q-\mathbf k|=k_0,
\end{equation}
a circle (for $|\mathbf Q|<2k_0$) of codimension $1$ on the sphere.

Hence, for fixed $\mathbf Q$, all $\mathbf k_i$ participating in pairs summing to $\mathbf Q$
must lie on this intersection circle, and the partner $\mathbf k_j$ is determined uniquely.

\begin{lemma}[Multiplicity bound for fixed $\mathbf Q$]
For any finite support set $K$ of size $N$ on the sphere, and any fixed $\mathbf Q\neq 0$,
\begin{equation}
M_K(\mathbf Q)\le N,
\end{equation}
with equality only if \emph{every} $\mathbf k_i\in K$ lies on the circle defined by $\mathbf Q$ and
$\mathbf Q-\mathbf k_i\in K$ for all $i$.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
For each choice of the first index $i$, the equation $\mathbf k_i+\mathbf k_j=\mathbf Q$ determines
$\mathbf k_j$ uniquely. Thus there is at most one $j$ for each $i$, hence at most $N$ ordered solutions.
\end{proof}

Combining with \eqref{eq:global_bound_Mmax} yields
\begin{equation}
\mathcal Q^{\rm fluc}(K,\mathbf a)\le N.
\label{eq:global_bound_N}
\end{equation}
This bound is extremely loose; to discriminate structures we need \emph{simultaneously large}
multiplicities for many $\mathbf Q$ channels, i.e.\ a high resonance \emph{density}.

\subsubsection{Resonance density functional and extremal candidates}

Define the resonance density
\begin{equation}
\mathscr R(K):=\sum_{\mathbf Q\in\mathcal P(K)} \left(\frac{M_K(\mathbf Q)}{N^2}\right)^2,
\end{equation}
which controls $\mathcal Q^{\rm fluc}$ under equal amplitudes:
\begin{equation}
\mathbf a=\frac{1}{\sqrt N}(1,\dots,1)
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\mathcal Q^{\rm fluc}(K,\mathbf a)=N^2\,\mathscr R(K).
\end{equation}

\begin{proposition}[Cubic stars maximize resonance density among small invariant sets]
Among the minimal finite support sets on the shell that close under $\pm$ and possess many distinct
pair-sum channels, the standard cubic stars are extremal candidates. In particular, BCC has the
largest nontrivial resonance-loop ratio $\mathcal C_S=N_{\rm loop}/N^2$ among cubic competitors.
\end{proposition}

\subsection{Status}

The above provides a rigorous global \emph{upper bound} and identifies the correct extremal mechanism:
maximizing resonance density across many $\mathbf Q$ channels.
To \emph{fully close} the non-cubic global maximization, one must solve a finite combinatorial geometry
problem on the sphere: classify finite sets $K$ on $S^2$ maximizing $\mathscr R(K)$ under the resonance
constraint. Within the TECT scope, we stop at the maximal universality class already proven
(Universality~I) plus the amplitude-optimization closure (Universality~J).

% ==============================
%  Universality K (final closure within "reasonable competitor class"):
%  competitor class = finite unions of cubic stars (multi-star superpositions)
%  Show: best competitor reduces to a single star; then BCC wins
% ==============================

\subsection{Closing the global problem within the multi-star competitor class}

We now define an explicit, physically standard competitor class on the $k_0$-shell:
finite unions of symmetry-related cubic stars (a.k.a.\ multi-star superpositions), which are precisely
the competitors generated by Landau expansions for cubic crystals and their harmonics.

\begin{definition}[Multi-star competitor class]
A configuration $K\subset S^2$ is a \emph{multi-star} if it can be written as a disjoint union
\begin{equation}
K=\bigsqcup_{\alpha=1}^m U_{S_\alpha}^{(g_\alpha)},
\end{equation}
where each $U_{S_\alpha}^{(g_\alpha)}$ is a rotated copy of one of the standard cubic stars
$U_{\rm SC},U_{\rm FCC},U_{\rm BCC}$ by some $g_\alpha\in SO(3)$, and the unions are disjoint on the shell.
\end{definition}

Let the field be supported on $K$ with amplitudes $a_{\alpha,i}$ on each star component:
\begin{equation}
\psi(\mathbf q)=\sum_{\alpha=1}^m \sum_{i=1}^{N_{S_\alpha}}
a_{\alpha,i}\,(2\pi)^3\delta(\mathbf q-\mathbf k_{\alpha,i}),
\qquad \sum_{\alpha,i} a_{\alpha,i}^2=1.
\end{equation}

\subsection{Lemma: cross-star resonance loops are generically absent}

\begin{lemma}[Generic decoupling of distinct rotated stars]
Let $U$ and $U'$ be two rotated cubic stars on the same shell, with $U'\neq U$.
Then for a generic relative rotation $R\in SO(3)$, there are no nontrivial mixed resonances of the form
\begin{equation}
\mathbf k+\mathbf k' + \mathbf p+\mathbf p'=\mathbf 0,
\qquad \mathbf k,\mathbf k'\in U,\ \mathbf p,\mathbf p'\in U',
\end{equation}
beyond the trivial $\pm$ pairings internal to each star.
Equivalently, the mixed-loop count vanishes:
\begin{equation}
N^{\rm mixed}_{\rm loop}(U,U')=0
\qquad\text{for a generic relative rotation.}
\end{equation}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The mixed resonance condition implies equality of pair-sums:
\begin{equation}
\mathbf k+\mathbf k' = -(\mathbf p+\mathbf p')=:\mathbf Q\neq 0.
\end{equation}
Thus $\mathbf Q$ must lie in the finite set of pair-sums of $U$ and simultaneously in that of $U'$.
For fixed $U$, the pair-sum set is finite; as $U'$ is rotated continuously, coincidence occurs only on a
finite union of lower-dimensional submanifolds of $SO(3)$ (measure zero). Hence generically there is no
coincidence and no mixed resonance.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Theorem: within the multi-star class, the maximizer collapses to a single star}

Let $\mathcal Q^{\rm fluc}$ denote the fluctuation functional (sum of squares of pair-fields).
Write $\psi=\sum_\alpha \psi_\alpha$ as a sum over star components.

\begin{theorem}[Single-star reduction in the multi-star class]
Assume the relative orientations of distinct star components are generic so that mixed resonances vanish.
Then
\begin{equation}
\mathcal Q^{\rm fluc}[\psi]
=
\sum_{\alpha=1}^m \mathcal Q^{\rm fluc}[\psi_\alpha].
\end{equation}
Under the normalization $\sum_\alpha \|\psi_\alpha\|_2^2=1$, the maximum of
$\mathcal Q^{\rm fluc}$ over the multi-star class is achieved by concentrating all norm into the single
component with the largest per-norm gain:
\begin{equation}
\max_{\psi\in \text{multi-star}}\mathcal Q^{\rm fluc}[\psi]
=
\max_{\alpha}\left(\max_{\psi_\alpha:\ \|\psi_\alpha\|_2^2=1}\mathcal Q^{\rm fluc}[\psi_\alpha]\right).
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
With vanishing mixed resonances, the square-sum representation contains only intra-star channels, so the
functional splits additively. Since each $\mathcal Q^{\rm fluc}[\psi_\alpha]$ is homogeneous of degree $4$
in $\psi_\alpha$, one has $\mathcal Q^{\rm fluc}[c\psi_\alpha]=c^4\mathcal Q^{\rm fluc}[\psi_\alpha]$.
With $\sum_\alpha c_\alpha^2=1$ (where $c_\alpha:=\|\psi_\alpha\|_2$), the sum
$\sum_\alpha c_\alpha^4 \mathcal Q^{\rm fluc}[\widehat\psi_\alpha]$ is maximized by putting all weight
on the largest coefficient (since $c^4$ is strictly convex), i.e.\ $c_{\alpha_*}=1$ and others $0$.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Corollary: BCC is globally optimal within the multi-star class}

By Universality~J, for each cubic star, the optimal intra-star amplitudes are equal.
Thus each star has a well-defined normalized gain proportional to $\mathcal C_S$.
Since
\begin{equation}
\mathcal C_{\rm BCC}>\mathcal C_{\rm FCC}>\mathcal C_{\rm SC},
\end{equation}
the single-star reduction implies the global maximizer in the multi-star class is the BCC star.

\subsection{Remark}

This closes the global variational step within the standard competitor class relevant to
cubic crystallization problems (finite unions of cubic stars).
Non-cubic competitors would require a separate spherical extremal classification problem.



% =========================================================
%  Supplement to Universality C:
%  What is rigorously true at higher loops, and what is not.
% =========================================================

\section*{Supplement to Universality C: Higher-loop factorization and its precise domain}

\subsection*{C.0. Notation and the actual claim}

Let $S$ label a candidate structure with star $U_S=\{\mathbf k_i\}_{i=1}^{N_S}$ on a single isotropic shell
$|\mathbf k|=k_0$. The equal-amplitude reduction restricts external momenta to the discrete set $\pm\mathbf k_i$.

At $l$ loops, the effective action coefficient at quartic order receives a finite sum of Feynman diagrams:
\begin{equation}
\Delta \beta^{(l)}_S
=
\sum_{D\in\mathfrak D_l} \mathcal A_D(S),
\end{equation}
where $\mathfrak D_l$ is the set of (connected) $l$-loop diagrams contributing to the 4-point function.

The strong (risk) claim is:
\begin{equation}
\forall l\ge 1,\quad
\Delta \beta^{(l)}_S \stackrel{?}{=} \Xi_l\,\mathcal P_l(C_S),
\qquad
C_S:=\frac{N_{{\rm loop},S}}{N_S^2},
\label{eq:strongC_claim}
\end{equation}
with $\Xi_l$ a structure-independent integral and $\mathcal P_l$ a polynomial.

\subsection*{C.1. Counterpoint: new invariants appear unless the vertex is ultra-local on the star}

The amplitude of a diagram $D$ at fixed external star legs can be written schematically as
\begin{equation}
\mathcal A_D(S)
=
\sum_{\{\text{internal star indices}\}}
\Big[\prod_{\text{vertices }v} W_v(\{\mathbf k\})\Big]\;
\Xi_D,
\label{eq:AD_general}
\end{equation}
where $\Xi_D$ is the loop-momentum integral (structure-independent if the propagator is isotropic)
and $W_v(\{\mathbf k\})$ is the discrete star evaluation of the vertex tensor at $v$.
At one loop with a constant local quartic coupling, $W_v$ is a Kronecker constraint enforcing
$\mathbf k_{i_1}+\mathbf k_{i_2}+\mathbf k_{i_3}+\mathbf k_{i_4}=0$, and the only nontrivial structure
dependence reduces to counting such quartets, i.e.\ $C_S$.

However, for $l\ge 2$, the summation in \eqref{eq:AD_general} involves multiple vertices and hence multiple
simultaneous resonance constraints. In general, the number of solutions depends not only on the \emph{single-vertex}
quartet count $N_{{\rm loop},S}$ but also on higher-order incidence data of the star, e.g.
\begin{equation}
I_{6}(S):=\#\{(i_1,\dots,i_6): \mathbf k_{i_1}+\cdots+\mathbf k_{i_6}=0\},
\qquad
I_{8}(S):=\#\{(i_1,\dots,i_8): \mathbf k_{i_1}+\cdots+\mathbf k_{i_8}=0\},
\end{equation}
or equivalently, multi-constraint intersections of the pair-sum sets $\Sigma(U_S)$.
Thus the unconditional claim \eqref{eq:strongC_claim} is \emph{not} generally valid without further hypotheses.

\subsection*{C.2. Precise theorem (what is rigorously true)}

\begin{definition}[Star-local constant-vertex truncation]
We say the theory is in the \emph{star-local constant-vertex truncation} if:
(i) the quadratic kernel is isotropic and depends only on $|\mathbf q|$ (shell propagator),
(ii) the quartic vertex is momentum-independent (a constant $u_0$) on the shell,
(iii) the effective action is truncated so that all higher-point vertices ($\psi^6,\psi^8,\dots$) are
either neglected or expressed as local functionals of $u_0$ with no additional star-dependent tensors.
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Higher-loop structure dependence is purely combinatorial in the constant-vertex class]
In the star-local constant-vertex truncation, each $l$-loop diagram amplitude factorizes as
\begin{equation}
\mathcal A_D(S)=\Xi_D\;\mathcal N_D(S),
\end{equation}
where $\Xi_D$ is a structure-independent isotropic loop integral and $\mathcal N_D(S)\in\mathbb N$ is a
\emph{pure counting number} of solutions of the discrete momentum-conservation constraints induced by the diagram
on the star $U_S$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{remark}[What replaces $\mathcal P_l(C_S)$]
The correct general statement at $l\ge 2$ is:
\begin{equation}
\Delta \beta^{(l)}_S
=
\sum_{D\in\mathfrak D_l}\Xi_D\;\mathcal N_D(S),
\end{equation}
and $\mathcal N_D(S)$ is, in general, a function of a \emph{finite set} of star invariants
\begin{equation}
\mathcal I(S)=\{I_4(S),I_6(S),I_8(S),\dots,I_{4+2l}(S)\},
\end{equation}
not only of $C_S=I_4(S)/N_S^2$.
Thus the strong polynomial reduction $\mathcal P_l(C_S)$ holds only if additional graph-theoretic identities
collapse all $\mathcal N_D(S)$ to functions of $I_4(S)$ alone, which need not be true for generic stars.
\end{remark}

\subsection*{C.3. Safe universality claim for the paper}

Therefore, the safe (and still strong) universality statement is:

\begin{quote}
\emph{Within the isotropic shell + constant local vertex truncation, all loop corrections factorize into
structure-independent integrals times discrete star-counting invariants. For the cubic competitors
(SC/FCC/BCC) these invariants preserve the BCC-preference and do not generate inversion within the
preemptive Brazovskii regime.}
\end{quote}

To prove non-inversion beyond one loop, it suffices to show that for the cubic stars the full set of relevant
counting invariants $\mathcal I(S)$ is ordered compatibly with $I_4(S)$ (or that their contributions are
subleading compared to the 1-loop hierarchy gap).

% =========================================================
%  Supplement to Universality C:
%  What is rigorously true at higher loops, and what is not.
% =========================================================

\section*{Supplement to Universality C: Higher-loop factorization and its precise domain}

\subsection*{C.0. Notation and the actual claim}

Let $S$ label a candidate structure with star $U_S=\{\mathbf k_i\}_{i=1}^{N_S}$ on a single isotropic shell
$|\mathbf k|=k_0$. The equal-amplitude reduction restricts external momenta to the discrete set $\pm\mathbf k_i$.

=
\sum_{D\in\mathfrak D_l} \mathcal A_D(S),
\end{equation}
where $\mathfrak D_l$ is the set of (connected) $l$-loop diagrams contributing to the 4-point function.

The strong (risk) claim is:
\begin{equation}
\forall l\ge 1,\quad

\qquad
C_S:=\frac{N_{{\rm loop},S}}{N_S^2},
\label{eq:strongC_claim}
\end{equation}

\qquad

\end{equation}
or equivalently, multi-constraint intersections of the pair-sum sets $\Sigma(U_S)$.
Thus the unconditional claim \eqref{eq:strongC_claim} is \emph{not} generally valid without further hypotheses.

\subsection*{C.2. Precise theorem (what is rigorously true)}

either neglected or expressed as local functionals of $u_0$ with no additional star-dependent tensors.
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Higher-loop structure dependence is purely combinatorial in the constant-vertex class]
In the star-local constant-vertex truncation, each $l$-loop diagram amplitude factorizes as
\begin{equation}
\mathcal A_D(S)=\Xi_D\;\mathcal N_D(S),
\end{equation}
where $\Xi_D$ is a structure-independent isotropic loop integral and $\mathcal N_D(S)\in\mathbb N$ is a
\emph{pure counting number} of solutions of the discrete momentum-conservation constraints induced by the diagram
on the star $U_S$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{remark}[What replaces $\mathcal P_l(C_S)$]
The correct general statement at $l\ge 2$ is:
\begin{equation}
\Delta \beta^{(l)}_S
=
\sum_{D\in\mathfrak D_l}\Xi_D\;\mathcal N_D(S),
\end{equation}
and $\mathcal N_D(S)$ is, in general, a function of a \emph{finite set} of star invariants
\begin{equation}
\mathcal I(S)=\{I_4(S),I_6(S),I_8(S),\dots,I_{4+2l}(S)\},
\end{equation}

Thus the strong polynomial reduction $\mathcal P_l(C_S)$ holds only if additional graph-theoretic identities

\end{remark}

\subsection*{C.3. Safe universality claim for the paper}

Therefore, the safe (and still strong) universality statement is:

\begin{quote}
\emph{Within the isotropic shell + constant local vertex truncation, all loop corrections factorize into
structure-independent integrals times discrete star-counting invariants. For the cubic competitors
(SC/FCC/BCC) these invariants preserve the BCC-preference and do not generate inversion within the
preemptive Brazovskii regime.}
\end{quote}
