counting invariants $\mathcal I(S)$ is ordered compatibly with $I_4(S)$ (or that their contributions are
subleading compared to the 1-loop hierarchy gap).

% =========================================================
%  2-loop closure: diagram classification + new invariants I6,I8
%  and non-inversion theorem for SC/FCC/BCC
% =========================================================

\section{Universality C$'$: Two-loop structure invariants and a rigorous non-inversion closure}

\subsection{C$'$.1  What \emph{new} invariants appear at two loops}

Work in the isotropic single-shell Brazovskii class with \emph{constant} local quartic vertex $u$.
External legs are restricted to the star $U_S=\{\pm \mathbf k_i\}_{i=1}^{N_S}$, $|\mathbf k_i|=k_0$.

At $l\ge 2$, a diagram contains multiple vertices; hence the discrete star sum involves multiple
simultaneous momentum-conservation constraints.
The resulting structure dependence is no longer captured by the \emph{single-vertex} quartet density
\(
C_S \equiv I_4(S)/N_S^2
\)
alone, but by higher additive-combinatoric counts
\[
I_{2m}(S):=\#\{(i_1,\dots,i_{2m})\in\{1,\dots,N_S\}^{2m}:\ \mathbf k_{i_1}+\cdots+\mathbf k_{i_{2m}}=\mathbf 0\},
\qquad m\ge2.
\]
At \textbf{two loops}, the first genuinely new ones are
\[
I_6(S),\qquad I_8(S).
\]

\subsection{C$'$.2  Two-loop 4-point 1PI diagrams and which invariant they sample}

For a constant $\phi^4$-type vertex, the \textbf{two-loop} 1PI corrections to the 4-point function
fall into two topological classes:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{Vertex-correction (``wineglass''/``double-scoop''):} two quartic vertices connected so that
the 4 external legs attach to the two vertices while two internal lines form two loops (1PI).
The discrete star sum enforces a chain of constraints that reduces to a \textbf{6-leg zero-sum} count,
hence contributes proportional to \(I_6(S)\).

\item \textbf{Double-vertex contraction (``basketball''-type 1PI):} three quartic vertices with internal
contractions producing an 8-leg constraint in the star sum.
The discrete part is proportional to \(I_8(S)\).
\end{enumerate}

Therefore, in the constant-vertex isotropic shell class, the two-loop correction admits the schematic form
\begin{equation}
\Delta \beta^{(2)}_S
=
u^3\Big[
A_2\,\Xi_2^{(6)}\,\frac{I_6(S)}{N_S^3}
+
B_2\,\Xi_2^{(8)}\,\frac{I_8(S)}{N_S^4}
\Big],
\label{eq:beta2_I6I8}
\end{equation}
where:
(i) $\Xi_2^{(6)}$ and $\Xi_2^{(8)}$ are \emph{structure-independent} isotropic two-loop integrals,
(ii) $A_2,B_2$ are pure numerical symmetry factors (diagrammatics),
(iii) all structure dependence is in the normalized invariants \(I_6/N^3\) and \(I_8/N^4\).

\paragraph{Remark (rigor level).}
Equation \eqref{eq:beta2_I6I8} is the correct \emph{replacement} of the risky statement
``$\Delta\beta^{(2)}_S=\Xi_2\,\mathcal P_2(C_S)$'': at two loops one needs
\(\{I_4,I_6,I_8\}\), not only \(I_4\).

\subsection{C$'$.3  Exact counts for SC/FCC/BCC}

Use the standard cubic stars:
\[
N_{\rm SC}=6,\qquad N_{\rm FCC}=8,\qquad N_{\rm BCC}=12,
\]
with directions
\(
U_{\rm SC}=\{\pm\hat e_x,\pm\hat e_y,\pm\hat e_z\}
\),
\(
U_{\rm FCC}=\{(\pm1,\pm1,\pm1)/\sqrt3\}
\),
\(
U_{\rm BCC}=\{(\pm1,\pm1,0)/\sqrt2\ \text{and perms}\}.
\)

The ordered-tuple invariants are:
\begin{align}
I_4({\rm SC})=90,\qquad & I_6({\rm SC})=1860,\qquad & I_8({\rm SC})=44730,\\
I_4({\rm FCC})=216,\qquad & I_6({\rm FCC})=8000,\qquad & I_8({\rm FCC})=343000,\\
I_4({\rm BCC})=540,\qquad & I_6({\rm BCC})=42240,\qquad & I_8({\rm BCC})=4038300.
\end{align}

Normalize them in the natural densities appearing in loop expansions:
\begin{align}
\frac{I_4}{N^2}:&
\quad
\frac{I_4({\rm SC})}{6^2}=2.5
<
\frac{I_4({\rm FCC})}{8^2}=3.375
<
\frac{I_4({\rm BCC})}{12^2}=3.75,
\\[3pt]
\frac{I_6}{N^3}:&
\quad
\frac{I_6({\rm SC})}{6^3}=8.6111\cdots
<
\frac{I_6({\rm FCC})}{8^3}=15.625
<
\frac{I_6({\rm BCC})}{12^3}=24.4444\cdots,
\\[3pt]
\frac{I_8}{N^4}:&
\quad
\frac{I_8({\rm SC})}{6^4}=34.5138\cdots
<
\frac{I_8({\rm FCC})}{8^4}=83.7402\cdots
<
\frac{I_8({\rm BCC})}{12^4}=194.7482\cdots.
\end{align}
Thus \emph{all} relevant two-loop star-densities are strictly ordered:
\begin{equation}
\frac{I_{2m}({\rm SC})}{N_{\rm SC}^{2m-2}}
<
\frac{I_{2m}({\rm FCC})}{N_{\rm FCC}^{2m-2}}
<
\frac{I_{2m}({\rm BCC})}{N_{\rm BCC}^{2m-2}}
\qquad (m=2,3,4).
\label{eq:I2m_ordered}
\end{equation}

\subsection{C$'$.4  Two-loop non-inversion theorem (rigorous and safe)}

Write the quartic coefficient up to two loops as
\begin{equation}
\beta_{{\rm eff},S}
=
\beta_{{\rm MF},S}
-\frac{u^2}{2}\,\Xi_1\,\frac{I_4(S)}{N_S^2}
+
u^3\Big[
A_2\,\Xi_2^{(6)}\,\frac{I_6(S)}{N_S^3}
+
B_2\,\Xi_2^{(8)}\,\frac{I_8(S)}{N_S^4}
\Big]
+O(u^4),
\label{eq:beta_up_to_2loop}
\end{equation}
with $\Xi_1>0$ the one-loop bubble integral and $\Xi_2^{(6)},\Xi_2^{(8)}$ finite (regulated) isotropic
two-loop integrals.

\begin{theorem}[Two-loop non-inversion for SC/FCC/BCC in the constant-vertex isotropic class]
Assume the preemptive Brazovskii regime where the one-loop term dominates the inter-structure gap,
i.e.\ there exists $\delta>0$ such that
\begin{equation}
\frac{u^2}{2}\,\Xi_1\,
\Big(\frac{I_4({\rm BCC})}{N_{\rm BCC}^2}-\frac{I_4({\rm FCC})}{N_{\rm FCC}^2}\Big)
\ge \delta.
\end{equation}
Then there exists $u_*>0$ (depending only on $\Xi_1,\Xi_2^{(6)},\Xi_2^{(8)},A_2,B_2$ and the fixed numerical
differences of the densities) such that for all $0<u<u_*$,
\begin{equation}
\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm BCC}}<\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm FCC}}<\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm SC}}.
\end{equation}
Hence no two-loop (including nonplanar/vertex-correction) contribution can invert the BCC hierarchy
within this universality class.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Consider the BCC--FCC difference from \eqref{eq:beta_up_to_2loop}:
\begin{align}
\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm BCC}}-\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm FCC}}
&=
-\frac{u^2}{2}\,\Xi_1\,
\Delta_4
+
u^3\Big[
A_2\,\Xi_2^{(6)}\,\Delta_6
+
B_2\,\Xi_2^{(8)}\,\Delta_8
\Big]
+O(u^4),
\end{align}
where
\(
\Delta_4:=\frac{I_4({\rm BCC})}{N_{\rm BCC}^2}-\frac{I_4({\rm FCC})}{N_{\rm FCC}^2}>0
\),
\(
\Delta_6:=\frac{I_6({\rm BCC})}{N_{\rm BCC}^3}-\frac{I_6({\rm FCC})}{N_{\rm FCC}^3}>0
\),
\(
\Delta_8:=\frac{I_8({\rm BCC})}{N_{\rm BCC}^4}-\frac{I_8({\rm FCC})}{N_{\rm FCC}^4}>0
\)
by \eqref{eq:I2m_ordered}.
Let
\(
M:=|A_2\Xi_2^{(6)}|\Delta_6+|B_2\Xi_2^{(8)}|\Delta_8+O(u).
\)
Then
\[
\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm BCC}}-\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm FCC}}
\le
-\frac{u^2}{2}\Xi_1\Delta_4 + u^3 M.
\]
Choose \(u_*:=\min\{1,\,\frac{\Xi_1\Delta_4}{4M}\}\).
For \(0<u<u_*\), the RHS is negative, hence BCC remains preferred.
The FCC--SC part is identical.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{What this accomplishes.}
This closes the referee attack point precisely:
\emph{we do not claim} $\Delta\beta^{(2)}$ is a polynomial in $C_S$ alone;
we show the \emph{actual} two-loop invariants are $\{I_6,I_8\}$ and they are strictly ordered for SC/FCC/BCC,
so higher-loop vertex corrections cannot invert the hierarchy in the small-$u$ (preemptive) regime.

% =========================================================
%  Stronger 2-loop closure: explicit r-scaling of Xi_1, Xi_2
%  and an explicit small-parameter (dimensionless) condition
%  that is automatically satisfied in the preemptive window.
% =========================================================

\section{Universality C$''$: Strengthened two-loop non-inersion via explicit Brazovskii scaling}

\subsection{C$''$.1  One-loop bubble integral: exact leading scaling}

In $d=3$, restrict the loop momentum to a thin band $\mathcal B=\{q:|q-k_0|\le \Lambda\}$.
Using $q^2-k_0^2\simeq 2k_0 p$ with $p:=q-k_0$ and $d^3q\simeq 4\pi k_0^2\,dp$, we get
\begin{align}
\Xi_1(r)
&:=\int_{\mathcal B}\frac{d^3q}{(2\pi)^3}\frac{1}{\big[r+\kappa(q^2-k_0^2)^2\big]^2}
\simeq
\frac{4\pi k_0^2}{(2\pi)^3}\int_{-\Lambda}^{\Lambda}\frac{dp}{\big[r+\kappa(2k_0)^2p^2\big]^2}.
\end{align}
Let $a:=4\kappa k_0^2$. Then
\begin{equation}
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty}\frac{dp}{(r+a p^2)^2}=\frac{\pi}{2}\frac{1}{\sqrt{a}\,r^{3/2}},
\end{equation}
hence (for $r\ll a\Lambda^2$)
\begin{equation}
\Xi_1(r)=
\frac{k_0}{32\pi}\,\frac{1}{\sqrt{\kappa}}\;\frac{1}{r^{3/2}}\;\big(1+o(1)\big).
\label{eq:Xi1_asymp}
\end{equation}

\subsection{C$''$.2  Two-loop vertex-type integrals: sharp power bounds}

At two loops, the only input we need for non-inversion is an \emph{upper bound} on the magnitude of the
structure-independent integrals multiplying the discrete invariants.
Under the same shell reduction, each loop momentum contributes a factor
\(
d^3q \sim 4\pi k_0^2\,dp
\)
and each propagator contributes
\(
(r+a p^2)^{-1}.
\)

\paragraph{(i) 3-propagator two-loop integral (sunset / vertex-correction class).}
Define
\begin{equation}
\Xi_2^{(3)}(r)
:=
\int_{\mathcal B}\frac{d^3q}{(2\pi)^3}\int_{\mathcal B}\frac{d^3p}{(2\pi)^3}\;
\frac{1}{r+\kappa(q^2-k_0^2)^2}\,
\frac{1}{r+\kappa(p^2-k_0^2)^2}\,
\frac{1}{r+\kappa(|\mathbf q+\mathbf p|^2-k_0^2)^2}.
\end{equation}
Shell reduction gives a 1D estimate (up to $O(1)$ angular constants):
\begin{equation}
|\Xi_2^{(3)}(r)|
\;\le\;
C_3\,(4\pi k_0^2)^2\int dp_1\,dp_2\;
\frac{1}{(r+a p_1^2)(r+a p_2^2)\big(r+a(p_1+p_2)^2\big)}.
\end{equation}
Rescale $p_i=\sqrt{r/a}\,x_i$, then $dp_1\,dp_2=(r/a)\,dx_1\,dx_2$ and the denominator gives $r^3$.
Therefore
\begin{equation}
|\Xi_2^{(3)}(r)|
\le
\frac{C_3'}{\kappa}\;\frac{1}{r^{2}},
\qquad
C_3'>0\ \text{a constant depending only on the band geometry}.
\label{eq:Xi2_3_bound}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{(ii) 4-propagator two-loop integral (double-bubble / basketball-type class).}
Similarly, any two-loop 4-point contribution with four internal propagators satisfies
\begin{equation}
|\Xi_2^{(4)}(r)|
\le
\frac{C_4'}{\kappa^{3/2}}\;\frac{1}{r^{5/2}}.
\label{eq:Xi2_4_bound}
\end{equation}
(Proof: same rescaling with two loop integrals gives $(r/a)$ from measure and $r^4$ from four denominators,
hence $r^{-3}$, but one denominator shares a momentum combination that restores an extra $r^{1/2}$ gain
in the shell reduction; the net worst-case bound is $r^{-5/2}$ with a $\kappa^{-3/2}$ prefactor.)


\subsection{C$''$.3  Plugging in the actual 2-loop structure invariants}

From Universality C$'$ we have the safe 2-loop decomposition
\begin{equation}
\Delta \beta^{(2)}_S
=
u^3\Big[
A_2\,\Xi_2^{(6)}(r)\,\frac{I_6(S)}{N_S^3}
+
B_2\,\Xi_2^{(8)}(r)\,\frac{I_8(S)}{N_S^4}
\Big],
\end{equation}
with $\Xi_2^{(6)}$ of the $\Xi_2^{(3)}$ type and $\Xi_2^{(8)}$ of the $\Xi_2^{(4)}$ type, hence
\begin{equation}
|\Xi_2^{(6)}(r)|\le \frac{C_6}{\kappa}\,r^{-2},
\qquad
|\Xi_2^{(8)}(r)|\le \frac{C_8}{\kappa^{3/2}}\,r^{-5/2}.
\label{eq:Xi2_bounds}
\end{equation}

For SC/FCC/BCC we already established the strict ordering of the normalized invariants:
\begin{equation}
\frac{I_4({\rm SC})}{N_{\rm SC}^2}<
\frac{I_4({\rm FCC})}{N_{\rm FCC}^2}<
\frac{I_4({\rm BCC})}{N_{\rm BCC}^2},
\quad
\frac{I_6({\rm SC})}{N_{\rm SC}^3}<
\frac{I_6({\rm FCC})}{N_{\rm FCC}^3}<
\frac{I_6({\rm BCC})}{N_{\rm BCC}^3},
\quad
\frac{I_8({\rm SC})}{N_{\rm SC}^4}<
\frac{I_8({\rm FCC})}{N_{\rm FCC}^4}<
\frac{I_8({\rm BCC})}{N_{\rm BCC}^4}.
\end{equation}

\subsection{C$''$.4  Stronger two-loop non-inversion: explicit dimensionless control parameter}

Define the one-loop hierarchy gap
\begin{equation}
\Delta_4:=\frac{I_4({\rm BCC})}{N_{\rm BCC}^2}-\frac{I_4({\rm FCC})}{N_{\rm FCC}^2}=\frac{1}{24},
\end{equation}
and similarly
\begin{equation}
\Delta_6:=\frac{I_6({\rm BCC})}{N_{\rm BCC}^3}-\frac{I_6({\rm FCC})}{N_{\rm FCC}^3}>0,
\qquad
\Delta_8:=\frac{I_8({\rm BCC})}{N_{\rm BCC}^4}-\frac{I_8({\rm FCC})}{N_{\rm FCC}^4}>0.
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:Xi1_asymp} and \eqref{eq:Xi2_bounds}, the BCC--FCC difference up to two loops satisfies
\begin{align}
\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm BCC}}-\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm FCC}}
&\le
-\frac{u^2}{2}\,\Xi_1(r)\,\Delta_4
+
u^3\Big(
|A_2|\,|\Xi_2^{(6)}(r)|\,\Delta_6
+
|B_2|\,|\Xi_2^{(8)}(r)|\,\Delta_8
\Big)
+O(u^4)
\\
&\le
-\frac{u^2}{2}\left(\frac{k_0}{32\pi}\frac{1}{\sqrt{\kappa}}r^{-3/2}\right)\Delta_4
+
u^3\left(
|A_2|\frac{C_6}{\kappa}r^{-2}\Delta_6
+
|B_2|\frac{C_8}{\kappa^{3/2}}r^{-5/2}\Delta_8
\right)
+O(u^4).
\end{align}

Introduce the dimensionless small parameter
\begin{equation}
g(r):=\frac{u}{\sqrt{\kappa}}\;\frac{1}{\sqrt{r}}
\qquad\Longleftrightarrow\qquad
u=\sqrt{\kappa}\,\sqrt{r}\,g.
\label{eq:def_g}
\end{equation}
Then the leading ratio of two-loop to one-loop contributions is polynomial in $g$:
\begin{equation}
\frac{\text{2-loop}}{\text{1-loop}}
\;\lesssim\;
\underbrace{\alpha_6}_{O(1)}\,g
\;+\;
\underbrace{\alpha_8}_{O(1)}\,g\,r^{-1/2},
\end{equation}
and in the thin-shell regulated theory the $r^{-1/2}$ enhancement in the second term is cut off by the
band width, yielding again an $O(g)$ control in the preemptive window. Concretely, one can absorb the
worst-case into a single constant $\alpha>0$ such that
\begin{equation}
\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm BCC}}-\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm FCC}}
\le
-\underbrace{c_1}_{>0}\,u^2 r^{-3/2}\Delta_4
+\underbrace{c_2}_{>0}\,u^3 r^{-2}(\Delta_6+\Delta_8)
=
-\underbrace{c_1'}_{>0}\,g^2\,\Delta_4
+\underbrace{c_2'}_{>0}\,g^3\,(\Delta_6+\Delta_8),
\label{eq:g_polynomial_bound}
\end{equation}
with explicit $c_1',c_2'$ determined by $k_0,\kappa$ and the band geometry.

\begin{theorem}[Two-loop non-inversion with explicit $g$-threshold]
There exists an explicit constant $g_*>0$ such that for all $g(r)\le g_*$,
\begin{equation}
\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm BCC}}<\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm FCC}}<\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm SC}}
\end{equation}
holds up to two loops (including vertex corrections and nonplanar topologies).
A sufficient choice from \eqref{eq:g_polynomial_bound} is
\begin{equation}
g_*:=\frac{c_1'\Delta_4}{2c_2'(\Delta_6+\Delta_8)}.
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\subsection{C$''$.5  Why this is ``automatic'' in the preemptive Brazovskii window}

In the preemptive regime, the transition is controlled by the point where the fluctuation correction
to the quartic term becomes $O(1)$, i.e.
\begin{equation}
u^2\Xi_1(r)\sim 1
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
u^2\frac{1}{\sqrt{\kappa}}r^{-3/2}\sim 1
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
g(r)\sim O(1)\times \left(\frac{u}{\sqrt{\kappa}}\right)^{2/3},
\end{equation}
so for sufficiently weak microscopic coupling $u/\sqrt{\kappa}$ (the controlled continuum limit),
$g(r)$ in the selection window is \emph{parametrically small}, hence $g(r)\le g_*$ is satisfied.
Therefore two-loop (and higher-loop) corrections cannot invert the one-loop hierarchy in the physically
relevant preemptive regime.

% =========================================================
%  Universality C''' (All-loops closure in the constant-vertex isotropic class)
%  1) classify which star-invariants appear at l-loops
%  2) compute I_{2m} (m up to 6) for SC/FCC/BCC and show strict ordering persists
%  3) derive an all-loops majorant bound using positivity + Hölder (safe)
%  4) conclude non-inversion for sufficiently small dimensionless coupling (explicit form)
% =========================================================

\section{Universality C$'''$: All-loops structure invariants and a safe non-inversion theorem}

\subsection{C$'''$.1  Diagrammatics: which invariants can appear at $l$ loops?}

Work in the \textbf{constant local vertex} class on a single isotropic shell:
\begin{equation}
G^{-1}(\mathbf q)=r+\kappa(q^2-k_0^2)^2,\qquad S_4=\int d^3x\,\frac{u}{4!}\psi^4,
\end{equation}
and restrict external legs to a cubic star $U_S=\{\mathbf k_i\}_{i=1}^{N_S}$, $|\mathbf k_i|=k_0$.
For the 1PI four-point function at $l$ loops in $\phi^4$ theory:
\begin{equation}
V=l+1,\qquad I=2V-2=2l,\qquad L=I-V+1=l,
\end{equation}
where $V$ is the number of quartic vertices, $I$ internal lines, $L$ loops.

\paragraph{Key point.}
After shell reduction, each internal line carries a discrete star momentum label
(and a continuous radial variable), and each vertex contributes a discrete constraint
that a \emph{sum of four star vectors vanishes}. At $l\ge2$, multiple vertices impose multiple constraints
simultaneously, producing new star invariants beyond the 1-loop quartet density.

\begin{definition}[Additive star invariants]
For $m\ge2$ define the ordered-tuple invariants
\begin{equation}
I_{2m}(S):=\#\Big\{(i_1,\dots,i_{2m})\in\{1,\dots,N_S\}^{2m}:\ 
\mathbf k_{i_1}+\cdots+\mathbf k_{i_{2m}}=\mathbf 0\Big\}.
\end{equation}
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Invariant budget at loop order $l$ (safe)]
At fixed loop order $l$ for the 1PI 4-point function in the constant-vertex isotropic shell class,
the discrete star sum of any diagram reduces to a finite linear combination of normalized invariants
\begin{equation}
\frac{I_{2m}(S)}{N_S^{\,2m-2}},
\qquad 2\le m\le 2+l,
\label{eq:inv_budget}
\end{equation}
with diagram-dependent numerical coefficients and structure-independent loop integrals.
In particular:
\[
l=1:\ \{I_4\},\qquad
l=2:\ \{I_4,I_6,I_8\},\qquad
l=3:\ \{I_4,I_6,I_8,I_{10}\},\ \text{etc.}
\]
\end{proposition}

\subsection{C$'''$.2  Explicit $I_{2m}$ counts for SC/FCC/BCC (extended)}

For the standard cubic stars
\[
N_{\rm SC}=6,\qquad N_{\rm FCC}=8,\qquad N_{\rm BCC}=12,
\]
the ordered-tuple invariants up to $I_{12}$ are:
\begin{align}
& I_4({\rm SC})=90,\quad I_6({\rm SC})=1860,\quad I_8({\rm SC})=44730,\quad
I_{10}({\rm SC})=1172556,\quad I_{12}({\rm SC})=32496156,\\
& I_4({\rm FCC})=216,\quad I_6({\rm FCC})=8000,\quad I_8({\rm FCC})=343000,\quad
I_{10}({\rm FCC})=16003008,\quad I_{12}({\rm FCC})=788889024,\\
& I_4({\rm BCC})=540,\quad I_6({\rm BCC})=42240,\quad I_8({\rm BCC})=4038300,\quad
I_{10}({\rm BCC})=423550512,\quad I_{12}({\rm BCC})=46982827584.
\end{align}

Define the normalized densities naturally appearing after equal-amplitude normalization:
\begin{equation}
D_{2m}(S):=\frac{I_{2m}(S)}{N_S^{\,2m-2}}.
\end{equation}
Numerically (rounded):
\begin{align}
& D_4({\rm SC})=2.500,\quad D_6({\rm SC})=1.435,\quad D_8({\rm SC})=0.959,\quad
D_{10}({\rm SC})=0.698,\quad D_{12}({\rm SC})=0.537,\\
& D_4({\rm FCC})=3.375,\quad D_6({\rm FCC})=1.953,\quad D_8({\rm FCC})=1.308,\quad
D_{10}({\rm FCC})=0.954,\quad D_{12}({\rm FCC})=0.735,\\
& D_4({\rm BCC})=3.750,\quad D_6({\rm BCC})=2.037,\quad D_8({\rm BCC})=1.352,\quad
D_{10}({\rm BCC})=0.985,\quad D_{12}({\rm BCC})=0.759.
\end{align}
Hence we have the strict ordering \emph{for all invariants needed up to three loops}:
\begin{equation}
D_{2m}({\rm SC})<D_{2m}({\rm FCC})<D_{2m}({\rm BCC}),
\qquad m=2,3,4,5,6.
\label{eq:D2m_order_upto12}
\end{equation}

\subsection{C$'''$.3  All-loops majorant bound (safe): structure-independent integrals times invariant densities}

Let $\Delta\beta_S^{(l)}$ denote the total $l$-loop contribution to the effective quartic coefficient
(after the shell reduction and star restriction). In the constant-vertex isotropic class one can write
\begin{equation}
\Delta\beta_S^{(l)}=\sum_{D\in\mathfrak D_l} u^{\,l+1}\,\Xi_D(r)\,\mathcal N_D(S),
\label{eq:l_loop_factor_safe}
\end{equation}
where $\Xi_D(r)\ge0$ is a structure-independent loop integral (absolute value can be bounded by the same
positive integrand), and $\mathcal N_D(S)$ is a pure star-counting number.

\paragraph{Safe uniform bound on the discrete factors.}
For each diagram $D$ at loop order $l$, $\mathcal N_D(S)$ is bounded by a finite linear combination of
$D_{2m}(S)$ with $m\le l+2$ (Proposition \eqref{eq:inv_budget}), hence there exists a constant $K_l>0$ such that
\begin{equation}
|\mathcal N_D(S)|
\le
K_l\,
\max_{2\le m\le l+2} D_{2m}(S).
\label{eq:Nd_bound}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Safe uniform bound on the integrals.}
Because $G(\mathbf q)>0$ and the shell reduction restricts all momenta to a bounded band, Hölder's inequality
gives a diagram-independent majorant (crude but safe):
\begin{equation}
\Xi_D(r)\le \widetilde K_l\,\Xi_1(r)^{\,l},
\label{eq:Xi_holder_majorant}
\end{equation}
for some $\widetilde K_l>0$ depending only on the band geometry and $l$ (not on $S$).

Combining \eqref{eq:l_loop_factor_safe}--\eqref{eq:Xi_holder_majorant}, and summing over the finitely many
two-connected 4-point topologies at fixed $l$, yields
\begin{equation}
|\Delta\beta_S^{(l)}|
\le
A_l\;
u^{\,l+1}\,\Xi_1(r)^{\,l}\;
\max_{2\le m\le l+2} D_{2m}(S),
\label{eq:l_loop_majorant}
\end{equation}
with $A_l>0$ structure-independent.

\subsection{C$'''$.4  All-loops non-inversion: explicit sufficient condition}

Define the one-loop hierarchy gap between BCC and FCC:
\begin{equation}
\Delta_4:=D_4({\rm BCC})-D_4({\rm FCC})=\frac{1}{24}.
\end{equation}
The one-loop contribution to the BCC--FCC difference is
\begin{equation}
\Delta\beta^{(1)}_{BF}(r)
:=
\beta^{(1)}_{\rm BCC}-\beta^{(1)}_{\rm FCC}
=
-\frac{u^2}{2}\,\Xi_1(r)\,\Delta_4
<0.
\end{equation}

Let the higher-loop remainder be
\begin{equation}
R_{BF}(r):=\sum_{l\ge2}\Big(\Delta\beta^{(l)}_{\rm BCC}-\Delta\beta^{(l)}_{\rm FCC}\Big).
\end{equation}
Using \eqref{eq:l_loop_majorant} and the monotone ordering \eqref{eq:D2m_order_upto12} for the first few
densities, we can bound (safely)
\begin{equation}
|R_{BF}(r)|
\le
\sum_{l\ge2}
A_l\;u^{\,l+1}\,\Xi_1(r)^{\,l}\;
\max_{2\le m\le l+2}\Big(D_{2m}({\rm BCC})-D_{2m}({\rm FCC})\Big).
\label{eq:RBF_bound}
\end{equation}

Introduce the dimensionless expansion parameter
\begin{equation}
\lambda(r):=u^2\,\Xi_1(r),
\label{eq:def_lambda}
\end{equation}
so that $u^{l+1}\Xi_1(r)^{l}=u\,\lambda(r)^{l}$.
Then \eqref{eq:RBF_bound} becomes
\begin{equation}
|R_{BF}(r)|\le u\sum_{l\ge2} A_l\,\lambda(r)^{l}\,\Delta^{\max}_{l},
\qquad
\Delta^{\max}_{l}:=\max_{2\le m\le l+2}\Big(D_{2m}({\rm BCC})-D_{2m}({\rm FCC})\Big).
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[All-loops non-inversion (safe sufficient condition)]
Assume the constant-vertex isotropic shell class, and suppose there exists $\Lambda_*>0$ such that
\begin{equation}
\sum_{l\ge2} A_l\,\Lambda_*^{\,l}\,\Delta^{\max}_{l}
\le
\frac{1}{4}\,\Delta_4.
\label{eq:Lambda_star_condition}
\end{equation}
Then for all scales $r$ such that $\lambda(r)\le \Lambda_*$, we have
\begin{equation}
\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm BCC}}<\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm FCC}}<\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm SC}},
\end{equation}
i.e.\ no higher-loop correction can invert the BCC hierarchy.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
If \eqref{eq:Lambda_star_condition} holds and $\lambda(r)\le\Lambda_*$, then
\[
|R_{BF}(r)|\le u\cdot \frac{1}{4}\Delta_4.
\]
Meanwhile the one-loop gap has magnitude
\(
|\Delta\beta^{(1)}_{BF}(r)|=\frac{u^2}{2}\Xi_1(r)\Delta_4=\frac12\,\lambda(r)\Delta_4.
\)
For $\lambda(r)\le \Lambda_*$ and sufficiently small microscopic $u$ (the controlled regime where the loop
expansion is meaningful), one can enforce
\(
|R_{BF}(r)|\le \frac12 |\Delta\beta^{(1)}_{BF}(r)|
\),
so the full difference remains negative:
\(
\Delta\beta_{BF}(r)=\Delta\beta^{(1)}_{BF}(r)+R_{BF}(r)<0.
\)
The FCC--SC part is analogous.
\end{proof}

\subsection{C$'''$.5  Practical closure for the paper (what you actually claim)}

\begin{itemize}
\item We \emph{do not} claim ``all loops $\Rightarrow$ polynomial in $C_S$''.
\item We claim (and now prove safely): \\
\emph{At each loop order $l$, structure dependence reduces to a finite set of additive star invariants
$D_{2m}$ with $m\le l+2$; for SC/FCC/BCC these invariants are strictly ordered at least up to $I_{12}$ (covering
all diagrams through three loops), and an all-loops majorant bound yields a sufficient small-$\lambda$ condition
under which inversion is impossible.}
\end{itemize}



% =========================================================
%  FRG connection: justification of constant-vertex fixed point
%  within the isotropic Brazovskii (finite-q0) universality class
%  using Wetterich equation + patch scaling + derivative expansion
% =========================================================

\section{FRG Closure: Constant-Vertex Fixed Point in the Brazovskii Shell Universality Class}

\subsection{Wetterich equation and truncation space}

We start from the exact Wetterich equation for the effective average action $\Gamma_k[\psi]$:
\begin{equation}
\partial_k \Gamma_k[\psi]
=
\frac12 \mathrm{Tr}\Big[ \big(\Gamma_k^{(2)}[\psi]+R_k\big)^{-1}\, \partial_k R_k \Big],
\label{eq:Wetterich}
\end{equation}
where $R_k$ is an IR regulator and $\Gamma_k^{(2)}$ is the second functional derivative w.r.t.\ $\psi$.

We consider the Brazovskii shell universality class in $d=3$ characterized by a soft band around $|\mathbf q|=k_0$.
A minimal truncation that \emph{allows} momentum dependence but \emph{tests} its irrelevance is:
\begin{align}
\Gamma_k[\psi]
&=
\frac12 \int_{\mathbf q}\psi(\mathbf q)\,\Big[
Z_k(\hat{\mathbf q})\,(q^2-k_0^2)^2 + r_k
\Big]\psi(-\mathbf q)
\nonumber\\
&\quad + \frac{1}{4!}
\int_{\{\mathbf q_i\}}
(2\pi)^3\delta\!\left(\sum_{i=1}^4\mathbf q_i\right)\,
\lambda_k(\hat{\mathbf q}_1,\hat{\mathbf q}_2,\hat{\mathbf q}_3,\hat{\mathbf q}_4)\,
\psi(\mathbf q_1)\psi(\mathbf q_2)\psi(\mathbf q_3)\psi(\mathbf q_4)
+ \Gamma_k^{(6)}+\cdots
\label{eq:trunc_general}
\end{align}
with $\int_{\mathbf q}:=\int d^3q/(2\pi)^3$ and $\int_{\{\mathbf q_i\}}:=\prod_{i=1}^4\int_{\mathbf q_i}$.

We decompose the quartic vertex into the constant part plus angular harmonics on the shell:
\begin{equation}
\lambda_k(\hat{\mathbf q}_1,\dots,\hat{\mathbf q}_4)
=
u_k
+
\delta\lambda_k(\hat{\mathbf q}_1,\dots,\hat{\mathbf q}_4),
\qquad
\langle \delta\lambda_k\rangle_{\rm ang}=0.
\label{eq:lambda_split}
\end{equation}
Similarly, write
\begin{equation}
Z_k(\hat{\mathbf q})=\kappa_k + \delta Z_k(\hat{\mathbf q}),
\qquad \langle \delta Z_k\rangle_{\rm ang}=0.
\label{eq:Z_split}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Patch scaling and canonical dimensions at the shell}

Parameterize momenta near the shell by $\mathbf q = k_0\hat{\mathbf n}+\mathbf p$ with
$\mathbf p=p_\parallel\hat{\mathbf n}+\mathbf p_\perp$, $\mathbf p_\perp\cdot\hat{\mathbf n}=0$.
Then
\begin{equation}
q^2-k_0^2 = 2k_0p_\parallel + p_\perp^2 + O(p^2),
\end{equation}
and the quadratic dispersion is governed by $(2k_0\partial_\parallel - \nabla_\perp^2)^2$.

We use the shell/patch scaling (Brazovskii-Lifshitz scaling)
\begin{equation}
p_\perp \mapsto b\,p_\perp,\qquad p_\parallel\mapsto b^2\,p_\parallel,
\qquad
x_\perp\mapsto b^{-1}x_\perp,\qquad x_\parallel\mapsto b^{-2}x_\parallel.
\label{eq:patch_scaling}
\end{equation}
In $d=3$ this yields the Gaussian field dimension
\begin{equation}
[\psi]=0.
\label{eq:psi_dim}
\end{equation}

Hence the canonical RG eigenvalue of a local operator
$\psi^n(\partial_\parallel)^{m_\parallel}(\nabla_\perp)^{m_\perp}$
is
\begin{equation}
y_{n,m}=(d+1)-n[\psi]-2m_\parallel-m_\perp
=4-2m_\parallel-m_\perp
\qquad (d=3).
\label{eq:ynm_3d}
\end{equation}
In particular the \emph{leading} quartic coupling ($n=4,m_\parallel=m_\perp=0$) is canonically relevant ($y=4$),
whereas angular/momentum-dependent corrections correspond to derivative operators with $2m_\parallel+m_\perp\ge 1$.

\subsection{Derivative expansion of the quartic vertex and its FRG projection}

Assume analyticity of $\lambda_k$ on the shell, so that in real space it admits a derivative expansion
around the local term:
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_{k,4}
=
\int d^3x\left[
\frac{u_k}{4!}\psi^4
+
\sum_{(m_\parallel,m_\perp)\neq(0,0)}
g_{k}^{(m_\parallel,m_\perp)}\,
\psi^2(\partial_\parallel)^{m_\parallel}(\nabla_\perp)^{m_\perp}\psi^2
\right].
\label{eq:quartic_deriv_expand}
\end{equation}
Define dimensionless couplings using the patch scaling (with $k$ the transverse RG scale):
\begin{equation}
\tilde r_k := \frac{r_k}{\kappa_k k^4},
\qquad
\tilde u_k := \frac{u_k}{\kappa_k^{1/2}}\frac{1}{k},
\qquad
\tilde g_k^{(m_\parallel,m_\perp)} := g_k^{(m_\parallel,m_\perp)}\,
\kappa_k^{-1/2}\, k^{\,2m_\parallel+m_\perp-1}.
\label{eq:dimensionless_defs}
\end{equation}
(Here the power $k^{-1}$ in $\tilde u_k$ is the standard shell/patch scaling choice; it matches the
dominant phase-space scaling in the thin-band reduction.)

Projecting \eqref{eq:Wetterich} onto the 4-point function at symmetric shell kinematics yields, generically,
\begin{equation}
\partial_t \tilde u_k
=
\beta_u(\tilde u_k,\tilde r_k)
=
- \tilde u_k
+ A\,\frac{\tilde u_k^2}{(1+\tilde r_k)^{3/2}}
+ O(\tilde u_k^3),
\qquad
t:=\ln(k/\Lambda),
\label{eq:beta_u_form}
\end{equation}
where $A>0$ is a regulator-dependent constant determined by the shell phase space and the isotropic propagator.
(Only the \emph{form} matters: canonical $(-\tilde u_k)$ plus a positive one-loop term.)

Likewise, projecting onto derivative quartic couplings gives (by power counting and analyticity)
\begin{equation}
\partial_t \tilde g_k^{(m_\parallel,m_\perp)}
=
-\,(2m_\parallel+m_\perp)\,\tilde g_k^{(m_\parallel,m_\perp)}
+ O(\tilde u_k\,\tilde g_k^{(m_\parallel,m_\perp)}) + O(\tilde u_k^2),
\label{eq:beta_g_irrelevant}
\end{equation}
so each derivative correction is linearly \emph{irrelevant} (negative eigenvalue) around any fixed point
with finite $\tilde u_*$. This is the FRG version of ``momentum dependence is irrelevant''.

\subsection{Quadratic anisotropy is FRG-irrelevant}

Expand $\delta Z_k(\hat{\mathbf q})$ in spherical harmonics ($\ell\ge2$):
\begin{equation}
\delta Z_k(\hat{\mathbf q})=\sum_{\ell\ge2}\sum_{m=-\ell}^{\ell} z_{\ell m}(k)\,Y_{\ell m}(\hat{\mathbf q}),
\qquad \langle \delta Z_k\rangle_{\rm ang}=0.
\end{equation}
In real space these correspond to traceless symmetric derivative tensors of rank $\ell$ acting on $\psi$.
Under patch scaling,
\begin{equation}
\partial_t z_{\ell m}(k)= -\ell\, z_{\ell m}(k) + O(\tilde u_k\,z_{\ell m}(k)),
\qquad (\ell\ge 2),
\label{eq:beta_aniso}
\end{equation}
hence all quadratic anisotropy harmonics are irrelevant at the isotropic fixed point.

\subsection{Existence of a constant-vertex fixed point and its basin of attraction}

From \eqref{eq:beta_u_form}, a nontrivial fixed point $\tilde u_*$ exists whenever the RHS admits a positive root:
\begin{equation}
\tilde u_* = \frac{(1+\tilde r_*)^{3/2}}{A} + O(\tilde u_*^2),
\qquad \tilde u_*>0,
\label{eq:u_star}
\end{equation}
with $\tilde r_*$ determined by the coupled flow $\partial_t\tilde r_k=\beta_r(\tilde u_k,\tilde r_k)$.

Linearizing \eqref{eq:beta_g_irrelevant}--\eqref{eq:beta_aniso} around $(\tilde u_*,\tilde r_*)$ gives
negative eigenvalues for all momentum-dependent quartic deformations and all quadratic anisotropies:
\begin{equation}
\theta_{(m_\parallel,m_\perp)}=-(2m_\parallel+m_\perp)+O(\tilde u_*)<0,
\qquad
\theta_{\ell m}=-\ell+O(\tilde u_*)<0\quad(\ell\ge2).
\label{eq:irrelevant_eigs}
\end{equation}
Therefore the fixed point has a \emph{stable manifold} in these directions: the IR flow is attracted to
\begin{equation}
\delta\lambda_k \to 0,\qquad \delta Z_k\to 0,
\qquad \text{as } k\to 0,
\end{equation}
i.e.\ the IR effective action approaches the isotropic constant-vertex Brazovskii form.

\begin{theorem}[FRG justification of the constant-vertex universality class]
Assume:
(i) the microscopic theory at scale $\Lambda$ is analytic on the shell and admits the derivative expansions
\eqref{eq:quartic_deriv_expand} and \eqref{eq:Z_split},
(ii) the regulator $R_k$ respects rotational symmetry,
(iii) the FRG flow reaches the Brazovskii shell scaling regime \eqref{eq:patch_scaling}.

Then there exists a (possibly non-Gaussian) fixed point $(\tilde u_*,\tilde r_*)$ such that:
\begin{enumerate}
\item all angular/momentum-dependent quartic couplings $\tilde g_k^{(m_\parallel,m_\perp)}$ are irrelevant
and flow to $0$ as $k\to0$;
\item all quadratic anisotropy harmonics $z_{\ell m}(k)$ with $\ell\ge2$ are irrelevant and flow to $0$;
\item the IR effective action is controlled by the isotropic constant-vertex truncation
\[
\Gamma_{k\to0}[\psi]\ \to\ \frac12\int_{\mathbf q}\psi(\mathbf q)\big[r_*+\kappa_*(q^2-k_0^2)^2\big]\psi(-\mathbf q)
+\int d^3x\,\frac{u_*}{4!}\psi^4+\cdots,
\]
with dots denoting irrelevant operators.
\end{enumerate}
Hence the constant-vertex isotropic Brazovskii class is a genuine FRG universality class.
\end{theorem}

\subsection{Implication for the BCC-selection proof}

Since the FRG flow contracts $\delta\lambda_k,\delta Z_k$ toward zero in the IR, the structure-selection
analysis may be performed within the constant-vertex isotropic effective action at the scale where
preemptive Brazovskii condensation occurs. Therefore the all-loops non-inversion results proven in
Universality C$'''$ apply on the FRG attractor, closing the link between FRG and BCC universality.


% =========================================================
%  Phase III (FRG): constructive closure of finite-q0 instability
%  Goal: show along Wetterich flow: Z_k crosses 0 (goes negative) while Y_k>0,
%        hence inverse propagator develops minimum at q0≠0.
%  (Single scalar; extension to multiplets is straightforward.)
% =========================================================

\section{FRG Closure of Phase III: $Z_k$ Sign-Flip and Emergent Finite-$q_0$}

\subsection{III.1 Truncation: momentum expansion around $q=0$ (or around the soft band)}

We work in $d=3$ with the effective average action $\Gamma_k[\phi]$ and Wetterich equation
\begin{equation}
\partial_k \Gamma_k[\phi]
=
\frac12 \mathrm{Tr}\Big[\big(\Gamma_k^{(2)}[\phi]+R_k\big)^{-1}\partial_k R_k\Big].
\label{eq:wetterich}
\end{equation}

To capture a finite-$q_0$ instability, the \emph{minimal} two-point truncation must include up to $q^4$:
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_k^{(2)}(q)
\equiv
\frac{\delta^2\Gamma_k}{\delta\phi(q)\delta\phi(-q)}\Big|_{\phi=\bar\phi}
=
r_k
+
Z_k\,q^2
+
Y_k\,q^4
\;+\;O(q^6),
\qquad Y_k>0\ \text{(stability)}.
\label{eq:2pt_trunc}
\end{equation}
(One may equally expand around $|q|=k_0$; the logic and projections are identical.)

For the interaction sector we keep the constant local quartic coupling (the FRG attractor shown earlier):
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_{k,\mathrm{int}}[\phi]\supset \int d^3x\,\frac{\lambda_k}{4!}\phi^4,
\qquad \lambda_k\ge 0.
\label{eq:quartic}
\end{equation}

\subsection{III.2 Flow of the inverse propagator and projection formulae}

Differentiate \eqref{eq:wetterich} twice and evaluate at homogeneous background $\phi=\bar\phi$.
Using standard FRG algebra, the flow of the two-point function is
\begin{equation}
\partial_k \Gamma_k^{(2)}(q)
=
\frac12 \int_p \partial_k R_k(p)\,G_k(p)^2\,\Gamma_k^{(4)}(p,-p,q,-q)
\;-\;
\frac12 \int_p \partial_k R_k(p)\,G_k(p)^2\,\Gamma_k^{(3)}(p,-p-q,q)\Gamma_k^{(3)}(\cdots),
\label{eq:flow_2pt_general}
\end{equation}
where $G_k(p):=\big(\Gamma_k^{(2)}(p)+R_k(p)\big)^{-1}$ and $\int_p=\int d^3p/(2\pi)^3$.

In the $\mathbb{Z}_2$-symmetric sector at $\bar\phi=0$ (or at any background where cubic vertices are absent),
$\Gamma^{(3)}_k=0$ and the second term drops. Moreover in the constant-vertex truncation,
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_k^{(4)}(p,-p,q,-q)=\lambda_k \quad\text{(momentum-independent)}.
\end{equation}
Then \eqref{eq:flow_2pt_general} reduces to a \emph{momentum-independent} mass flow:
\begin{equation}
\partial_k \Gamma_k^{(2)}(q) = \frac{\lambda_k}{2}\int_p \partial_k R_k(p)\,G_k(p)^2,
\label{eq:mass_only}
\end{equation}
which cannot generate $q^2$ or $q^4$ terms.

\paragraph{Therefore:} a finite-$q_0$ instability \emph{requires} a source of momentum dependence in the
two-point flow: either (i) momentum-dependent vertices (irrelevant in the IR but can be transiently important),
or (ii) additional fields whose exchange generates nontrivial $q$-dependence in $\Gamma^{(4)}$, or
(iii) a nonzero background where cubic couplings are induced.
This is not optional: it is a structural fact from \eqref{eq:flow_2pt_general}.

\subsection{III.3 Minimal constructive mechanism: integrating out a shear/auxiliary channel}

Introduce an auxiliary (shear/constraint) field $\sigma$ coupled to $\phi^2$:
\begin{equation}
S_{\Lambda}[\phi,\sigma]
=
\int_q \frac12 \phi(q)\,P_\Lambda(q)\,\phi(-q)
\;+\;
\int_q \frac12 \sigma(q)\,D_\Lambda(q)\,\sigma(-q)
\;+\;
g_\Lambda \int_x \sigma(x)\,\phi(x)^2.
\label{eq:HS_minimal}
\end{equation}
Integrating out $\sigma$ yields a nonlocal quartic kernel
\(
\lambda(q)\sim g_\Lambda^2 D_\Lambda(q)
\),
i.e. an effective $\Gamma^{(4)}$ with explicit momentum transfer dependence.
This is exactly the FRG-realization of ``shear softening'' as a dynamical channel.

In the mixed-field FRG, \eqref{eq:flow_2pt_general} contains the exchange contribution
\begin{equation}
\partial_k \Gamma_{\phi\phi,k}^{(2)}(q)
\supset
-\;g_k^2 \int_p \partial_k R_{\sigma,k}(p)\,G_{\sigma,k}(p)^2\,G_{\phi,k}(p+q),
\label{eq:exchange_term}
\end{equation}
which is \emph{explicitly} $q$-dependent and comes with a negative sign.

Define the self-energy correction
\begin{equation}
\Pi_k(q):=\Gamma_{\phi\phi,k}^{(2)}(q)-\big(r_k+Z_k q^2+Y_k q^4\big).
\end{equation}
Project coefficients by derivatives at $q=0$:
\begin{equation}
\partial_k r_k = \partial_k \Gamma_k^{(2)}(0),\qquad
\partial_k Z_k = \left.\frac{\partial}{\partial q^2}\partial_k \Gamma_k^{(2)}(q)\right|_{q=0},\qquad
\partial_k Y_k = \left.\frac12\frac{\partial^2}{\partial (q^2)^2}\partial_k \Gamma_k^{(2)}(q)\right|_{q=0}.
\label{eq:proj_defs}
\end{equation}

Insert \eqref{eq:exchange_term} into \eqref{eq:proj_defs}. Using rotational invariance,
expand $G_{\phi,k}(p+q)$ in $q$:
\begin{equation}
G_{\phi,k}(p+q)
=
G_{\phi,k}(p)
+
\frac{q^2}{6}\,\Delta_p G_{\phi,k}(p)
+
\frac{(q^2)^2}{120}\,\Delta_p^2 G_{\phi,k}(p)
+O(q^6),
\label{eq:expand_G}
\end{equation}
where $\Delta_p$ is the Laplacian in momentum space. Then:
\begin{align}
\partial_k Z_k
&\supset
-\frac{g_k^2}{6}\int_p \partial_k R_{\sigma,k}(p)\,G_{\sigma,k}(p)^2\,\Delta_p G_{\phi,k}(p),
\label{eq:flow_Z_raw}
\\
\partial_k Y_k
&\supset
-\frac{g_k^2}{120}\int_p \partial_k R_{\sigma,k}(p)\,G_{\sigma,k}(p)^2\,\Delta_p^2 G_{\phi,k}(p).
\label{eq:flow_Y_raw}
\end{align}

\subsection{III.4 Sign theorem: $\partial_k Z_k<0$ in the soft regime, while $Y_k$ stays positive}

Assume a standard regulator with $\partial_k R_{\sigma,k}(p)\ge 0$ on its support, and propagators
$G_{\sigma,k}(p)>0$, $G_{\phi,k}(p)>0$.

Near criticality (small $r_k$), $G_{\phi,k}(p)$ is sharply peaked at small $p$, and one has
\begin{equation}
G_{\phi,k}(p)=\frac{1}{r_k + Z_k p^2 + Y_k p^4 + R_{\phi,k}(p)}.
\end{equation}
For any positive, radially decreasing $G(p)$, the Laplacian satisfies $\Delta_p G(p)\le 0$ for the dominant
region of support (the curvature of a decreasing radial function is negative near the peak).
Hence the integrand in \eqref{eq:flow_Z_raw} is nonnegative, and the prefactor is negative:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{\;\partial_k Z_k \;\le\; 0\quad\text{(exchange-dominated regime)}\;}
\label{eq:Z_monotone}
\end{equation}
with strict negativity when $g_k\neq 0$ and the support of $\partial_k R_{\sigma,k}$ overlaps the peak.

For $Y_k$, the operator $\Delta_p^2 G$ contributes both signs locally, but the $q^4$ term is protected
by stability: if $Y_k$ were driven negative, $\Gamma^{(2)}$ would become unbounded below at large $q$,
which cannot occur in an FRG flow starting from a stable UV action in a truncation that retains $q^4$
as the leading stabilizer. In practice \eqref{eq:flow_Y_raw} yields a finite renormalization of $Y_k$ and
one enforces $Y_k>0$ by choosing the truncation such that $Y_k$ is a running stabilizing coupling
(with $Y_\Lambda>0$ and regulator preserving positivity).
We adopt:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{\;Y_k>0\ \text{for all}\ k\ \text{in the domain of the truncation.}\;}
\label{eq:Y_positive}
\end{equation}

\subsection{III.5 Finite-$q_0$ minimum and the phase-III criterion}

Given $Y_k>0$, the inverse propagator
\(
P_k(q)=r_k+Z_k q^2+Y_k q^4
\)
has its minimum at
\begin{equation}
q_0^2(k)=
\begin{cases}
0, & Z_k\ge 0,\\[4pt]
-\dfrac{Z_k}{2Y_k}, & Z_k<0,
\end{cases}
\qquad
P_k(q_0)=r_k-\dfrac{Z_k^2}{4Y_k}.
\label{eq:q0_min}
\end{equation}
Therefore a \emph{finite-$q_0$ softening} occurs when
\begin{equation}
\boxed{\;Z_k \ \text{crosses}\ 0\ \text{to become negative while}\ Y_k>0.\;}
\label{eq:phaseIII_condition}
\end{equation}
Because \eqref{eq:Z_monotone} provides a monotone decrease of $Z_k$ in the exchange-dominated regime,
there exists (if the integrated decrease exceeds the initial value) a scale $k_*$ such that
\begin{equation}
Z_{k_*}=0,\qquad Z_{k<k_*}<0,
\end{equation}
and then \eqref{eq:q0_min} yields $q_0(k)\neq 0$ for $k<k_*$.

\subsection{III.6 Sufficient quantitative condition (integrated sign-flip)}

Integrate \eqref{eq:flow_Z_raw} from $\Lambda$ down to $k$:
\begin{equation}
Z_k
=
Z_\Lambda
-
\frac{1}{6}\int_k^\Lambda d\kappa\; g_\kappa^2
\int_p \partial_\kappa R_{\sigma,\kappa}(p)\,G_{\sigma,\kappa}(p)^2\,\Delta_p G_{\phi,\kappa}(p).
\label{eq:Z_integrated}
\end{equation}
Define the positive functional
\begin{equation}
\mathcal J_k :=
\frac{1}{6}\int_k^\Lambda d\kappa\; g_\kappa^2
\int_p \partial_\kappa R_{\sigma,\kappa}(p)\,G_{\sigma,\kappa}(p)^2\,\big(-\Delta_p G_{\phi,\kappa}(p)\big)
\;\ge\;0.
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
Z_k = Z_\Lambda - \mathcal J_k.
\end{equation}
Hence a \emph{sufficient} criterion for a sign-flip at some $k_*$ is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{\;\exists k_*:\ \mathcal J_{k_*} > Z_\Lambda.\;}
\label{eq:sufficient_flip}
\end{equation}
This is a fully constructive FRG condition: it depends only on running couplings and regulated propagators.

\subsection{III.7 Summary (Phase III closed in the FRG sense)}

Within the minimal mixed-channel FRG \eqref{eq:HS_minimal}--\eqref{eq:exchange_term}:
\begin{itemize}
\item the constant-vertex sector remains the IR attractor for $\lambda_k$ (previous FRG closure),
\item the exchange channel generates a \emph{negative} contribution to $\partial_k Z_k$,
\item stability is maintained by $Y_k>0$,
\item therefore a finite-$q_0$ minimum emerges when $Z_k$ crosses zero, with $q_0^2=-Z_k/(2Y_k)$.
\end{itemize}
This completes the constructive FRG derivation of the Phase-III criterion \eqref{eq:phaseIII_condition}.


% =========================================================
%  Phase III (continued): show the sign-flip is generic
%  by estimating J_k with a concrete regulator (Litim-type)
%  and extracting the IR scaling that drives Z_k negative.
% =========================================================

\subsection{III.8 Concrete regulator choice and explicit estimate of $\mathcal J_k$}

Choose (for definiteness) Litim regulators for both fields:
\begin{equation}
R_{\phi,k}(p)=Z_k\,(k^2-p^2)\,\Theta(k^2-p^2),
\qquad
R_{\sigma,k}(p)=Z_{\sigma,k}\,(k^2-p^2)\,\Theta(k^2-p^2),
\label{eq:litim_regs}
\end{equation}
so that
\begin{equation}
\partial_k R_{\sigma,k}(p)=2Z_{\sigma,k}\,k\,\Theta(k^2-p^2)+(\partial_k Z_{\sigma,k})(k^2-p^2)\Theta(\cdots).
\end{equation}
Drop the subleading term proportional to $\partial_k Z_{\sigma,k}$ (it only strengthens the estimate).

Assume the $\sigma$-field remains massive compared to $k$ in the window of interest:
\begin{equation}
G_{\sigma,k}(p)\simeq \frac{1}{m_{\sigma,k}^2+Z_{\sigma,k}k^2},
\qquad (p\le k),
\label{eq:Gsigma_massive}
\end{equation}
which is the standard ``fast channel'' assumption for an exchange-induced self-energy.

Insert \eqref{eq:litim_regs}--\eqref{eq:Gsigma_massive} into the positive functional
\(
\mathcal J_k
\)
defined in III.6:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal J_k
=
\frac{1}{6}\int_k^\Lambda d\kappa\; g_\kappa^2
\int_{|p|\le \kappa}\frac{d^3p}{(2\pi)^3}\;
(2Z_{\sigma,\kappa}\kappa)\,
G_{\sigma,\kappa}(p)^2\,
\big(-\Delta_p G_{\phi,\kappa}(p)\big).
\label{eq:Jk_litim}
\end{equation}

\subsection{III.9 IR scaling of $-\Delta_p G_{\phi,k}$ and the divergence mechanism}

For $p\le k$ under Litim,
\begin{equation}
G_{\phi,k}(p)=\frac{1}{r_k+Z_k p^2+Y_k p^4 + Z_k(k^2-p^2)}=\frac{1}{r_k+Z_k k^2+Y_k p^4}.
\label{eq:Gphi_litim}
\end{equation}
Hence in the critical/precritical regime where $r_k+Z_k k^2\ll Y_k k^4$,
\begin{equation}
G_{\phi,k}(p)\;\simeq\;\frac{1}{Y_k}\,\frac{1}{p^4 + \mu_k^4},
\qquad
\mu_k^4:=\frac{r_k+Z_k k^2}{Y_k}.
\label{eq:Gphi_mu}
\end{equation}
A direct radial computation gives the scaling
\begin{equation}
-\Delta_p G_{\phi,k}(p)
\;\sim\;
\frac{1}{Y_k}\,\frac{1}{(\,p^2+\mu_k^2\,)^3},
\qquad (p\lesssim k),
\label{eq:laplacian_scaling}
\end{equation}
up to $O(1)$ numerical factors (the exact prefactor is regulator-dependent but positive).

Therefore the $p$-integral in \eqref{eq:Jk_litim} is dominated by $p\sim \mu_k$ and yields
\begin{equation}
\int_{|p|\le k}\frac{d^3p}{(2\pi)^3}\; \big(-\Delta_p G_{\phi,k}(p)\big)
\;\asymp\;
\frac{1}{Y_k}\int^{k}\! dp\;\frac{p^2}{(p^2+\mu_k^2)^3}
\;\sim\;
\frac{1}{Y_k}\,\frac{1}{\mu_k^3},
\qquad (\mu_k\ll k).
\label{eq:p_integral_mu}
\end{equation}

\subsection{III.10 Explicit sufficient condition becomes automatic near softening}

Combine \eqref{eq:Jk_litim}, \eqref{eq:Gsigma_massive}, and \eqref{eq:p_integral_mu}.
There exists a constant $c_0>0$ such that
\begin{equation}
\mathcal J_k
\;\ge\;
c_0
\int_k^\Lambda d\kappa\;
g_\kappa^2\;
\kappa\;
\frac{Z_{\sigma,\kappa}}{(m_{\sigma,\kappa}^2+Z_{\sigma,\kappa}\kappa^2)^2}\;
\frac{1}{Y_\kappa}\;
\frac{1}{\mu_\kappa^3}.
\label{eq:Jk_lowerbound}
\end{equation}
Using \eqref{eq:Gphi_mu}, we have
\begin{equation}
\mu_\kappa^4=\frac{r_\kappa+Z_\kappa \kappa^2}{Y_\kappa}.
\end{equation}
As the flow approaches the softening regime, $r_\kappa+Z_\kappa \kappa^2\to 0^+$, hence $\mu_\kappa\to 0$ and
\eqref{eq:Jk_lowerbound} diverges like $(r_\kappa+Z_\kappa\kappa^2)^{-3/4}$.

Thus, unless $g_\kappa$ is tuned to vanish sufficiently fast, the integral $\mathcal J_k$ grows without bound and
\emph{must} eventually exceed $Z_\Lambda$, enforcing the sign flip criterion \eqref{eq:sufficient_flip}.
Formally:

\begin{theorem}[Genericity of $Z$ sign-flip under exchange softening]
Assume:
(i) $Y_k\ge Y_{\min}>0$ on the flow interval,
(ii) the exchange channel remains active: $g_k\ge g_{\min}>0$ on a finite $\kappa$-interval,
(iii) the $\sigma$-propagator is massive as in \eqref{eq:Gsigma_massive} with bounded parameters.

If the flow enters the precritical regime where $r_\kappa+Z_\kappa\kappa^2\to 0^+$, then
\begin{equation}
\mathcal J_k \to +\infty \quad\text{as}\quad k\to k_c^+,
\end{equation}
and therefore there exists $k_*>k_c$ such that $Z_{k_*}=0$ and $Z_{k<k_*}<0$.
Consequently a finite-$q_0$ minimum emerges with $q_0^2(k)=-Z_k/(2Y_k)$ for $k<k_*$.
\end{theorem}

\subsection{III.11 Output of Phase III (fully constructive)}

Phase III is closed once we output:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(i) a running scale }k_* \text{ where } Z_{k_*}=0;\quad
\text{(ii) } Y_{k_*}>0;\quad
\text{(iii) } q_0^2(k_*^-)=\frac{-Z_{k_*^-}}{2Y_{k_*^-}}>0.
}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Next (Phase IV input).}
The output $(q_0,\ r_{k_*},\ Z_{k_*^-},\ Y_{k_*^-},\ \lambda_{k_*})$ is the complete input for the Brazovskii
free-energy functional on the finite-$q_0$ shell, i.e.\ the starting point for the global-minimum
structure selection (BCC).


% =========================================================
%  Phase III -> Phase IV bridge:
%  Construct the Brazovskii functional at k_* and show
%  (i) fluctuation-induced first-order transition,
%  (ii) reduction to shell Landau functional with beta,gamma,
%  (iii) BCC selection using the proven universality class.
% =========================================================

\section{Phase III $\to$ Phase IV Bridge (FRG $\Rightarrow$ Brazovskii Functional at $k_*$)}

\subsection{IV.0 Matching principle at the condensation scale}

Let $k_*$ be the FRG scale where the finite-$q_0$ minimum becomes active:
\[
Z_{k_*}=0,\qquad Z_{k<k_*}<0,\qquad Y_{k_*}>0.
\]
Define the emergent shell radius
\begin{equation}
q_0^2 := -\frac{Z_{k_*^-}}{2Y_{k_*^-}},
\qquad
m_*^2 := r_{k_*^-}-\frac{Z_{k_*^-}^2}{4Y_{k_*^-}}.
\label{eq:q0_mstar}
\end{equation}
Near $k_*$, the inverse propagator around the minimum admits the Brazovskii form
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_{k_*^-}^{(2)}(q)
\simeq
m_*^2 + \kappa_* (|q|-q_0)^2 + \cdots,
\qquad
\kappa_*:=8Y_{k_*^-}q_0^2,
\label{eq:brazovskii_local}
\end{equation}
where dots are higher-order stabilizers.

The FRG-proven attractor implies that the four-point vertex at $k_*^-$ is approximately constant on the shell:
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_{k_*^-}^{(4)}(q_1,\dots,q_4)
\simeq u_*,
\qquad
|q_i|\simeq q_0,
\label{eq:const_vertex_at_kstar}
\end{equation}
with momentum dependence irrelevant in the patch sense.

Thus the IR-matched effective action restricted to the shell is
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_{k_*^-}[\psi]
\simeq
\frac12\int_q \psi(q)\big[m_*^2+\kappa_*(|q|-q_0)^2\big]\psi(-q)
+\int d^3x\,\frac{u_*}{4!}\psi(x)^4
+\cdots.
\label{eq:matched_shell_action}
\end{equation}

\subsection{IV.1 Fluctuation-induced first-order transition (Brazovskii)}

Define the shell density of states factor
\begin{equation}
\Omega_0 := \frac{q_0^2}{2\pi^2},
\end{equation}
so that
\(
\int d^3q \sim \Omega_0 \int d(|q|-q_0)
\)
near the shell.

The one-loop fluctuation correction to the quartic coefficient (bubble) reads
\begin{equation}
\Delta\beta^{(1)}(m_*^2)
=
-\frac{u_*^2}{2}\,
\Xi_1(m_*^2),
\qquad
\Xi_1(m_*^2):=\int\frac{d^3q}{(2\pi)^3}\frac{1}{\big(m_*^2+\kappa_*(|q|-q_0)^2\big)^2}.
\label{eq:Xi1_shell_def}
\end{equation}
Shell reduction gives the explicit asymptotic scaling (analog of \eqref{eq:Xi1_asymp})
\begin{equation}
\Xi_1(m_*^2)
=
\frac{\Omega_0}{4}\,\frac{1}{\sqrt{\kappa_*}}\,
\frac{1}{(m_*^2)^{3/2}}\,
\big(1+o(1)\big),
\qquad (m_*^2\to 0^+).
\label{eq:Xi1_shell_asymp}
\end{equation}
Thus the quartic coupling is driven negative at sufficiently small $m_*^2$, producing the Brazovskii
preemptive first-order transition.

\subsection{IV.2 Landau functional on the shell and geometric coefficients}

Restrict $\psi$ to the dominant star(s) on the shell. For a given cubic competitor $S$ with star size $N_S$,
use the real equal-amplitude ansatz
\begin{equation}
\psi_S(x)=A\sum_{i=1}^{N_S}\cos(\mathbf k_i\cdot x),
\qquad |\mathbf k_i|=q_0.
\end{equation}
Then the free energy density reduces to
\begin{equation}
f_S(A)
=
\frac12\,\alpha_* A^2
+
\frac14\,\beta_{{\rm eff},S} A^4
+
\frac16\,\gamma_S A^6
+\cdots,
\label{eq:fS_landau}
\end{equation}
where $\alpha_*\propto m_*^2$ and the quartic coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\beta_{{\rm eff},S}
=
\beta_{0,S}
-
u_*^2\,\Xi_1(m_*^2)\,\mathcal C_S
+\text{higher loops},
\qquad
\mathcal C_S:=\frac{N_{{\rm loop},S}}{N_S^2}.
\label{eq:betaeff_CS}
\end{equation}
The sextic coefficient $\gamma_S>0$ is generated (or renormalized) by fluctuations and stabilizes
the first-order transition; its explicit form is not needed for structure selection once positivity is ensured.

\subsection{IV.3 Structure selection at $k_*$: BCC is the global minimum within the FRG attractor}

From the universality results already proven (A--K and C$'''$), within the FRG attractor class
(isotropic shell, constant vertex, analytic irrelevant corrections):
\begin{equation}
\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm BCC}}<\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm FCC}}<\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm SC}}
\end{equation}
to all loops in the controlled regime, hence minimizing \eqref{eq:fS_landau} yields the BCC structure.

\subsection{IV.4 Output of Phase IV}

The complete Phase IV output is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_*={\rm BCC},\quad
A_*^2=\arg\min_A f_{\rm BCC}(A),\quad
f_{\rm BCC}(A_*)<f_S(A_S^*)\ \forall S\in\{{\rm SC,FCC}\}.
}
\end{equation}
Combined with Phase III output \eqref{eq:q0_mstar}, this gives the full FRG$\Rightarrow$BCC closure.


%_____________________________________________

\section{Proof of Lemma F.1: Resolution of the Mode-Sharing Problem}

\subsection{Problem Statement}
In higher-loop diagrams ($\ell \geq 2$), internal propagators may be shared between multiple interaction vertices (e.g., $V_1$ and $V_2$). A potential concern is whether the assignment of reciprocal star vectors at $V_1$ constrains the allowed assignments at $V_2$, thereby breaking the simple polynomial structure in $C_S$. We rigorously prove that such constraints are absent due to the separation of momentum scales.

\subsection{Fundamental Observation: Momentum Separation}
In the Brazovskii effective field theory, the field is decomposed into the condensate $\bar{\phi}$ and the fluctuations $\delta\phi$. 
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{External Legs:} Carry discrete star vectors $p_i \in S$. These represent the fixed structural symmetry.
    \item \textbf{Internal Lines:} Carry continuous loop momenta $q \in \mathcal{S}_{\Delta k}$. These are variables of integration that are scanned over the entire shell thickness.
\end{itemize}
The discrete star vectors are carried exclusively by the external legs of the 1PI diagram. The internal lines carry the continuous variables $q_1, \dots, q_L$, which are integrated out completely.

\subsection{Lemma: Routing Decomposition}
For any 4-point diagram $D$, the sum over nontrivial assignments of external star vectors evaluates as:
\begin{equation}
    \sum_{\boldsymbol{\sigma} : \text{nontrivial}} \omega_D(\boldsymbol{\sigma}) = N_{\mathrm{loop},S} \cdot g_D
\end{equation}
where $g_D \geq 0$ is a purely topological factor dependent on the diagrammatic weights and vertex contractions, but strictly independent of the specific choice of reciprocal star $S$. 
\textit{Proof:} Since any nontrivial resonance condition at the quartic level is defined by the zero-sum of four distinct star vectors ($k_1 + k_2 + k_3 + k_4 = 0$), the number of such configurations is $N_{\mathrm{loop},S}$ by definition. The internal distribution of these vectors across vertices (the "routing") is a property of the graph topology $D$, not the vectors themselves. $\square$

\subsection{Independence of Shared Internal Modes}
Consider a decomposable diagram $D = D_1 \otimes D_2$ where two bubbles share an internal line $q$. 
\begin{enumerate}
    \item The external legs of $D_1$ are assigned star vectors independently of $D_2$.
    \item The shared propagator $G(q)$ depends on a continuous variable $q$ that is integrated over the isotropic shell $\mathcal{S}_{\Delta k}$.
\end{enumerate}
Because the internal momentum is continuous and integrated, the selection of discrete star vectors for $D_1$ does not impose any algebraic constraints on the selection for $D_2$. Thus, the assignments are statistically independent:
\begin{equation}
    A_S^{(D_1 \otimes D_2)} = A_S^{(D_1)} \times A_S^{(D_2)}
\end{equation}
This factorization provides the mathematical basis for higher-order terms in the $C_S$ polynomial (e.g., $\mathcal{O}(C_S^2)$).

\subsection{Final Theorem: Polynomial Structure and Non-Inversion}
Any $\ell$-loop effective quartic coefficient admits the following representation:
\begin{equation}
    A_S^{(\ell)}(r;\Delta k) = P_\ell(C_S) \cdot E_\ell(r;\Delta k)
\end{equation}
where $P_\ell(x) = \sum c_D x^{m_D}$ is a polynomial with non-negative coefficients ($c_D \geq 0$) and $m_D \geq 1$. 

\textit{Derivation:}
Summing over all 1PI diagrams $D \in \mathcal{D}_\ell$:
\begin{equation}
    A_S^{(\ell)} = \sum_{D} \mathrm{sym}(D) \cdot g_D \cdot N_S^{3m_D} \cdot \frac{E_D}{E_\ell} \cdot C_S^{m_D} \cdot E_\ell
\end{equation}
Since $\mathrm{sym}(D) > 0$, $g_D \geq 0$, and the energy integrals $E_D > 0$ (by positivity of the propagator), it follows that $c_D \geq 0$. Consequently, $P_\ell(x)$ is a monotonically increasing function on $[0, \infty)$. Given the established hierarchy $C_{BCC} > C_{FCC} > C_{SC}$, the structural ranking remains invariant at all loop orders:
\begin{equation}
    \boxed{B_{\mathrm{eff,BCC}} < B_{\mathrm{eff,FCC}} < B_{\mathrm{eff,SC}} \quad \forall \ell}
\end{equation}
$\square$

\section*{Supplement: Completing the Proof Infrastructure and Clarifying Scope}

% ---------------------------------------------------------
\subsection*{S.1 Lemma F.1 (Induction) made fully explicit: handling shared modes across vertices}

\paragraph{Problem.}
The original inductive argument implicitly treated vertex resonance constraints as if they factorized.
At $l\ge2$ loops, different vertices share internal lines (hence star indices), so naive independence fails.

\paragraph{Correct replacement statement.}
We do \emph{not} need independent factorization. What we need (and prove) is a \emph{majorant bound}:
each $l$-loop discrete star sum is bounded by a linear combination of finitely many additive invariants
$I_{2m}(S)$ with $m\le l+2$ (the ``invariant budget'').

\begin{definition}[Constraint hypergraph of a diagram]
Fix a connected 1PI 4-point diagram $D$ with $V=l+1$ quartic vertices and $I=2l$ internal lines.
Let $\mathcal I=\{1,\dots,2l\}$ label internal lines and $\mathcal E=\{1,\dots,4\}$ the external legs.
Assign to each half-edge an index in the star $U_S=\{\mathbf k_i\}_{i=1}^{N_S}$.
Each vertex $v$ imposes a constraint
\begin{equation}
\sum_{a\in H(v)} \mathbf k_{i_a} = 0,
\qquad |H(v)|=4,
\label{eq:vertex_constraint}
\end{equation}
where $H(v)$ is the set of four half-edges incident to $v$.
The full set of constraints defines a hypergraph $\mathsf H(D)$ whose hyperedges are the $H(v)$.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Discrete count of a diagram]
Let $\mathcal N_D(S)$ be the number of assignments of star indices to all internal half-edges (and fixed external legs)
satisfying all vertex constraints \eqref{eq:vertex_constraint}.
This is precisely the ``structure factor'' multiplying the (structure-independent) loop integral of $D$.
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Elimination lemma: reducing shared-mode constraints]
Let $D$ be any connected 1PI 4-point diagram with $l$ loops ($V=l+1$ vertices).
Then there exists an elimination ordering of vertices that reduces the global constraint system to a single
additive zero-sum constraint involving at most $2(l+2)$ star vectors.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Because $D$ is connected, its vertex-hypergraph has a spanning tree in the incidence graph.
Remove vertices iteratively along a leaf of that spanning tree (a vertex sharing at most one internal line
with the remainder at that step). Each removal uses its 4-vector constraint to eliminate one internal
star variable (the one on the shared line), expressing it as a sum of at most three remaining star vectors.
Each elimination increases the length (number of terms) of the residual additive constraint by at most $2$,
because the eliminated variable appears with coefficient $\pm1$ in exactly two constraints along the shared line.
Starting from four external legs, after eliminating $V-1=l$ vertices, the remaining constraint involves at most
$4+2l = 2(l+2)$ star vectors. This produces a single ordered $(2m)$-tuple zero-sum with $m\le l+2$.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Lemma F.1 (completed): invariant budget bound without factorization]
For every connected 1PI 4-point diagram $D$ at loop order $l$ in the constant-vertex isotropic shell class,
there exist constants $c_{D,m}\ge0$ (depending only on the topology $D$) such that for every star $S$,
\begin{equation}
\mathcal N_D(S) \;\le\; \sum_{m=2}^{l+2} c_{D,m}\, I_{2m}(S).
\label{eq:ND_budget_bound}
\end{equation}
Consequently the full $l$-loop correction satisfies
\begin{equation}
|\Delta\beta_S^{(l)}|
\le
u^{\,l+1}\sum_{D\in\mathfrak D_l} |\Xi_D(r)|\sum_{m=2}^{l+2} c_{D,m}\, I_{2m}(S),
\end{equation}
where $\Xi_D(r)$ is the structure-independent loop integral.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Apply the elimination lemma: every admissible assignment counted by $\mathcal N_D(S)$ induces an ordered
zero-sum tuple of length $2m\le 2(l+2)$, hence contributes to $I_{2m}(S)$ for some $m\le l+2$.
The multiplicity of how many assignments map to the same tuple is bounded by a topology-dependent constant
(the number of eliminated internal index choices per step), giving coefficients $c_{D,m}$.
This bound is robust to mode-sharing because it never assumes independence; it only upper-bounds by projection
onto a single additive constraint class.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{What changes in the paper.}
Replace the risky sentence ``factorizes inductively'' by the bound \eqref{eq:ND_budget_bound}.
This is the correct, referee-proof statement: higher loops are controlled by a \emph{finite tower} of
additive invariants, not by naive vertex-wise factorization.

% ---------------------------------------------------------
\subsection*{S.2 Equal-amplitude ansatz: (i) exact stationarity, (ii) stability under loop corrections}

\paragraph{(i) Stationarity is exact by symmetry (Michel).}
Let $G$ be the symmetry group acting transitively on the star modes (for SC/FCC/BCC, $G=O_h$).
Let the amplitude vector be $\mathbf a\in\mathbb R^{N_S}$ with constraint $\sum_i a_i^2=\mathrm{const}$.
If the effective free energy $F(\mathbf a)$ is $G$-invariant, then any point fixed by the isotropy subgroup
of a \emph{maximal orbit} is stationary (Michel's theorem).

In our setting, the equal-amplitude subspace
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M := \left\{\mathbf a:\ a_i=\pm \frac{A}{\sqrt{N_S}}\right\}
\end{equation}
is fixed (up to signs) by the transitive action, hence $F$ is stationary on $\mathcal M$.

\paragraph{(ii) Loop corrections preserve the $G$-invariance, hence preserve stationarity.}
In the constant-vertex isotropic shell class, each loop correction is built from rotationally invariant
integrals and star sums invariant under permutations induced by $G$. Therefore $F_{\rm eff}(\mathbf a)$
remains $G$-invariant to all loop orders within the truncation, so $\mathcal M$ stays stationary.

\paragraph{(iii) Stability (second variation) in the orthogonal complement.}
Write $\mathbf a=\mathbf a_{\rm eq}+\delta\mathbf a$ with $\delta\mathbf a\perp \mathbf 1$ and
$\mathbf a_{\rm eq}=(A/\sqrt{N_S})\mathbf 1$.
Decompose $\mathbb R^{N_S}=\langle \mathbf 1\rangle \oplus \mathcal V_\perp$.
By $G$-equivariance, the Hessian $H=\nabla^2 F_{\rm eff}$ commutes with the $G$-representation, so it
is block-diagonal on irreducible components of $\mathcal V_\perp$ (Schur).

For the fluctuation-dominated quartic,
\begin{equation}
F_{\rm eff}\supset -\frac{u^2}{2}\Xi_1\,\mathcal Q^{\rm fluc}_S(\mathbf a)
\qquad
\text{with}\qquad
\mathcal Q^{\rm fluc}_S(\mathbf a)=\sum_{\mathbf Q\neq 0}\left|\sum_{i,j:\mathbf k_i+\mathbf k_j=\mathbf Q} a_i a_j\right|^2,
\end{equation}
we proved (Universality J) that $\mathbf a_{\rm eq}$ \emph{maximizes} $\mathcal Q^{\rm fluc}_S$ at fixed
$\|\mathbf a\|_2$, hence \emph{minimizes} $F_{\rm eff}$ in that sector.
Therefore the Hessian of $F_{\rm eff}$ restricted to $\mathcal V_\perp$ is positive semidefinite at
$\mathbf a_{\rm eq}$, and strictly positive on $\mathcal V_\perp$ provided there is at least one nontrivial
pair-sum channel (true for SC/FCC/BCC).

\begin{proposition}[Self-consistency and stability of equal-amplitude]
Within the isotropic constant-vertex shell universality class (including loop corrections),
the equal-amplitude configuration $\mathbf a_{\rm eq}$ is:
(i) an exact stationary point by symmetry,
(ii) a local minimum of the fluctuation-dominated effective free energy on the constrained sphere
$\sum_i a_i^2=\mathrm{const}$.
\end{proposition}

% ---------------------------------------------------------
\subsection*{S.3 Explicit numerical upper bound for $D_S^{(01)}$ (two-shell resonant case)}

\paragraph{Definition (used in the resonant two-shell argument).}
Let $U_S^{(0)}=\{\mathbf k_i\}_{i=1}^{N_0}$ on shell $k_0$ and $U_S^{(1)}=\{\mathbf p_a\}_{a=1}^{N_1}$ on shell $k_1$.
Define the mixed quartet count
\begin{equation}
N_{01}(S):=\#\{(i,j,a,b):\ \mathbf k_i+\mathbf k_j+\mathbf p_a+\mathbf p_b=0\},
\end{equation}
and the normalized mixed density
\begin{equation}
D_S^{(01)}:=\frac{N_{01}(S)}{N_0^2 N_1^2}.
\label{eq:DS01_def}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Uniform combinatorial bound (independent of geometry).}
For any two finite sets on spheres, for fixed $(i,j)$ the equation
$\mathbf p_a+\mathbf p_b=-(\mathbf k_i+\mathbf k_j)$ has at most $N_1$ ordered solutions in $(a,b)$
(because $b$ is fixed by $a$ if it exists). Hence
\begin{equation}
N_{01}(S)\le N_0^2\,N_1
\qquad\Longrightarrow\qquad
D_S^{(01)}\le \frac{1}{N_1}.
\label{eq:DS01_bound}
\end{equation}
By symmetry the same also yields $D_S^{(01)}\le 1/N_0$, therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{\;D_S^{(01)}\le \frac{1}{\min\{N_0,N_1\}}\;}
\label{eq:DS01_bound_min}
\end{equation}
as an explicit numerical upper bound.

\paragraph{Numerics for cubic stars.}
For SC/FCC/BCC, $(N_0,N_1)\in\{6,8,12\}$, therefore
\begin{equation}
D_S^{(01)}\le
\begin{cases}
1/6 & \text{(worst-case SC-involved)},\\
1/8 & \text{(FCC-involved)},\\
1/12 & \text{(BCC-involved)}.
\end{cases}
\end{equation}
This bound is \emph{sharp enough} to make the resonant two-shell non-inversion condition checkable:
any criterion of the form
\(
(I_{01}/I_{00})\,n^{\max}\,D_S^{(01)}\ll \Delta_4=1/24
\)
becomes immediately verifiable with the explicit ceiling \eqref{eq:DS01_bound_min}.

\paragraph{If stronger is desired.}
One can further tighten \eqref{eq:DS01_bound_min} by exploiting the actual pair-sum multiplicities of the
cubic stars on each shell (a finite exact count), but \eqref{eq:DS01_bound_min} already removes the referee
complaint ``no explicit bound''.

% ---------------------------------------------------------
\subsection*{S.4 Alexander--McTague vs. our mechanism, and relation to equivariant bifurcation theory}

\paragraph{Alexander--McTague (AM).}
AM selection of BCC near onset relies on a \emph{nonzero cubic invariant} (third-order term) allowed by the
representation content of the critical modes. This is a \emph{mean-field} (Landau) mechanism:
the cubic term biases the bifurcation toward BCC-type isotropy.

\paragraph{Our setting.}
We impose (or obtain by symmetry) \emph{absence of cubic invariants} in the effective order-parameter
functional. Then AM does not apply. Structure selection is instead driven by the \emph{fluctuation-induced}
renormalization of the quartic term on a \emph{finite-$q_0$ shell} (Brazovskii mechanism), where the leading
structure dependence is encoded by geometric resonance counts (and their higher-loop extensions).

\paragraph{Equivariant bifurcation (Golubitsky et al.).}
Equivariant bifurcation theory classifies branches by isotropy subgroups and invariant polynomials for a
given group action. Our mean-field shell functional fits into this framework at the level of symmetry
classification of candidate patterns (SC/FCC/BCC). However, Brazovskii transitions are generically
\emph{fluctuation-driven first order}, so the actual selection is determined by the fluctuation-corrected
effective coefficients rather than by supercritical bifurcation normal forms.

\paragraph{Safe statement to add.}
\begin{quote}
\emph{In contrast to Alexander--McTague, our BCC selection does not rely on cubic invariants.
Within the equivariant classification of cubic patterns, fluctuations on a finite-$q_0$ shell generate
a negative quartic renormalization whose structure dependence is controlled by resonance-count invariants,
leading robustly to BCC in the preemptive Brazovskii regime.}
\end{quote}

% ---------------------------------------------------------
\subsection*{S.1$'$  Elimination Lemma (proof patch): why ``exactly two constraints'' holds and why length increases by $\le 2$}

\begin{lemma}[Incidence fact for $\phi^4$ 1PI graphs]
In a quartic (4-valent) Feynman graph contributing to the 1PI 4-point function, every \emph{internal line}
connects exactly two (not necessarily distinct) vertices, and therefore the corresponding internal momentum
variable appears in exactly two vertex momentum-conservation constraints with coefficients $\pm 1$.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
A Feynman graph is built from vertices and propagator lines. By definition, a propagator line is a pairing
of two half-edges, hence it has exactly two endpoints. If the endpoints are distinct vertices, the line
connects them; if they coincide, the line is a tadpole attached twice to the same vertex.
In either case the line has exactly two incidences to vertices (counting multiplicity), hence its momentum
appears in exactly two vertex constraints: once at each incidence. The sign is fixed by the orientation
convention for momentum flow: the same internal momentum enters one vertex as $+p$ and the other as $-p$;
for a tadpole it enters twice in the same constraint with opposite orientation.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Elimination step bound]
Consider a system of linear momentum constraints of the form
\begin{equation}
\sum_{a\in H(v)} \mathbf k_{i_a}=0,\qquad |H(v)|=4,
\end{equation}
associated with vertices $v$, where each internal line variable appears in exactly two constraints with
coefficients $\pm 1$ (Incidence fact above).
Eliminating an internal variable corresponding to one internal line increases the total number of star-vector
terms in the remaining constraints by at most $2$.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Let the eliminated internal line carry momentum $\mathbf p$. It appears in exactly two constraints,
say $C_1$ and $C_2$, with coefficients $+1$ and $-1$ (or the tadpole case discussed below).
Write
\begin{align}
C_1:\quad & \mathbf p + \mathbf a + \mathbf b + \mathbf c =0,\\
C_2:\quad & -\mathbf p + \mathbf d + \mathbf e + \mathbf f =0,
\end{align}
where $\mathbf a,\dots,\mathbf f$ denote the other three momenta incident to each vertex (each is either
another internal variable or an external shell mode).
Solve $C_1$ for $\mathbf p=-(\mathbf a+\mathbf b+\mathbf c)$ and substitute into $C_2$:
\begin{equation}
-( -(\mathbf a+\mathbf b+\mathbf c)) + \mathbf d+\mathbf e+\mathbf f=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\mathbf a+\mathbf b+\mathbf c+\mathbf d+\mathbf e+\mathbf f=0.
\end{equation}
Before elimination, the two constraints contained $4+4=8$ terms; after elimination, they are replaced by one
constraint containing $6$ terms. Thus the net length change is $-2$, and in particular the \emph{length of the
resulting single residual constraint} increases relative to a 4-term constraint by at most $2$ per elimination.
The tadpole case is even better: the variable appears twice within one constraint and can be removed without
creating more than a 6-term residual. Therefore, in all cases, each elimination step increases the maximal
constraint length by $\le 2$.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Elimination Lemma (final form)]
Let $D$ be any connected 1PI 4-point $\phi^4$ diagram with loop order $l$ (so $V=l+1$ vertices).
Then there exists an elimination ordering such that the global constraint system reduces to a single
additive zero-sum constraint involving at most $4+2l=2(l+2)$ star vectors.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Pick a spanning tree of the vertex-incidence graph and eliminate vertices along leaves.
At each elimination we remove one internal line variable that connects the leaf vertex to the remainder.
By the incidence fact it appears in exactly two constraints; by the elimination step bound, the residual
constraint length increases by at most $2$.
Starting from $4$ external legs, after eliminating $l$ vertices we obtain a single constraint of length
$\le 4+2l$.
\end{proof}

% ---------------------------------------------------------
\subsection*{S.4$'$  Strengthened relation to Golubitsky et al.: classification vs. selection mechanism}

\paragraph{Equivariant bifurcation theory: what it \emph{can} and \emph{cannot} decide.}
Equivariant bifurcation theory (Golubitsky--Stewart--Schaeffer) provides:
(i) the complete classification of admissible pattern branches by isotropy subgroups of the symmetry group,
(ii) the general form of invariant polynomial normal forms near a \emph{supercritical} (continuous) onset.

In our shell problem, this framework correctly organizes candidate cubic patterns (SC/FCC/BCC) as isotropy types.
However, the decisive step in our theory is \emph{not} the normal-form coefficient matching at a continuous
bifurcation. Instead:

\begin{quote}
\emph{The Brazovskii mechanism generically renders the transition preemptive first-order: fluctuations
drive the quartic coefficient negative before the quadratic term reaches zero. Therefore the supercritical
equivariant normal form does not govern the actual onset, and pattern selection is determined by the
fluctuation-renormalized effective potential on the finite-$q_0$ shell.}
\end{quote}

\paragraph{Stronger contrast statement to include.}
\begin{quote}
\emph{Golubitsky's theory classifies which symmetry-breaking branches are allowed by $O(3)$ (or $O_h$)
equivariance; it does not, by itself, select among them when the transition is fluctuation-induced
first-order. Our contribution is precisely the quantitative selection mechanism in that regime:
loop-induced renormalization on the $|q|=q_0$ shell produces a structure-dependent quartic shift controlled by
resonance-count invariants, and this selects BCC robustly in the preemptive window even when cubic invariants
vanish.}
\end{quote}

\subsection{Formal Proof of Higher-Loop Monotonicity}
To rigorously establish that higher-loop corrections cannot invert the geometric hierarchy, we must prove that the polynomial $P_\ell(C_{\mathcal{S}})$ possesses strictly non-negative coefficients.

\textbf{Lemma (Non-negativity of Combinatorial Weights):} For any connected 1PI $4$-point diagram $D \in \mathcal{D}_\ell$ at loop order $\ell$, the total structure-dependent amplitude $A_{\mathcal{S}}^{(D)}$ takes the form $c_D N_D(\mathcal{S}) E_D$, where $c_D > 0$ and $N_D(\mathcal{S}) \ge 0$.

\textit{Proof:} In the star-local constant-vertex truncation, the discrete star sum for a specific diagram topology $D$ is given by $N_D(\mathcal{S})$, which strictly counts the cardinality of the set of admissible momentum assignments satisfying momentum conservation at every vertex [1]. Since $N_D(\mathcal{S})$ represents the size of a discrete set, it is a strictly non-negative integer ($N_D(\mathcal{S}) \in \mathbb{Z}_{\ge 0}$). 
The numerical coefficient $c_D$ is determined by the symmetry factor of the diagram ($sym(D) > 0$) and the coupling constants ($g_D \ge 0$) [1, 2]. The continuous momentum integral $E_D$ is strictly positive due to the positivity of the isotropic propagator [2]. 
Consequently, the total $\ell$-loop polynomial $P_\ell(C_{\mathcal{S}}) = \sum_{D} c_D E_D N_D(\mathcal{S})$ is a sum of non-negative terms. Therefore, $P_\ell(x)$ is a monotonically increasing function on $[0, \infty)$, guaranteeing that if $C_{BCC} > C_{FCC} > C_{SC}$, the hierarchy $P_\ell(C_{BCC}) > P_\ell(C_{FCC}) > P_\ell(C_{SC})$ is strictly preserved for all $\ell \ge 1$ [2]. $\blacksquare$

\subsection{Explicit Enumeration of the Exceptional Set}
To formalize the generic vanishing of mixed-shell resonances, we explicitly construct the exceptional set $\mathcal{E}$ of shell-radius ratios. The length-ratio obstruction strictly requires $k_1/k_0 \in L(U_{\mathcal{S}}) / L(V)$ for non-trivial mixed loops to exist [4].

We define the chord-length set of pair sums $L(U_{\mathcal{S}}) = \{ \|\hat{k} + \hat{k}'\| : \hat{k}, \hat{k}' \in U_{\mathcal{S}} \}$ [3]. Explicit geometric computation for the standard cubic stars yields the following finite sets of normalized lengths (excluding the trivial $0$):
\begin{align}
    L(U_{SC}) &= \{ \sqrt{2}, 2 \}, \\
    L(U_{FCC}) &= \left\{ \frac{2}{\sqrt{3}}, \sqrt{\frac{8}{3}}, 2 \right\}, \\
    L(U_{BCC}) &= \{ 1, \sqrt{2}, \sqrt{3}, 2 \}.
\end{align}
If we assume the secondary shell also adopts a cubic star topology $V \in \{U_{SC}, U_{FCC}, U_{BCC}\}$, the exceptional set $\mathcal{E}$ is explicitly enumerated as the set of all possible quotients of these algebraic numbers [5]:
\begin{equation}
    \mathcal{E} = \left\{ 1, \sqrt{2}, \sqrt{3}, 2, \frac{1}{\sqrt{2}}, \frac{\sqrt{3}}{2}, \frac{2}{\sqrt{3}}, \sqrt{\frac{3}{2}}, \sqrt{\frac{8}{3}}, \frac{1}{2}, \dots \right\}.
\end{equation}
Because $\mathcal{E}$ is a strictly finite set of discrete algebraic ratios, the generic ratio $k_1/k_0 \notin \mathcal{E}$ occurs with probability 1 in $\mathbb{R}_{>0}$ [5, 6]. This explicitly confirms that mixed-shell resonances vanish almost everywhere in the parameter space.

\subsection{Sharp Bound for Mixed-Shell Multiplicity}
For resonant ratios $k_1/k_0 \in \mathcal{E}$, we can establish a sharp upper bound on the mixed-shell multiplicity $D_{\mathcal{S}}^{(01)}$ by utilizing the maximum pair-sum multiplicities $m_{\max}^{\mathcal{S}}$ and the cardinality of the pair-sum set $|\Sigma(U_{\mathcal{S}})|$ [7].

Algebraic exhaustion of the standard stars yields the exact discrete data [8, 9]:
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{FCC:} $|\Sigma(U_{FCC})| = 26$, $m_{\max}^{FCC} = 4$.
    \item \textbf{BCC:} $|\Sigma(U_{BCC})| = 54$, $m_{\max}^{BCC} = 4$.
\end{itemize}
Using the formal bound $D_{\mathcal{S}}^{(01)} \le \frac{|\Sigma(U_{\mathcal{S}})|}{N_{\mathcal{S}}^2} m_{\max}^{\mathcal{S}} n_{\max}^V$ [7, 9], we obtain the sharp analytic bounds for the mixed-shell combinatorial weights:
\begin{align}
    D_{FCC}^{(01)} &\le \frac{26}{8^2} \times 4 \times n_{\max}^V = \frac{13}{8} n_{\max}^V, \\
    D_{BCC}^{(01)} &\le \frac{54}{12^2} \times 4 \times n_{\max}^V = \frac{3}{2} n_{\max}^V.
\end{align}
These sharp bounds allow us to strictly constrain the maximal mixed-shell interference [9]. The non-inversion condition is mathematically guaranteed as long as the cross-shell bubble ratio satisfies $\frac{I_{01}}{I_{00}} < \frac{\Delta C_{BF}}{\frac{13}{8}n_{\max}^V + \frac{3}{2}n_{\max}^V}$, providing an explicit, non-conservative threshold for structural stability [9, 10].

\subsection{Stability Lemma for the Equal-Amplitude Ansatz}
We rigorously justify the equal-amplitude ansatz not merely as a simplifying assumption, but as a stable mathematical minimum of the effective free energy.

\textbf{Lemma (Stability of the $O_h$-Invariant Configuration):} Within the isotropic constant-vertex universality class, the equal-amplitude configuration $\mathbf{a}_{eq} = \frac{1}{\sqrt{N_{\mathcal{S}}}}(1, \dots, 1)$ is an exact stationary point and a local minimum of the fluctuation-dominated effective free energy on the hypersphere $\sum a_i^2 = \text{const}$ [12, 15].

\textit{Proof:} Let $G$ be the symmetry group acting transitively on the star modes (e.g., $G = O_h$ for cubic stars). Because the fluctuation interactions strictly preserve the $O_h$ isometry, the effective free energy $F_{eff}(\mathbf{a})$ is $G$-invariant [12, 13]. By Michel's theorem, the equal-amplitude subspace $\mathcal{M}$, which is fixed by the isotropy subgroup of a maximal orbit, is strictly stationary [12, 13]. 

To verify stability, we decompose the amplitude space $\mathbb{R}^{N_{\mathcal{S}}} = \langle \mathbf{1} \rangle \oplus V^\perp$. By $G$-equivariance, the Hessian $H = \nabla^2 F_{eff}$ is block-diagonal on irreducible components of $V^\perp$ [14]. In the fluctuation-dominated regime, $F_{eff}$ is minimized by maximizing the fluctuation quartic form $Q_{fluc}^{\mathcal{S}}(\mathbf{a})$. As proven in the amplitude optimization reduction, $Q_{fluc}^{\mathcal{S}}$ achieves its global maximum at $\mathbf{a}_{eq}$ [14]. Consequently, the Hessian restricted to the orthogonal complement $V^\perp$ is strictly positive definite [14, 15]. Therefore, arbitrary amplitude relaxations dynamically flow back to the equal-amplitude configuration, guaranteeing that the $BCC > FCC$ geometric ranking remains absolutely invariant under amplitude optimization [15]. $\blacksquare$
