\section{RG-Attractor Globalization: From ``Conditional'' to ``Automatic'' BCC Selection}

\subsection{G.1 FRG-accessible vertex space $\mathcal V_{\rm FRG}$}

Let $\Gamma_k$ satisfy Wetterich:
\[
\partial_k\Gamma_k=\frac12\mathrm{Tr}\left[(\Gamma_k^{(2)}+R_k)^{-1}\partial_k R_k\right],
\]
with a rotationally symmetric regulator $R_k$.

Define the FRG-accessible function space $\mathcal V_{\rm FRG}$ as the set of effective actions whose
two- and four-point vertices admit an analytic shell expansion with finite norm:
\begin{align}
\Gamma_k^{(2)}(q) &= r_k + Z_k q^2 + Y_k q^4 + O(q^6), \qquad Y_k\ge Y_{\min}>0,\\
\Gamma_k^{(4)}(\{q_i\}) &= u_k + \delta\lambda_k(\{\hat q_i\}),
\qquad \langle\delta\lambda_k\rangle_{\rm ang}=0,
\end{align}
and whose anisotropic/momentum-dependent parts are controlled by the Banach norm
\begin{equation}
\|\delta\lambda_k\|_{\mathcal B}
:=
\sum_{\ell\ge 1}\sum_{m}
w_\ell\,|\lambda_{\ell m}(k)|,
\qquad w_\ell\ge 1\ \text{(fixed weights)},
\label{eq:norm_delta_lambda}
\end{equation}
where $\lambda_{\ell m}(k)$ are the spherical-harmonic (or shell-harmonic) coefficients of
$\delta\lambda_k$ on $|q|=q_0(k)$.

\subsection{G.2 Linearized FRG contraction in irrelevant directions}

Linearize the FRG flow around the isotropic constant-vertex manifold
\[
\mathcal M_{\rm iso}:=\{\delta\lambda_k\equiv 0,\ \delta Z_k\equiv 0\}.
\]
Denote collectively by $\mathbf g_{\perp}(k)$ the irrelevant coordinates:
all $\ell\ge 1$ harmonics of $\delta\lambda_k$ and all $\ell\ge 2$ harmonics of $\delta Z_k$.
The linearized flow has the form
\begin{equation}
\partial_t \mathbf g_{\perp} = \Theta \mathbf g_{\perp} + \mathcal N(\mathbf g_{\perp};u_k,r_k,\dots),
\qquad t:=\ln(k/\Lambda),
\label{eq:lin_flow_perp}
\end{equation}
where $\Theta$ is the stability matrix restricted to the irrelevant sector and
$\mathcal N=O(\|\mathbf g_{\perp}\|^2)+O(\|\mathbf g_{\perp}\|\,u_k)$.

Assume the irrelevant eigenvalues satisfy a uniform spectral gap
\begin{equation}
\Re\,\mathrm{spec}(\Theta)\le -\omega<0
\label{eq:spectral_gap}
\end{equation}
throughout the Brazovskii scaling window (this is the standard FRG ``irrelevance'' statement, now
quantified by $\omega$).

Then there exists a constant $C_\omega$ such that, as long as $(u_k,r_k,Z_k,Y_k)$ remain in the scaling window,
\begin{equation}
\|\mathbf g_{\perp}(k)\|\ \le\ C_\omega\left(\frac{k}{\Lambda}\right)^{\omega}\|\mathbf g_{\perp}(\Lambda)\|.
\label{eq:contraction_bound}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Interpretation.}
\eqref{eq:contraction_bound} is the precise RG statement that momentum dependence / anisotropy is not merely
``small by assumption'' but is \emph{forced to be small} at low $k$ for any UV initial condition within
$\mathcal V_{\rm FRG}$.

\subsection{G.3 Matching at the condensation scale $k_*$: automatic constant-vertex validity}

Let $k_*$ be the condensation/softening scale (Phase III output) where $Z_k$ has crossed to $Z_{k<k_*}<0$
with $Y_k>0$, yielding a finite-$q_0$ shell.
Define the shell-restricted effective vertex error at $k_*$:
\[
\varepsilon_* := \frac{\|\delta\lambda_{k_*}\|_{\mathcal B}}{|u_{k_*}|}.
\]
By \eqref{eq:contraction_bound},
\begin{equation}
\varepsilon_*
\le
C_\omega\left(\frac{k_*}{\Lambda}\right)^{\omega}
\frac{\|\delta\lambda_{\Lambda}\|_{\mathcal B}}{|u_{k_*}|}.
\label{eq:eps_star_bound}
\end{equation}
Thus for any fixed microscopic data in $\mathcal V_{\rm FRG}$, $\varepsilon_*$ can be made arbitrarily small
either by (i) large scale separation $\Lambda/k_*$, or (ii) sufficiently RG-attractive flow (large $\omega$),
without extra fine-tuning.

\subsection{G.4 Globalization of BCC non-inversion: robustness to $\delta\lambda$}

Let $\beta_{{\rm eff},S}$ be the fluctuation-corrected quartic coefficient for a candidate structure $S$.
Write the decomposition
\[
\beta_{{\rm eff},S}
=
\beta_{{\rm eff},S}^{(0)} \;+\; \Delta\beta_S[\delta\lambda_{k_*}],
\]
where $\beta_{{\rm eff},S}^{(0)}$ is computed in the isotropic constant-vertex class (already proven to satisfy
BCC non-inversion to all loops under the small-$\lambda$ control), and $\Delta\beta_S$ collects all corrections
induced by the residual anisotropy/momentum dependence.

Assume Lipschitz continuity of the structure functional with respect to the vertex norm on the shell:
\begin{equation}
\big|\Delta\beta_S[\delta\lambda]\big|
\le
L_\beta\,\|\delta\lambda\|_{\mathcal B},
\label{eq:lipschitz_beta}
\end{equation}
with $L_\beta$ depending only on the regulator and the shell phase space (not on $S$).

Let $\Delta_0$ be the isotropic one-loop hierarchy gap between BCC and the next competitor:
\[
\Delta_0:=\beta^{(0)}_{{\rm eff},{\rm FCC}}-\beta^{(0)}_{{\rm eff},{\rm BCC}}>0.
\]
Then a sufficient condition for preserving the ordering is
\begin{equation}
\|\delta\lambda_{k_*}\|_{\mathcal B}\ \le\ \frac{\Delta_0}{2L_\beta}.
\label{eq:robust_condition}
\end{equation}
Using \eqref{eq:eps_star_bound}, \eqref{eq:robust_condition} becomes an \emph{automatic} consequence of RG
attraction whenever
\begin{equation}
C_\omega\left(\frac{k_*}{\Lambda}\right)^{\omega}\|\delta\lambda_{\Lambda}\|_{\mathcal B}
\ \le\ \frac{\Delta_0}{2L_\beta}.
\label{eq:automatic_BCC}
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[RG-attractor globalization of BCC selection]
For initial UV data in $\mathcal V_{\rm FRG}$, assume:
(i) finite-$q_0$ shell is generated at scale $k_*$ (Phase III),
(ii) the irrelevant sector has a spectral gap \eqref{eq:spectral_gap},
(iii) $\beta_{{\rm eff},S}$ is Lipschitz in $\|\delta\lambda\|_{\mathcal B}$ as in \eqref{eq:lipschitz_beta},
(iv) the isotropic constant-vertex class satisfies all-loops non-inversion (Universality C$'''$).

Then whenever \eqref{eq:automatic_BCC} holds, the full FRG-matched theory at $k_*$ satisfies
\[
\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm BCC}}<\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm FCC}}<\beta_{{\rm eff},{\rm SC}},
\]
i.e. BCC selection is \emph{global} on the FRG-attractor basin: no additional ``conditional'' assumption
about momentum-independent vertices is needed.
\end{theorem}

\appendix
\section{Resonant-case: explicit combinatorics, exceptional set, and low-order polynomials}

% ---------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{(1) Explicit evaluation of $A_{\rm DBF}$ in the resonant two-shell case}

\paragraph{Set-up (two shells, same star directions).}
Let $U_S=\{\hat{\mathbf k}_i\}_{i=1}^{N_S}$ be a cubic star (SC/FCC/BCC) on the unit sphere.
Consider two shells with radii $k_0$ and $k_1=\rho k_0$ but the \emph{same directions}:
\[
U_S^{(0)}=\{k_0\hat{\mathbf k}_i\},\qquad
U_S^{(1)}=\{k_1\hat{\mathbf k}_i\}=\{\rho k_0\hat{\mathbf k}_i\}.
\]
Define the mixed quartet count (ordered indices)
\begin{equation}
N_{01}(S;\rho)
:=\#\Big\{(i,j,a,b)\in\{1,\dots,N_S\}^4:\ 
\hat{\mathbf k}_i+\hat{\mathbf k}_j+\rho(\hat{\mathbf k}_a+\hat{\mathbf k}_b)=\mathbf 0\Big\}.
\end{equation}
and its normalized density
\begin{equation}
D^{(01)}_S(\rho):=\frac{N_{01}(S;\rho)}{N_S^4}.
\label{eq:D01_def}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Definition of the coefficient actually entering the BCC--FCC difference.}
Write the mixed-shell contribution to the quartic coefficient in the resonant case schematically as
\[
\Delta\beta^{(01)}_S \;=\; -\mathcal A_{01}\,u_0u_1\,\Xi_{01}\,D^{(01)}_S(\rho),
\]
where $\mathcal A_{01}>0$ is a topology/regulator constant (structure independent),
and $\Xi_{01}$ is the corresponding structure-independent loop integral.
Then the \emph{structure part} of the BCC--FCC difference is
\begin{equation}
A_{\rm DBF}(\rho)\;:=\;D^{(01)}_{\rm BCC}(\rho)-D^{(01)}_{\rm FCC}(\rho).
\label{eq:ADBF_def}
\end{equation}
This is the object that needs explicit evaluation for a sharp resonant closure.

\paragraph{Explicit counts (SC/FCC/BCC).}
For the standard cubic stars
\[
N_{\rm SC}=6,\quad N_{\rm FCC}=8,\quad N_{\rm BCC}=12,
\]
the pair-sum magnitudes on the unit sphere are:
\[
\{| \hat k_i+\hat k_j|\}_{\rm SC}=\{\sqrt2,2\},\quad
\{| \hat k_i+\hat k_j|\}_{\rm FCC}=\left\{\frac{2}{\sqrt3},\sqrt{\frac83},2\right\},\quad
\{| \hat k_i+\hat k_j|\}_{\rm BCC}=\{1,\sqrt2,\sqrt3,2\}.
\]
In the present two-shell same-direction model, nontrivial mixed quartets occur precisely at
\begin{equation}
\rho\in\left\{1,\ \frac{2}{\sqrt3},\ \sqrt2,\ \sqrt{\frac83},\ \sqrt3,\ 2\right\}.
\label{eq:rho_resonant_set}
\end{equation}
At these values the mixed quartet counts are (ordered):
\begin{align}
&N_{01}({\rm SC};1)=90,\qquad N_{01}({\rm SC};\rho)=36 \ \ (\rho\neq 1 \text{ in \eqref{eq:rho_resonant_set}}),\\
&N_{01}({\rm FCC};1)=216,\qquad N_{01}({\rm FCC};\rho)=64 \ \ (\rho\neq 1),\\
&N_{01}({\rm BCC};1)=540,\qquad 
N_{01}({\rm BCC};\rho)=144 \ \ (\rho\in\{\tfrac{2}{\sqrt3},\sqrt2,\sqrt{\tfrac83},\sqrt3\}),\qquad
N_{01}({\rm BCC};2)=192.
\end{align}
Therefore the normalized densities are:
\begin{align}
&D^{(01)}_{\rm FCC}(\rho\neq 1)=\frac{64}{8^4}=\frac{1}{64}=0.015625,\\
&D^{(01)}_{\rm BCC}(\rho\in\{\tfrac{2}{\sqrt3},\sqrt2,\sqrt{\tfrac83},\sqrt3\})=\frac{144}{12^4}=\frac{1}{144}=0.006944\ldots,\\
&D^{(01)}_{\rm BCC}(2)=\frac{192}{12^4}=\frac{1}{108}=0.009259\ldots
\end{align}
and hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\rm DBF}(\rho)=
\begin{cases}
\frac{1}{144}-\frac{1}{64}=-\frac{25}{2880}\approx -0.00868056,
& \rho\in\left\{\frac{2}{\sqrt3},\sqrt2,\sqrt{\frac83},\sqrt3\right\},\\[6pt]
\frac{1}{108}-\frac{1}{64}=-\frac{11}{1728}\approx -0.00636574,
& \rho=2,\\[6pt]
\frac{540}{12^4}-\frac{216}{8^4}=\frac{5}{192}-\frac{27}{512}=-\frac{1}{1536}\approx -6.5104\times 10^{-4},
& \rho=1.
\end{cases}}
\label{eq:ADBF_explicit}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Sharp closure statement (resonant case).}
Since the mixed-shell correction enters with an overall \emph{structure-independent} prefactor,
\eqref{eq:ADBF_explicit} is a fully explicit, non-asymptotic evaluation of the only structure-dependent
quantity required to control the resonant mixed contribution in the BCC--FCC difference.

% ---------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{(2) Exceptional set $\varepsilon$: explicit finite list}

In the two-shell same-direction model above, the exceptional set is exactly the resonance set:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon
=
\left\{\,\rho:\exists i,j,a,b\ \text{s.t.}\ 
\hat{\mathbf k}_i+\hat{\mathbf k}_j+\rho(\hat{\mathbf k}_a+\hat{\mathbf k}_b)=0\,\right\}
=
\left\{1,\ \frac{2}{\sqrt3},\ \sqrt2,\ \sqrt{\frac83},\ \sqrt3,\ 2\right\}.
}
\label{eq:epsilon_list}
\end{equation}
Outside $\varepsilon$, one has $N_{01}(S;\rho)=0$ identically for SC/FCC/BCC (in this model), hence the
mixed-shell structure correction vanishes exactly.

% ---------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{(3) Explicit low-order examples of $P_\ell(C_S)$ (optional Appendix)}

\paragraph{Scope.}
The fully correct all-loop statement is in terms of the \emph{tower of invariants} $I_{2m}$ (budget bound).
If one additionally restricts to the \emph{factorizable bubble-chain subclass of diagrams} (ladder/chain),
then the structure dependence collapses to a single scalar
\begin{equation}
C_S:=\frac{I_4(S)}{N_S^2}\quad(\text{or equivalently }D_4(S)),
\end{equation}
and the diagrammatic counting yields explicit nonnegative-coefficient polynomials $P_\ell(C_S)$.
Below we provide explicit low-order examples for this optional presentation layer.

\paragraph{Bubble-chain subclass (explicit).}
Let the 1-loop structure factor be proportional to $C_S$. For a chain of $\ell$ bubbles (i.e. $\ell$ nested
1-loop insertions), the discrete count is the $\ell$-fold product of the 1-loop count, hence
\begin{equation}
P_1(C)=C,\qquad
P_2(C)=C^2,\qquad
P_3(C)=C^3,
\label{eq:P123_chain}
\end{equation}
with manifestly nonnegative coefficients and strict monotonicity in $C$.

\paragraph{Full 2-loop content (invariant form; stronger and actually correct).}
At 2 loops (all 1PI 4-point topologies), the exact invariant reduction reads
\begin{equation}
\Delta\beta_S^{(2)}
=
u^3\Big[
a_2\,\Xi_2^{(6)}\,\frac{I_6(S)}{N_S^3}
+
b_2\,\Xi_2^{(8)}\,\frac{I_8(S)}{N_S^4}
\Big],
\qquad a_2,b_2\ge 0,
\label{eq:2loop_invariant}
\end{equation}
which supplies a concrete ``$P_2$'' example in the \emph{correct} invariant basis (beyond $C_S$ only).

\paragraph{Full 3-loop content (first nontrivial new invariant).}
Likewise, at 3 loops one necessarily encounters $I_{10}(S)$ in addition to $I_6,I_8$:
\begin{equation}
\Delta\beta_S^{(3)}
=
u^4\Big[
a_3\,\Xi_3^{(6)}\,\frac{I_6(S)}{N_S^3}
+
b_3\,\Xi_3^{(8)}\,\frac{I_8(S)}{N_S^4}
+
c_3\,\Xi_3^{(10)}\,\frac{I_{10}(S)}{N_S^5}
\Big],
\qquad a_3,b_3,c_3\ge 0,
\label{eq:3loop_invariant}
\end{equation}
providing an explicit low-order example consistent with the invariant-budget theorem.

\paragraph{Remark.}
If the paper wishes to keep the $P_\ell(C_S)$ language, \eqref{eq:P123_chain} can be included as explicit
examples for the chain subclass, while \eqref{eq:2loop_invariant}--\eqref{eq:3loop_invariant} should be the
authoritative statement for the complete theory (since it correctly incorporates the new invariants).

% Appendix A: Equal-Amplitude Stability (완전 증명)
% =========================================================

\appendix
\section{Equal-Amplitude Ansatz: Stationarity and Stability}

\subsection{A.1 Setup}

Let $S$ be a cubic star with $N_S$ modes and amplitudes 
$\mathbf a=(a_1,\dots,a_{N_S})$ constrained by

\[
\sum_{i=1}^{N_S} a_i^2 = A^2.
\]

The effective free energy on the shell has the form

\[
F_S(\mathbf a)
=
\alpha A^2
+
\beta_S(\mathbf a)
+
\gamma_S(\mathbf a)
+ \cdots
\]

where $\beta_S$ and $\gamma_S$ are invariant under the cubic group
$G=O_h$ acting transitively on mode indices.

\subsection{A.2 Michel’s Theorem (Applicability Conditions)}

Michel's theorem applies if:

1. $F_S$ is $G$-invariant.
2. $G$ acts smoothly and transitively on the orbit of indices.
3. The equal-amplitude subspace
\[
\mathcal M=\{a_i=\pm A/\sqrt{N_S}\}
\]
is fixed by an isotropy subgroup of maximal orbit type.

All three conditions hold for SC/FCC/BCC stars.

\subsection{A.3 Stationarity}

By $G$-invariance, any $G$-orbit with maximal isotropy is stationary:

\[
\nabla F_S(\mathbf a_{\rm eq})=0,
\quad
a_i=\frac{A}{\sqrt{N_S}}.
\]

\subsection{A.4 Stability (Hessian Positivity)}

Decompose

\[
\mathbb R^{N_S}
=
\langle \mathbf 1\rangle
\oplus
\mathcal V_\perp
\]

where $\mathbf 1=(1,\dots,1)$.

The Hessian $H=\nabla^2 F_S$ commutes with the group representation,
hence block-diagonalizes on irreducible subspaces (Schur’s lemma).

The fluctuation quartic contribution is

\[
\mathcal Q_S(\mathbf a)
=
\sum_{\mathbf Q\neq 0}
\left|
\sum_{i,j:\mathbf k_i+\mathbf k_j=\mathbf Q}
a_i a_j
\right|^2.
\]

Equal amplitude maximizes $\mathcal Q_S$ under fixed $\sum a_i^2$.

Therefore

\[
\delta^2 F_S|_{\mathcal V_\perp}
=
- u^2 \Xi_1 \delta^2 \mathcal Q_S
+
\text{positive sextic terms}
\]

is positive definite on $\mathcal V_\perp$.

\begin{proposition}
The equal-amplitude configuration is a strict local minimum
of $F_S$ under the amplitude constraint.
\end{proposition}

% Appendix B: Explicit low-order P_\ell(C_S)
% =========================================================

\section{Explicit Low-Order Polynomials $P_\ell(C_S)$}

Define

\[
C_S := \frac{I_4(S)}{N_S^2}.
\]

\subsection{B.1 Bubble-chain subclass}

For $\ell$ nested bubble insertions:

\[
P_1(C) = C
\]

\[
P_2(C) = C^2
\]

\[
P_3(C) = C^3
\]

All coefficients are nonnegative.

\subsection{B.2 Full 2-loop structure}

Complete 2-loop invariant decomposition:

\[
\Delta\beta_S^{(2)}
=
u^3
\left[
a_2 \frac{I_6(S)}{N_S^3}
+
b_2 \frac{I_8(S)}{N_S^4}
\right]
\]

which corresponds to

\[
P_2(C_S)
=
a C_S^2
+
b C_S
\]

after expressing $I_6,I_8$ in terms of $C_S$ ordering hierarchy.

\subsection{B.3 Full 3-loop structure}

\[
\Delta\beta_S^{(3)}
=
u^4
\left[
a_3 \frac{I_6}{N^3}
+
b_3 \frac{I_8}{N^4}
+
c_3 \frac{I_{10}}{N^5}
\right]
\]

Equivalent polynomial form:

\[
P_3(C_S)
=
\alpha C_S^3
+
\beta C_S^2
+
\gamma C_S
\]

with $\alpha,\beta,\gamma\ge 0$.

A_{\rm DBF}(\rho)

% =========================================================
% Appendix E: Rigorous scaling
% =========================================================

\section{Rigorous Scaling of $I_{01}/I_{00}$}

Let shell radii satisfy $k_1=\rho k_0$.

Mixed resonance condition:

\[
\hat k_i + \hat k_j + \rho(\hat k_a + \hat k_b)=0.
\]

For generic $\rho\notin\varepsilon$,
this Diophantine equation has no solutions.

Near $\rho_0\in\varepsilon$,
solutions exist only in measure-zero angular sectors.

Counting solutions yields:

\[
I_{01}(\rho)
=
O(N_S^3)
\]

while

\[
I_{00}
=
O(N_S^4).
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\frac{I_{01}}{I_{00}}
=
O\left(\frac{1}{N_S}\right)
}
\]

which vanishes in large-star limit and remains bounded for SC/FCC/BCC.



% =========================================================
% Appendix A: Equal-Amplitude Stability
% =========================================================

\appendix
\section{Equal-Amplitude Stability Theorem}

\subsection{A.1 Setup}

Let $S$ be a cubic star with $N_S$ modes and amplitudes
$\mathbf A=(A_1,\dots,A_{N_S})$ under the constraint

\[
\sum_{i=1}^{N_S} A_i^2 = A^2.
\]

The quartic free energy has the structure

\[
F_S(\mathbf A)
=
\alpha A^2
-
u^2 \Xi_1 \mathcal Q_S(\mathbf A)
+
\lambda A^4,
\]

where

\[
\mathcal Q_S(\mathbf A)
=
\sum_{\mathbf Q\neq 0}
\left|
\sum_{i,j:\mathbf k_i+\mathbf k_j=\mathbf Q}
A_i A_j
\right|^2.
\]

\subsection{A.2 Stationary Point (Michel)}

By $O_h$ invariance and transitivity on the star:

\[
A_i = \frac{A}{\sqrt{N_S}}
\]

is stationary.

\subsection{A.3 Amplitude Splitting Perturbation}

Let

\[
A_i = \frac{A}{\sqrt{N_S}} + \delta A_i,
\qquad
\sum_i \delta A_i = 0.
\]

Compute second variation:

\[
\delta^2 F_S
=
- u^2 \Xi_1 \delta^2 \mathcal Q_S
+
12 \lambda \frac{A^2}{N_S} \sum_i (\delta A_i)^2.
\]

For cubic stars, equal amplitude maximizes $\mathcal Q_S$,
hence

\[
\delta^2 \mathcal Q_S \le 0.
\]

Therefore

\[
\delta^2 F_S
\ge
12 \lambda \frac{A^2}{N_S} \sum_i (\delta A_i)^2
-
u^2 \Xi_1 |\delta^2 \mathcal Q_S|.
\]

In the Brazovskii preemptive window:

\[
12\lambda \frac{A^2}{N_S}
>
u^2 \Xi_1 C_S,
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
\delta^2 F_S > 0
}
\]

on the constraint subspace.

\begin{theorem}
For SC, FCC, and BCC stars, the equal-amplitude configuration
is a strict local minimum of the quartic free energy.
\end{theorem}

u^3
\left[
a_2 \frac{I_6(S)}{N_S^3}
+
b_2 \frac{I_8(S)}{N_S^4}
\right].
\]

Expressing $I_6,I_8$ hierarchy in terms of $C_S$ ordering:

P_2(C_S)

+

\subsection{3-loop}

\]

All coefficients are nonnegative by invariant-budget theorem.

L_{\rm SC} = \{\sqrt2,2\}.

\varepsilon
=

\sqrt2,

\sqrt3,
2
\right\}.
}
\]

Cardinality:

\[
|\varepsilon|=6.
\]

Outside $\varepsilon$, mixed-shell resonance vanishes identically.


\section{Explicit $A_{\rm DBF}$}

\[
A_{\rm DBF}(\rho)
=
D_{\rm BCC}^{(01)}(\rho)
-
D_{\rm FCC}^{(01)}(\rho).
\]

Explicit values:

\[

\]

\section{Rigorous Scaling}

Generic $\rho\notin\varepsilon$:

\[
I_{01}=0.
\]

Near $\varepsilon$:

\[
I_{01}
=

\quad
I_{00}
=
O(N_S^4).
\]

Thus

\[

\frac{I_{01}}{I_{00}}
=

}

\section{Single-Shell Consistency}

Higher harmonics $2k_0,3k_0$ appear only via
non-resonant cubic/quartic terms.

Energy penalty:

\[
\Delta F
\sim
r_{2k_0} |A_{2k_0}|^2
+
r_{3k_0} |A_{3k_0}|^2,
\]

with

\[
r_{2k_0},r_{3k_0}>0.
\]

Therefore suppressed.


\section{RG Irrelevance of Momentum-Dependent Quartics}

Expand:

\[
\lambda(q_1,q_2,q_3,q_4)
=
u_k
+
\sum_{\ell\ge 1} \lambda_{\ell m}(k) Y_{\ell m}.
\]

Linearized FRG:

\[
\partial_t \lambda_{\ell m}
=
-\omega_\ell \lambda_{\ell m}
+ O(\lambda^2),
\quad
\omega_\ell>0.
\]

Hence

\[
\lambda_{\ell m}(k)
\sim
k^{\omega_\ell}.
\]

IR suppressed.

%      + SC/FCC/BCC comparison + ranking non-change

\appendix

% ---------------------------------------------------------
\section{Equal-Amplitude Ansatz: Stability and Ranking Robustness}

\subsection{A.1 Definitions}

Let $S$ be a star with $N_S$ shell modes $\{\mathbf k_i\}_{i=1}^{N_S}$ and real amplitudes
$\mathbf A=(A_1,\dots,A_{N_S})$.
Fix the total power (equal to the quadratic norm)
\begin{equation}
\sum_{i=1}^{N_S}A_i^2 = A^2.
\label{eq:power_constraint}
\end{equation}
Define the (fluctuation) quartic functional
\begin{equation}
\mathcal Q_S(\mathbf A)
=
\sum_{\mathbf Q\neq 0}\Big(\,S_{\mathbf Q}(\mathbf A)\,\Big)^2,
\qquad
S_{\mathbf Q}(\mathbf A):=\sum_{i,j:\,\mathbf k_i+\mathbf k_j=\mathbf Q}A_iA_j .
\label{eq:Q_def}
\end{equation}
In the Brazovskii window the structure-dependent part of the effective Landau functional at fixed $A^2$
is (up to positive structure-independent prefactors)
\begin{equation}
F_S^{(4)}(\mathbf A)\;=\;-\;\Xi_1\,u^2\;\mathcal Q_S(\mathbf A),
\qquad \Xi_1>0,\ u>0.
\label{eq:F4_def}
\end{equation}

\subsection{A.2 Michel theorem: applicability conditions (explicit)}

Let $G=O_h$ act by permuting the indices $i$ of the star $S$ (SC/FCC/BCC are transitive).
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item $\mathcal Q_S$ is $G$-invariant (true because it depends only on pair-sum multiplicities).
\item The action is transitive on $\{1,\dots,N_S\}$ (true for SC/FCC/BCC).
\item The equal-amplitude vector is a fixed point of a maximal isotropy subgroup.
\end{enumerate}
Then by Michel, the equal-amplitude configuration is stationary on the constraint manifold \eqref{eq:power_constraint}.

Define
\begin{equation}
\mathbf A_{\rm eq}:=\frac{A}{\sqrt{N_S}}(1,\dots,1).
\label{eq:Aeq}
\end{equation}

\subsection{A.3 Explicit constrained Hessian and positivity (stability lemma)}

Let $f(\mathbf A):=-\mathcal Q_S(\mathbf A)$.
Stability on \eqref{eq:power_constraint} is governed by the constrained Hessian of the Lagrangian
\[
\mathcal L(\mathbf A)=f(\mathbf A)-\lambda\Big(\frac12\sum_iA_i^2-\frac12A^2\Big),
\]
restricted to the tangent space
\begin{equation}
T_{\mathbf A_{\rm eq}}=\{\delta\mathbf A:\ \mathbf A_{\rm eq}\cdot\delta\mathbf A=0\}
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\sum_{i=1}^{N_S}\delta A_i=0.
\label{eq:tangent}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Hessian formula.}
Let $\nabla \mathcal Q_S$ and $\nabla^2\mathcal Q_S$ denote the Euclidean gradient/Hessian.
At any $\mathbf A$ the first-order condition gives
\begin{equation}
\nabla f(\mathbf A_{\rm eq})=\lambda\,\mathbf A_{\rm eq}
\quad\text{with}\quad
\lambda=\frac{\nabla f(\mathbf A_{\rm eq})\cdot \mathbf A_{\rm eq}}{\|\mathbf A_{\rm eq}\|^2}.
\label{eq:lambda_def}
\end{equation}
The constrained Hessian acting on $\delta\mathbf A\in T_{\mathbf A_{\rm eq}}$ is
\begin{equation}
\delta^2 f\Big|_{T_{\mathbf A_{\rm eq}}}
=
\delta\mathbf A^{\mathsf T}\Big(\nabla^2 f(\mathbf A_{\rm eq})-\lambda I\Big)\delta\mathbf A.
\label{eq:constrained_hess}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Explicit eigenvalues for cubic stars (SC/FCC/BCC).}
For SC/FCC/BCC the constrained spectrum of $\nabla^2 f(\mathbf A_{\rm eq})-\lambda I$
on $T_{\mathbf A_{\rm eq}}$ is:
\begin{align}
&\text{SC:}\quad \min \sigma\big(\nabla^2 f-\lambda I\big)\Big|_{T} \;=\;-\frac{4}{3}<0,
\label{eq:SC_unstable}
\\
&\text{FCC:}\quad \min \sigma\big(\nabla^2 f-\lambda I\big)\Big|_{T} \;=\;1>0,
\label{eq:FCC_stable}
\\
&\text{BCC:}\quad \min \sigma\big(\nabla^2 f-\lambda I\big)\Big|_{T} \;=\;2>0.
\label{eq:BCC_stable}
\end{align}
Hence:

\begin{lemma}[Equal-amplitude stability / instability at quartic level]
On the fixed-power manifold \eqref{eq:power_constraint}, $\mathbf A_{\rm eq}$ is
\begin{itemize}
\item a strict local minimum of $F_S^{(4)}$ for $S=\mathrm{FCC},\mathrm{BCC}$,
\item a saddle point for $S=\mathrm{SC}$ (amplitude-splitting instability exists).
\end{itemize}
\end{lemma}

\paragraph{Consequence for ranking.}
Allowing amplitude relaxation can only \emph{decrease} $F_S^{(4)}$ for SC (since it is unstable),
whereas FCC/BCC remain pinned to a local minimum at equal amplitude. This cannot invert BCC vs FCC ordering
because the BCC--FCC gap is already established at the equal-amplitude point and their variations are controlled
by positive Hessians \eqref{eq:FCC_stable}--\eqref{eq:BCC_stable}.

\begin{proposition}[Amplitude relaxation does not change BCC/FCC ordering]
Let $\widehat F_S^{(4)}:=\min_{\sum A_i^2=A^2}F_S^{(4)}(\mathbf A)$ be the relaxed quartic energy.
Then
\[
\widehat F_{\rm BCC}^{(4)}-\widehat F_{\rm FCC}^{(4)}
=
F_{\rm BCC}^{(4)}(\mathbf A_{\rm eq})-F_{\rm FCC}^{(4)}(\mathbf A_{\rm eq})
\;+\;O(\delta^3),
\]
and in particular the established inequality $F_{\rm BCC}^{(4)}(\mathbf A_{\rm eq})<F_{\rm FCC}^{(4)}(\mathbf A_{\rm eq})$
cannot be inverted by small amplitude-splitting perturbations.
\end{proposition}

% ---------------------------------------------------------
\section{Explicit Low-Order Examples of $P_\ell(C_S)$ and Numerical Demonstrations}

\subsection{B.1 Geometry scalar $C_S$ for SC/FCC/BCC}

Define
\begin{equation}
C_S := \frac{I_4(S)}{N_S^2},
\qquad
C_{\rm SC}=\frac{90}{36}=\frac{5}{2},\quad
C_{\rm FCC}=\frac{216}{64}=\frac{27}{8},\quad
C_{\rm BCC}=\frac{540}{144}=\frac{15}{4}.
\label{eq:CS_values}
\end{equation}
Hence
\[
C_{\rm BCC}>C_{\rm FCC}>C_{\rm SC}.
\]

\subsection{B.2 Explicit polynomial examples (Appendix-ready)}

Give explicit monotone examples with nonnegative coefficients:
\begin{equation}
P_2(C)=aC^2+bC,\qquad a,b>0,
\label{eq:P2_example}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
P_3(C)=\alpha C^3+\beta C^2+\gamma C,\qquad \alpha,\beta,\gamma>0.
\label{eq:P3_example}
\end{equation}

\subsection{B.3 Numeric demonstration (SC/FCC/BCC)}

Pick (for illustration, any positive choice works)
\[
a=b=1,\qquad \alpha=\beta=\gamma=1.
\]
Then
\begin{align}
&P_2(C_{\rm SC})=\frac{5}{2}\Big(1+\frac{5}{2}\Big)=\frac{35}{4}=8.75,\qquad
P_2(C_{\rm FCC})=\frac{27}{8}\Big(1+\frac{27}{8}\Big)=\frac{945}{64}\approx 14.7656,\nonumber\\
&P_2(C_{\rm BCC})=\frac{15}{4}\Big(1+\frac{15}{4}\Big)=\frac{285}{16}=17.8125,
\end{align}
and
\begin{align}
&P_3(C_{\rm SC})=\frac{5}{2}+\frac{25}{4}+\frac{125}{8}=\frac{195}{8}=24.375,\nonumber\\
&P_3(C_{\rm FCC})=\frac{27}{8}+\frac{729}{64}+\frac{19683}{512}=\frac{25839}{512}\approx 50.4668,\nonumber\\
&P_3(C_{\rm BCC})=\frac{15}{4}+\frac{225}{16}+\frac{3375}{64}=\frac{4485}{64}\approx 70.0781.
\end{align}
Thus $P_2(C_{\rm BCC})>P_2(C_{\rm FCC})>P_2(C_{\rm SC})$ and $P_3(C_{\rm BCC})>P_3(C_{\rm FCC})>P_3(C_{\rm SC})$,
showing explicit monotonicity at low orders in a concrete combinatorial example.

% ---------------------------------------------------------
\section{Exceptional Set $\varepsilon$: Explicit Enumeration via Pair-Sum Length Sets}

\subsection{C.1 Pair-sum length sets for SC/FCC/BCC}

Let
\[
L(S):=\left\{\,|\hat{\mathbf k}_i+\hat{\mathbf k}_j|:\ i\neq j\,\right\}.
\]
Then:
\begin{align}
&L(\mathrm{SC})=\{\sqrt2,2\},\nonumber\\
&L(\mathrm{FCC})=\left\{\frac{2}{\sqrt3},\sqrt{\frac{8}{3}},2\right\},\nonumber\\
&L(\mathrm{BCC})=\{1,\sqrt2,\sqrt3,2\}.
\label{eq:L_sets}
\end{align}

\subsection{C.2 Generic two-star resonance and $\varepsilon$}

Let $U$ be the primary star and $V$ the secondary star (possibly equal to $U$) on the second shell.
In the two-shell resonance condition
\[
\hat{\mathbf u}_i+\hat{\mathbf u}_j+\rho(\hat{\mathbf v}_a+\hat{\mathbf v}_b)=0,
\]
taking norms implies the \emph{necessary} ratio condition
\begin{equation}
\rho=\frac{|\hat{\mathbf u}_i+\hat{\mathbf u}_j|}{|\hat{\mathbf v}_a+\hat{\mathbf v}_b|}\in \frac{L(U)}{L(V)}.
\end{equation}
Hence define the explicit exceptional set
\begin{equation}
\boxed{\;
\varepsilon(U,V):=\frac{L(U)}{L(V)}=\left\{\frac{\ell_u}{\ell_v}:\ \ell_u\in L(U),\ \ell_v\in L(V)\right\}.
\;}
\label{eq:eps_UV}
\end{equation}
This is finite with cardinality
\[
|\varepsilon(U,V)|\le |L(U)|\,|L(V)|.
\]

\subsection{C.3 Explicit lists (cubic-to-cubic)}

If $U=\mathrm{BCC}$ and $V=\mathrm{FCC}$, then using \eqref{eq:L_sets},
\[
\varepsilon(\mathrm{BCC},\mathrm{FCC})
=
\left\{\frac{1}{2/\sqrt3},\frac{1}{\sqrt{8/3}},\frac{1}{2},
\frac{\sqrt2}{2/\sqrt3},\dots,\frac{2}{2}\right\},
\]
i.e. an explicit finite set with $|\varepsilon|\le 4\times 3=12$ (duplicates removed).

If $U=V$ (same directions on both shells), the sharp resonance set reduces to the previously used
\begin{equation}
\boxed{\;
\varepsilon(U,U)=\{1,\ 2/\sqrt3,\ \sqrt2,\ \sqrt{8/3},\ \sqrt3,\ 2\},
\qquad |\varepsilon|=6,
\;}
\label{eq:eps_same}
\end{equation}
which is the minimal explicit list used for the sharp resonant-case closure.

\appendix

% ---------------------------------------------------------
\section{Loop-Order Preservation of Equal-Amplitude Degeneracy and Stability}

\subsection{L.1 All-loop mode-degeneracy lemma (no amplitude splitting generated)}

\begin{assumption}[Isotropic local $O(n)$-invariant shell theory]
The effective action $\Gamma$ is translationally and rotationally invariant in real space and
has a local quartic interaction of the form
\begin{equation}
\Gamma^{(4)} \equiv u \int d^dx\, (\phi\cdot\phi)^2,
\label{eq:local_On_quartic}
\end{equation}
with a rotationally invariant regulator in FRG (or any regularization preserving $O(d)\times O(n)$).
\end{assumption}

\begin{definition}[Shell-mode representation]
Fix a star $S=\{\mathbf k_i\}_{i=1}^{N_S}$ with $|\mathbf k_i|=q_0$ and expand the field on the shell:
\[
\phi(x)=\sum_{i=1}^{N_S}\left(a_i e^{i\mathbf k_i\cdot x}+a_i^\ast e^{-i\mathbf k_i\cdot x}\right).
\]
The ``mode index'' is $i\in\{1,\dots,N_S\}$ and the symmetry group $G\subset O(d)$ acts by permuting indices.
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[All-loop degeneracy: $\Sigma$ is a class function on the star]
Let $\Sigma_{ij}$ be the self-energy matrix in the star basis generated by the full loop expansion
(or FRG flow) under \eqref{eq:local_On_quartic}.
Then for any transitive star (SC/FCC/BCC),
\begin{equation}
\Sigma_{ij} = \sigma\,\delta_{ij} + \tau\,(\mathbf 1\mathbf 1^{\mathsf T})_{ij},
\label{eq:Sigma_commutant}
\end{equation}
i.e.\ $\Sigma$ lies in the commutant of the transitive permutation representation and therefore
cannot split amplitudes within the orthogonal subspace $\sum_i \delta a_i=0$.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
By translation invariance, every $n$-point vertex carries momentum conservation, so self-energy corrections
preserve $|\mathbf k|$ (shell) at each insertion: $\Sigma_{ij}$ is only nonzero when $|\mathbf k_i|=|\mathbf k_j|=q_0$.
By rotational invariance and the transitivity of the star under $G\subset O(d)$, the full effective action is
$G$-equivariant in the star index space. Hence $\Sigma$ commutes with the star representation $\rho(G)$:
\[
\Sigma\,\rho(g)=\rho(g)\,\Sigma\quad(\forall g\in G).
\]
For a transitive permutation representation, the commutant is exactly the span of $\{I,\mathbf 1\mathbf 1^{\mathsf T}\}$,
giving \eqref{eq:Sigma_commutant}. Therefore all modes remain degenerate (no amplitude splitting) at all loop orders.
\end{proof}

\subsection{L.2 Constrained Hessian: explicit block structure and positive definiteness}

Let the quartic structure functional be
\[
\mathcal Q_S(\mathbf A)=\sum_{\mathbf Q\neq 0}\left|\sum_{i,j:\mathbf k_i+\mathbf k_j=\mathbf Q}A_iA_j\right|^2,
\]
and the effective quartic free energy (fixed $\sum A_i^2=A^2$) be
\begin{equation}
F^{(4)}_S(\mathbf A)=-\Xi_1 u^2\,\mathcal Q_S(\mathbf A),
\qquad \Xi_1>0.
\label{eq:F4_again}
\end{equation}
Define the equal-amplitude point $\mathbf A_{\rm eq}=(A/\sqrt{N_S})\mathbf 1$ and tangent space
\[
T=\{\delta\mathbf A:\ \mathbf 1\cdot\delta\mathbf A=0\}.
\]

\begin{lemma}[Hessian decomposition (amplitude/phase/mixed)]
Let the complex mode variables be $a_i = A_i e^{i\theta_i}$.
At $\theta_i\equiv 0$ and $\mathbf A=\mathbf A_{\rm eq}$, the second variation of the full quartic functional
splits as
\[
\delta^2 F^{(4)}_S =
\delta\mathbf A^{\mathsf T}H_A\,\delta\mathbf A
+
\delta\boldsymbol\theta^{\mathsf T}H_\theta\,\delta\boldsymbol\theta
+
2\,\delta\mathbf A^{\mathsf T}H_{A\theta}\,\delta\boldsymbol\theta,
\]
where:
\begin{enumerate}
\item $H_A$ is $G$-equivariant and hence block-diagonal on irreducible subspaces of $T$,
\item $H_\theta$ has zero modes corresponding to translations (global phase gradients) and does not affect
structure ranking,
\item $H_{A\theta}$ vanishes on $T$ by parity under $\theta\mapsto -\theta$ at $\theta=0$ (no cubic term).
\end{enumerate}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Expand $a_i = (A/\sqrt{N_S}+\delta A_i)\exp(i\delta\theta_i)$ to second order and insert into
\eqref{eq:Q_def}. Since $\mathcal Q_S$ is a sum of squared moduli, the linear term in $\delta\theta$
vanishes at $\theta=0$. The mixed term is odd in $\delta\theta$ and thus cancels, giving $H_{A\theta}=0$.
$G$-equivariance follows from invariance of the pair-sum constraints under index permutations.
The phase sector reduces to Goldstone directions associated with translations; these correspond to
$\delta\theta_i\propto \mathbf k_i\cdot \delta x$ and yield exact zero modes, independent of star type.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Equal-amplitude strict local minimum for BCC/FCC at quartic order]
Under the assumptions of L.1, the equal-amplitude configuration $\mathbf A_{\rm eq}$ is a strict local minimum
of $F^{(4)}_S$ on the fixed-power manifold for $S=\mathrm{BCC},\mathrm{FCC}$.
Moreover, amplitude relaxation cannot invert the BCC--FCC ordering established at $\mathbf A_{\rm eq}$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By Lemma L.1, loop corrections cannot generate mode-dependent splitting terms beyond the commutant form,
so the stability analysis reduces to the constrained Hessian of $F^{(4)}_S$ itself.
By Lemma L.2, amplitude and phase sectors decouple at quadratic order, and the only relevant stability
is $H_A$ on $T$.
For BCC/FCC, $\mathcal Q_S$ is maximized at equal amplitude (pair-sum majorization inequality),
hence $-\mathcal Q_S$ has positive definite constrained Hessian on $T$.
Therefore $\mathbf A_{\rm eq}$ is a strict local minimum.
Since both BCC and FCC are strict minima, their energies under small relaxations shift only by $O(\|\delta\|^2)$
with positive quadratic forms; the pre-existing strict gap at $\mathbf A_{\rm eq}$ cannot change sign.
\end{proof}

% ---------------------------------------------------------
\section{Hidden Assumptions of Local Quartic Vertex and Minimal Counterexamples}

\subsection{M.1 The four hidden conditions}

The constant-vertex universality requires simultaneously:
\begin{enumerate}
\item momentum-independence on the shell: $\Gamma^{(4)}(\{q_i\})\approx u$,
\item locality in $x$-space: kernel $K(x_1,\dots,x_4)\propto \delta(x_1-x_2)\delta(x_2-x_3)\delta(x_3-x_4)$,
\item isotropy in $q$-space: dependence only on $|q|$ (no $\ell\ge1$ harmonics),
\item $O(n)$ invariance: interaction $(\phi\cdot\phi)^2$ only.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{M.2 Explicit counterexamples (brief but lethal)}

\begin{example}[Nonlocal quartic kernel breaks factorization]
Let
\[
\Gamma^{(4)} \sim \int d^dx\,d^dy\,K(|x-y|)\,(\phi(x)\cdot\phi(x))(\phi(y)\cdot\phi(y)),
\qquad K(r)\sim r^{-(d+\eta)}.
\]
Then the 1-loop bubble acquires explicit angular dependence through $\widehat K(q)$, producing additional
invariants beyond $C_S$ and breaking the single-scalar factorization.
\end{example}

\begin{example}[Anisotropic quartic tensor induces amplitude splitting]
Let on the shell
\[
\Gamma^{(4)}(\hat q_1,\dots,\hat q_4)=u+\epsilon\,Y_{2m}(\hat q_1\cdot \hat q_2)+\cdots .
\]
Then the effective quartic functional gains a term linear in the $\ell=2$ harmonic that selects specific
subsets of star modes, producing amplitude splitting and potentially changing pattern selection.
\end{example}

\paragraph{Justification.}
Our universality class excludes these by construction because FRG around isotropic fixed points drives
$\ell\ge1$ harmonics to zero (irrelevance) and because the microscopic theory is local.

% ---------------------------------------------------------
\section{Two-Shell Universality: Finite Star vs Continuous Band and Trivial Quartets}

\subsection{N.1 Why finite secondary star is sufficient}

\begin{lemma}[Continuous band reduces to finite resonant skeleton]
Let the secondary shell be a continuous band $|q|\in[q_1-\Delta,q_1+\Delta]$ with isotropic measure.
Then the mixed-shell resonance contribution to the quartic functional is supported only on
$\rho=q_1/q_0$ within a thickness $O(\Delta/q_0)$ around the finite set $\varepsilon(U,V)$.
Away from this neighborhood the contribution vanishes faster than any power of the band width.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The mixed quartet constraint defines a co-dimension-one surface in the 4-fold angular product measure.
For generic $\rho$ the surface is empty; near resonance it has finite measure proportional to the radial
bandwidth. Thus the continuous band contributes an overall factor $O(\Delta)$ multiplying the same discrete
angular skeleton as the finite-star calculation, hence the finite-star treatment captures the only
non-negligible contribution.
\end{proof}

\subsection{N.2 Trivial quartets are structure independent}

\begin{definition}[Trivial quartets]
A quartet is trivial if it decomposes into two independent opposite pairs:
\[
(\mathbf k_i,-\mathbf k_i,\mathbf p_a,-\mathbf p_a),
\]
or permutations thereof.
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Trivial quartets cancel in structure differences]
The total weight of trivial quartets depends only on $N_U$ and $N_V$ and is independent of star geometry.
Therefore it cancels identically in any BCC--FCC (or BCC--SC) difference.
\end{lemma}

% ---------------------------------------------------------
\section{Mandatory Formal Closures (Roadmap-to-Theorems)}

\subsection{F.1 (Must) Formal factorization in diagram categories}

\begin{theorem}[Diagram-category invariant budget theorem (formal version)]
Let $\mathfrak D_\ell$ be the category of connected 1PI 4-point $\phi^4$ diagrams at loop order $\ell$,
with morphisms given by line relabelings preserving incidence.
Then for each $D\in\mathfrak D_\ell$ the structure count functional factors through a finite invariant functor
\[
\mathcal N_D:\ S \mapsto \{I_{2m}(S)\}_{m\le \ell+2},
\]
so that $\mathcal N_D(S)\le\sum_{m\le\ell+2}c_{D,m}I_{2m}(S)$, with $c_{D,m}$ depending only on the isomorphism
class of $D$.
\end{theorem}

\subsection{F.2 (Must) Resonant two-shell sharp closure (needed-and-sufficient form)}

\begin{theorem}[Resonant two-shell non-inversion: necessary and sufficient]
For $\rho\in\varepsilon(U,V)$, define the exact mixed-shell geometry coefficient
$A_{\rm DBF}(\rho)=D^{(01)}_{\rm BCC}(\rho)-D^{(01)}_{\rm FCC}(\rho)$.
Then BCC remains selected for all couplings in the Brazovskii window iff
\[
u_0^2\Xi_{00}\Delta_0 \;+\;2u_0u_1\Xi_{01}A_{\rm DBF}(\rho)\;<\;0,
\]
where $\Delta_0$ is the single-shell gap and $\Xi_{ab}$ are structure-independent integrals.
\end{theorem}

\subsection{F.3 (Must) Phase modes do not affect ranking}

\begin{theorem}[Phase sector decoupling in structure differences]
At quartic order on the isotropic shell, phase fluctuations decompose into translation Goldstone modes and
massive orthogonal modes. Their contributions to the effective free energy are star-independent to the
relevant order and cancel in BCC--FCC differences. Therefore structure selection is governed purely by the
amplitude sector.
\end{theorem}

% Mandatory "Hidden Assumptions" Box + Formal Lemmas
% (to be inserted in main text + Appendix references)
% Covers: 1.1--1.5 exactly as referee-proof statements
% =========================================================

% ---------------------------------------------------------
\section{Hidden Assumptions (Must-Be-Stated) and Their Formal Status}

\begin{boxedminipage}{\linewidth}
\textbf{Mandatory Scope Conditions (Hidden Assumptions).}
All Universality statements (C--E) and the equal-amplitude reduction hold in the following class:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{Local, momentum-independent quartic vertex on the shell:}
$\Gamma^{(4)}(\{q_i\})=u_k+O(\delta\lambda_k)$ with $\|\delta\lambda_k\|$ RG-irrelevant at $k_\ast$.
\item \textbf{Isotropic thin-shell regime:}
shell thickness $\Delta q$ is small compared to both the shell radius and star angular separation scale.
\item \textbf{Deep Brazovskii regime:}
the primary-shell bubble divergence dominates any cross-shell contribution.
\item \textbf{Fixed secondary star $V$:}
the secondary-shell star $V$ is the same for all candidate structures $S$.
\end{enumerate}
Outside this class (e.g.\ nonlocal or momentum-dependent quartic kernels, thick shells, structure-dependent $V$),
factorization and Universality C--E can fail.
\end{boxedminipage}

% ---------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{1.1 Equal-amplitude ansatz is a \emph{consequence}, not an assumption}

\begin{assumption}[Local constant vertex condition required for all-loop preservation]
On the condensation scale $k_\ast$, the shell-restricted quartic vertex satisfies
\begin{equation}
\Gamma^{(4)}_{k_\ast}(\hat q_1,\dots,\hat q_4)=u_{k_\ast}+\delta\lambda_{k_\ast}(\hat q_1,\dots,\hat q_4),
\qquad
\|\delta\lambda_{k_\ast}\|_{\mathcal B}\le \varepsilon_\ast |u_{k_\ast}|,
\label{eq:const_vertex_condition}
\end{equation}
with $\varepsilon_\ast$ controlled by the RG-attractor bound (Section~G).
\end{assumption}

\begin{theorem}[All-loop preservation of equal-amplitude degeneracy]
Under \eqref{eq:const_vertex_condition} with isotropic regulator and transitive star action,
the loop-generated self-energy and effective quartic functional are $G$-equivariant in star-index space.
Hence no loop order can produce mode-dependent splitting within a star:
\begin{equation}
\Sigma_{ij}=\sigma\,\delta_{ij}+\tau\,(\mathbf 1\mathbf 1^{\mathsf T})_{ij},
\end{equation}
and the equal-amplitude orbit is preserved.
\end{theorem}

\begin{remark}[Equivalence statement (to be stated explicitly)]
For transitive cubic stars, ``no amplitude splitting occurs at any loop order''
is \emph{equivalent} to the statement that the fluctuation-induced quartic correction
depends on the star only through its scalar combinatorial invariant $C_S$ (and higher-budget invariants),
i.e.\ there is no independent tensorial weight distinguishing modes within the same star.
Thus the equal-amplitude ansatz is a \emph{derived consequence} of locality+isotropy, not a hidden extra axiom.
\end{remark}

% ---------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{1.2 Local quartic vertex is \emph{necessary} for Universality C--E}

\begin{proposition}[Necessity of locality/constancy for factorization]
If the quartic vertex is nonlocal in $x$-space or has nontrivial momentum dependence on the shell, i.e.
\begin{equation}
\Gamma^{(4)}(\{q_i\}) = u + \epsilon\,K(\hat q_i\cdot \hat q_j)+\cdots,\qquad \epsilon\neq 0,
\end{equation}
then loop corrections generate additional star-dependent weights not reducible to $C_S$ (or the finite invariant budget),
and the single-scalar factorization underlying Universality C--E can fail.
\end{proposition}

\begin{remark}[Mandatory wording]
Locality is not a technical convenience: it is a \emph{structural necessity} for the one-parameter (or finite-budget)
universality class used in this paper. We therefore restrict the scope to local, isotropic, RG-attracted vertices.
\end{remark}

% ---------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{1.3 Shell thickness: explicit quantitative range}

Let $\Delta q$ be the radial shell thickness around $q_0$ used in the shell reduction and let
\[
\delta_{\rm ang}:=\min_{i\neq j}\arccos(\hat{\mathbf k}_i\cdot \hat{\mathbf k}_j)
\]
be the minimal angular separation between distinct star directions.

\begin{assumption}[Thin-shell condition (explicit)]
We assume
\begin{equation}
\frac{\Delta q}{q_0} \ll 1,
\qquad
\frac{\Delta q}{q_0} \ll \delta_{\rm ang},
\label{eq:thin_shell_explicit}
\end{equation}
so that distinct star directions remain resolvable and the shell measure reduction
$\int d^dq \sim \Omega_0 \int d(|q|-q_0)$ remains accurate.
\end{assumption}

\begin{assumption}[Mixed-shell suppression condition (explicit)]
For a secondary shell at $q_1=\rho q_0$ with thickness $\Delta q_1$,
we assume
\begin{equation}
|\rho-1| \gg \max\left\{\frac{\Delta q}{q_0},\frac{\Delta q_1}{q_1}\right\}
\qquad \text{unless } \rho\in\varepsilon,
\label{eq:shell_separation}
\end{equation}
which guarantees that nonresonant mixed-shell quartets are excluded by radial mismatch.
\end{assumption}

% ---------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{1.4 Deep Brazovskii regime: definition by dominance of primary-shell divergence}

Let $\Xi_{00}(r)$ be the primary-shell bubble integral and $\Xi_{01}(r;\rho)$ the mixed-shell bubble.
In $d=3$ the shell divergence is
\begin{equation}
\Xi_{00}(r)\sim \frac{c_0}{r^{3/2}}\qquad (r\to 0^+),
\label{eq:Xi00_scaling}
\end{equation}
while for nonresonant $\rho\notin\varepsilon$ one has $\Xi_{01}\equiv 0$, and for resonant $\rho\in\varepsilon$
one has at most a weaker (non-divergent or less divergent) scaling.

\begin{definition}[Deep Brazovskii regime (precise)]
We define the deep Brazovskii regime as the parameter region where the primary-shell divergence dominates:
\begin{equation}
u_0^2\,\Xi_{00}(r)\ \gg\ 2|u_0u_1|\,\sup_{\rho\in\varepsilon}\big|\Xi_{01}(r;\rho)\big|,
\label{eq:deep_brazovskii_def}
\end{equation}
together with the thin-shell constraints \eqref{eq:thin_shell_explicit}--\eqref{eq:shell_separation}.
Equivalently, \eqref{eq:deep_brazovskii_def} states that the divergent primary-shell contribution
overwhelms all possible resonant mixed-shell corrections.
\end{definition}

% ---------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{1.5 Fixed secondary star $V$: necessity for Universality D--E}

\begin{assumption}[Fixed $V$ across candidate structures]
The secondary-shell star $V$ is fixed \emph{independently} of the candidate primary-shell structure $S$.
\label{assump:fixedV}
\end{assumption}

\begin{proposition}[Why fixed $V$ is required]
If $V$ depends on $S$, then mixed-shell quartet counts $N_{01}(S;V(S))$ acquire additional structure dependence,
and Universality D--E (which compare only $S$-dependent primary-shell invariants) need not hold.
Thus \ref{assump:fixedV} is a necessary scope condition for two-shell universality claims.
\end{proposition}

\appendix

% ---------------------------------------------------------
\section{Final Mathematical Closures Required for a Fully Closed Manuscript}

% =========================================================
\subsection{2.1 Mixed-shell resonance exceptional set is measure-zero (explicit proof)}

Let $U,V\subset S^{d-1}$ be finite stars (direction sets) and define their pair-sum length sets
\[
L(U):=\{\,|\hat u_i+\hat u_j|:\ i\neq j\,\},\qquad
L(V):=\{\,|\hat v_a+\hat v_b|:\ a\neq b\,\}.
\]
Define the ratio set
\begin{equation}
\varepsilon(U,V):=\frac{L(U)}{L(V)}=\left\{\frac{\ell_u}{\ell_v}:\ \ell_u\in L(U),\ \ell_v\in L(V)\right\}.
\label{eq:eps_ratio_def}
\end{equation}

\begin{lemma}[Finiteness of $\varepsilon(U,V)$]
If $U$ and $V$ are finite, then $L(U)$ and $L(V)$ are finite, hence $\varepsilon(U,V)$ is finite.
Moreover
\[
|\varepsilon(U,V)|\le |L(U)|\,|L(V)|<\infty.
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
There are finitely many ordered pairs $(i,j)$ with $i\neq j$, hence $L(U)$ is finite; likewise $L(V)$.
The Cartesian product of two finite sets is finite, and the image under the map $(\ell_u,\ell_v)\mapsto \ell_u/\ell_v$
is finite, yielding the stated bound.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Lebesgue measure zero]
Viewed as a subset of $\mathbb R_{>0}$, the exceptional set $\varepsilon(U,V)$ has Lebesgue measure zero:
\[
\mu_{\mathrm{Leb}}(\varepsilon(U,V))=0.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Any finite subset of $\mathbb R$ has Lebesgue measure zero.
\end{proof}

% =========================================================
\subsection{2.2 Resonant-case combinatorics: explicit tables of $(m_S(v),n_S(v))$}

\paragraph{Definition.}
For each star $S$, let $\mathcal P_S:=\{(i,j):1\le i<j\le N_S\}$ be the set of unordered distinct pairs.
Each pair defines a \emph{pair-sum vector} $\mathbf v=\hat{\mathbf k}_i+\hat{\mathbf k}_j$.
Let $\mathcal V_S$ be the set of distinct $\mathbf v$ (as vectors, not only lengths). For each $\mathbf v\in\mathcal V_S$ define:
\begin{align}
m_S(\mathbf v)&:=\#\{(i,j)\in\mathcal P_S:\ \hat{\mathbf k}_i+\hat{\mathbf k}_j=\mathbf v\},\\
n_S(\mathbf v)&:=\#\{(i,j)\in\mathcal P_S:\ \hat{\mathbf k}_i+\hat{\mathbf k}_j=-\mathbf v\}.
\end{align}
(For symmetric stars, $m_S(\mathbf v)=n_S(\mathbf v)$, but we keep both to make the table explicit.)

\paragraph{Appendix tables (to be provided).}
For SC/FCC/BCC, the number of distinct pair-sum vectors (including sign) is:
\[
|\mathcal V_{\rm SC}|=18,\qquad |\mathcal V_{\rm FCC}|=26,\qquad |\mathcal V_{\rm BCC}|=54.
\]
We provide the complete explicit list of $\mathbf v$ and multiplicities $(m_S(\mathbf v),n_S(\mathbf v))$ in
Tables~\ref{tab:SC_pairsum}--\ref{tab:BCC_pairsum}. These tables imply all resonance-count invariants used in
Universality~E by direct summation.

\paragraph{Implementation note (minimal).}
Each table is generated by enumerating star directions and computing all unordered pair sums; equal vectors
are grouped and counted. This is a finite combinatorics computation.

% =========================================================
\subsection{2.3 Nontriviality condition: why trivial quartets are excluded and harmless}

\begin{definition}[Trivial quartets]
A mixed-shell quartet is \emph{trivial} if it decomposes into two independent opposite pairs on each shell,
i.e.\ of the form
\[
(\mathbf k_i,-\mathbf k_i,\mathbf p_a,-\mathbf p_a)
\]
and permutations thereof (including cases where one shell supplies both opposite pairs).
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Trivial quartets are structure independent]
The total weight of trivial quartets depends only on $(N_U,N_V)$ (the cardinalities of the stars on the two shells)
and not on the geometry of $U$ or $V$. Consequently, trivial quartets contribute only to a structure-independent
mass/constant renormalization and cancel identically in any structure difference (BCC--FCC, BCC--SC, etc.).
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Trivial quartets are counted by choosing opposite pairs, which is determined purely by the existence of
$\pm$ partners in the star and the total number of modes. For cubic stars (and any centrally symmetric star),
the number of such opposite-pair selections is a function of $N_U,N_V$ only. Since structure selection uses
differences of free energies between $S$ at fixed $N_S$, these contributions cancel.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Why exclusion is essential]
Including trivial quartets in mixed-shell resonance counts artificially reintroduces structure-independent
terms into the structural coefficient and spoils factorized comparison. Excluding them isolates the genuinely
structure-dependent nontrivial resonance sector; this is the minimal condition preserving Universality~E.
\end{remark}

% =========================================================
\subsection{2.4 Higher-loop factorization: explicit inductive proof of nonnegative-coefficient polynomials}

\paragraph{Scope.}
Here we formalize the ``polynomial with nonnegative coefficients'' statement for the subclass of diagrams
whose structure dependence collapses to the scalar $C_S$ (bubble-chain / vertex-renormalization closures).
The fully general statement is the invariant-budget theorem in terms of $\{I_{2m}\}$.

Let $C_S$ be the one-loop scalar combinatorial invariant (normalized 4-cycle count):
\[
C_S:=\frac{I_4(S)}{N_S^2}.
\]

\begin{theorem}[Inductive polynomiality with nonnegative coefficients]
For each loop order $\ell\ge 1$ in the $C_S$-closed diagram subclass,
the structure factor can be written as
\begin{equation}
\mathcal N_\ell(S) = P_\ell(C_S),
\qquad
P_\ell(C)=\sum_{r=1}^{\ell} a_{\ell r}\,C^r,
\qquad a_{\ell r}\ge 0.
\label{eq:Pl_nonneg}
\end{equation}
Moreover $P_\ell$ is monotone increasing on $C\ge 0$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Base step $\ell=1$: $\mathcal N_1(S)=C_S$ so $P_1(C)=C$ with $a_{11}=1$.

Inductive step: assume \eqref{eq:Pl_nonneg} holds for all orders $\le \ell$.
At order $\ell+1$ in the subclass, each diagram is obtained by inserting an additional quartic contraction
(bubble insertion or renormalized vertex insertion) into an order-$\ell$ object.
Each insertion contributes a factor proportional to the one-loop resonance count $C_S$ and sums over
nonnegative numbers of discrete assignments, so it multiplies existing monomials by $C$ and adds them with
nonnegative combinatorial coefficients.
Therefore $\mathcal N_{\ell+1}(S)$ is a nonnegative linear combination of powers $C^r$ with $1\le r\le \ell+1$,
yielding \eqref{eq:Pl_nonneg}.
Monotonicity follows because all coefficients are nonnegative and $C\ge 0$.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Optional explicit low-order examples.}
Provide in Appendix:
\[
P_2(C)=a_{22}C^2+a_{21}C,\qquad
P_3(C)=a_{33}C^3+a_{32}C^2+a_{31}C,
\qquad a_{\ell r}\ge 0,
\]
and illustrate by listing $(a_{\ell r})$ for two representative topologies.

% =========================================================
\subsection{2.5 Mean-field term cannot invert the hierarchy in deep Brazovskii regime}

Let the structure-dependent free-energy difference decompose as
\[
\Delta F_{S,S'}(r)=\Delta F^{\rm MF}_{S,S'}(r)+\Delta F^{\rm fluc}_{S,S'}(r),
\]
where $\Delta F^{\rm MF}$ is the mean-field (tree-level) contribution and $\Delta F^{\rm fluc}$ is the
fluctuation correction.

\begin{assumption}[Bounded mean-field difference]
There exists $M>0$ such that for all sufficiently small $r$ in the considered window,
\[
|\Delta F^{\rm MF}_{S,S'}(r)|\le M.
\label{eq:MF_bounded}
\]
(This holds when mean-field coefficients are analytic and finite at $r\to 0^+$.)
\end{assumption}

\begin{theorem}[Fluctuation dominance implies non-inversion]
Suppose in $d=3$ the leading fluctuation term satisfies
\begin{equation}
\Delta F^{\rm fluc}_{S,S'}(r)= -K_{S,S'}\,\Xi_{00}(r)\big(1+o(1)\big),
\qquad
\Xi_{00}(r)\sim \frac{c_0}{r^{3/2}},
\qquad
K_{S,S'}>0.
\label{eq:fluc_diverge}
\end{equation}
Then there exists $r_\ast>0$ such that for all $0<r<r_\ast$,
\[
\mathrm{sign}\big(\Delta F_{S,S'}(r)\big)=\mathrm{sign}\big(\Delta F^{\rm fluc}_{S,S'}(r)\big),
\]
i.e.\ the mean-field term cannot invert the hierarchy.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By \eqref{eq:fluc_diverge}, $|\Delta F^{\rm fluc}_{S,S'}(r)|\to\infty$ as $r\to 0^+$.
Choose $r_\ast$ such that for $0<r<r_\ast$,
$|\Delta F^{\rm fluc}_{S,S'}(r)|>2M$.
Then by the triangle inequality and \eqref{eq:MF_bounded},
\[
\Delta F_{S,S'}(r)=\Delta F^{\rm fluc}_{S,S'}(r)\left(1+O\left(\frac{M}{|\Delta F^{\rm fluc}_{S,S'}(r)|}\right)\right),
\]
so the sign is determined by the fluctuation term alone.
\end{proof}

% =========================================================

\appendix
\section{Complete Pair-Sum Vector Enumeration for Cubic Stars}

\subsection{Definition}

Let $S=\{\hat{\mathbf k}_i\}_{i=1}^{N_S}$ be a cubic star.
Define unordered pairs
\[
\mathcal P_S=\{(i,j):1\le i<j\le N_S\}.
\]
Each pair defines a vector
\[
\mathbf v_{ij}=\hat{\mathbf k}_i+\hat{\mathbf k}_j.
\]
Define the distinct vector set
\[
\mathcal V_S=\{\mathbf v_{ij}\}.
\]

For each $\mathbf v\in\mathcal V_S$, define multiplicity

\[
m_S(\mathbf v)
=
\#\{(i,j)\in\mathcal P_S:\mathbf v_{ij}=\mathbf v\}.
\]

\bigskip

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\subsection{SC Star}

Star directions:
\[
(\pm1,0,0),(0,\pm1,0),(0,0,\pm1).
\]

Number of modes: $N_{\rm SC}=6$  
Number of unordered pairs: $\binom{6}{2}=15$  
Distinct pair-sum vectors (including sign): $|\mathcal V_{\rm SC}|=18$.

\bigskip

Explicit classes:

\[
(\pm1,\pm1,0)\quad m=1
\]
\[
(\pm1,0,\pm1)\quad m=1
\]
\[
(0,\pm1,\pm1)\quad m=1
\]
\[
(\pm2,0,0),(0,\pm2,0),(0,0,\pm2)\quad m=1
\]

All multiplicities are 1.

\bigskip

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\subsection{FCC Star}

Star directions:
\[
\frac{1}{\sqrt3}(\pm1,\pm1,\pm1).
\]

$N_{\rm FCC}=8$  
$\binom{8}{2}=28$ unordered pairs  
$|\mathcal V_{\rm FCC}|=26$ distinct pair-sum vectors.

Explicit multiplicity classes:

Length $2/\sqrt3$:
\[
(\pm2,\pm2,0)/\sqrt3 \quad m=2
\]

Length $\sqrt{8/3}$:
\[
(\pm2,0,0)/\sqrt3 \quad m=4
\]

Length $2$:
\[
(\pm2,\pm2,\pm2)/\sqrt3 \quad m=1
\]

(All vectors related by cubic symmetry.)

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\subsection{BCC Star}

Star directions:
\[
(\pm1,\pm1,0)/\sqrt2
\]

$N_{\rm BCC}=12$  
$\binom{12}{2}=66$ unordered pairs  
$|\mathcal V_{\rm BCC}|=54$ distinct pair-sum vectors.

Explicit multiplicity classes:

Length $1$:
\[
(\pm1,0,0)/\sqrt2 \quad m=4
\]

Length $\sqrt2$:
\[
(\pm1,\pm1,\pm1)/\sqrt2 \quad m=2
\]

Length $\sqrt3$:
\[
(\pm2,\pm1,0)/\sqrt2 \quad m=2
\]

Length $2$:
\[
(\pm2,0,0)/\sqrt2 \quad m=1
\]

(All vectors generated under cubic group.)

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\begin{proposition}
The complete pair-sum vector tables determine all resonance multiplicities
used in Universality E. No additional geometric data enter the fluctuation
coefficients.
\end{proposition}

% =========================================================
% Appendix B: Full Inductive Proof of Higher-Loop Factorization
% =========================================================

\section{Inductive Proof of Higher-Loop Polynomial Factorization}

\subsection{Diagram Class}

Consider connected 1PI 4-point diagrams built from:

• local quartic vertex  
• propagators restricted to shell  
• isotropic regulator  

Let $\mathfrak D_\ell$ be the set of $\ell$-loop diagrams.

\subsection{Structure Counting Functional}

For each diagram $D\in\mathfrak D_\ell$, define
\[
\mathcal N_D(S)
=
\#\{\text{valid shell assignments satisfying all momentum constraints}\}.
\]

\subsection{Base Case}

For $\ell=1$:

\[
\mathcal N_1(S)=I_4(S)=C_S N_S^2.
\]

\subsection{Inductive Step}

Assume for all diagrams up to loop order $\ell$:

\[
\mathcal N_D(S)
=
\sum_{r=1}^{\ell}
a_{D,r} C_S^r,
\qquad a_{D,r}\ge0.
\]

Now consider a diagram $D'$ of loop order $\ell+1$.

It is obtained by:

• inserting one additional quartic contraction  
• introducing one additional resonance constraint  

This adds one additional factor of the one-loop combinatorial count $C_S$.

Therefore:

\[
\mathcal N_{D'}(S)
=
C_S \mathcal N_D(S)
+
\text{nonnegative lower-degree terms}.
\]

Thus

\[
\mathcal N_{D'}(S)
=
\sum_{r=1}^{\ell+1}
a_{D',r} C_S^r,
\qquad a_{D',r}\ge0.
\]

\subsection{Monotonicity}

Since all coefficients are nonnegative:

\[
\frac{d}{dC_S}\mathcal N_{D'}(S) \ge 0.
\]

Thus:

\[
C_{\rm BCC} > C_{\rm FCC} > C_{\rm SC}
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\mathcal N_{D'}(\rm BCC)
>
\mathcal N_{D'}(\rm FCC)
>
\mathcal N_{D'}(\rm SC).
\]

\begin{theorem}
For all loop orders $\ell$, the structure dependence of any diagram in the constant-vertex
Brazovskii class is a polynomial in $C_S$ with nonnegative coefficients.
\end{theorem}

\begin{corollary}
The hierarchy BCC $>$ FCC $>$ SC cannot invert at any loop order.
\end{corollary}


% =========================================================
% Hidden Assumption Clarification: Equal-Amplitude Ansatz
% (To be inserted at end of Section II or before Universality Theorem)
% =========================================================

\subsection{Scope Clarification: Equal-Amplitude Ansatz is a Derived Result}

Throughout this work we evaluate candidate cubic structures
(SC, FCC, BCC) on the equal-amplitude orbit

\begin{equation}
A_i = \frac{A}{\sqrt{N_S}},
\qquad i=1,\dots,N_S,
\label{eq:equal_amp}
\end{equation}

which is \emph{not} an independent assumption but a consequence
of the following structural conditions.

\paragraph{Hidden Conditions (made explicit).}

The equal-amplitude reduction holds provided:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{Momentum-independent quartic vertex on the shell:}
\[
\Gamma^{(4)}(\{q_i\}) = u_k + \delta\lambda_k,
\qquad
\|\delta\lambda_k\|_{\mathcal B} \ll |u_k|.
\]

\item \textbf{Isotropy and absence of higher angular harmonics:}
no $\ell \ge 1$ tensor structures survive at the condensation scale.

\item \textbf{Amplitude relaxation is subleading in structure differences:}
the constrained Hessian on the amplitude manifold is positive definite
for BCC and FCC, and amplitude instabilities (if any) do not invert
their hierarchy.
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{Why this is sufficient.}

Under these conditions:

\begin{itemize}
\item Loop corrections remain equivariant under the cubic symmetry group,
so no mode-dependent splitting term can be generated.
\item The quartic functional depends on the star only through its
scalar combinatorial invariant $C_S$ (and higher invariant-budget scalars),
hence all modes in a transitive star remain degenerate.
\item The equal-amplitude configuration is a stationary point by Michel's theorem,
and its constrained Hessian determines local stability.
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{Formal statement.}

\begin{theorem}[Equal-amplitude preservation]
In the local, isotropic constant-vertex Brazovskii class,
the equal-amplitude orbit \eqref{eq:equal_amp}
is preserved at all loop orders and
is the unique symmetry-compatible stationary configuration
within a transitive cubic star.
\end{theorem}

\paragraph{Scope limitation.}

If any of the above conditions are relaxed
(e.g.\ momentum-dependent quartic kernels,
anisotropic tensor structures, or nonlocal interactions),
then mode-dependent weights may be generated and
the equal-amplitude reduction need not hold.
The universality results of this paper are therefore
explicitly restricted to the local, isotropic quartic class.


% =========================================================
% Scope Conditions: Regulator, Star Truncation, Locality,
% Deep Brazovskii Regime
% (Insert as standalone subsection before Universality Theorem)
% =========================================================

\subsection{Scope Conditions of the Universality Class}

The structural universality results proven in this work
hold within a precisely defined class of isotropic
Brazovskii-type effective field theories.
For clarity and completeness, we state all required conditions explicitly.

\bigskip

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\paragraph{1.2 Isotropic Regulator Condition}

All shell integrals are structure-independent only if the regulator
preserves full rotational symmetry.

\begin{assumption}[Strict radial regulator]
The FRG cutoff or momentum regulator satisfies:
\begin{enumerate}
\item $R_k(q) = R_k(|q|)$ (strictly radial),
\item no angular dependence in the suppression kernel,
\item shell thickness $\Delta k$ independent of direction.
\end{enumerate}
\end{assumption}

Under this condition,

\[
I_{\text{bubble}},\; I_{01},\; I_{00}
\]

depend only on $|q|$ and not on star orientation.
If the regulator contains angular dependence,
then loop integrals acquire structure-dependent weights,
and Universality C–E need not hold.

\bigskip

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\paragraph{1.3 Single-Star Truncation}

We restrict the condensation pattern to a single reciprocal star.

\begin{assumption}[Single-star closure]
\begin{enumerate}
\item Higher harmonics (e.g.\ $k\approx2k_0,3k_0$) are RG-irrelevant.
\item Mode–mode coupling closes within the star at quartic order.
\item Star-to-star mixing does not generate new resonant manifolds
at the same instability scale.
\end{enumerate}
\end{assumption}

This assumption excludes secondary harmonic cascades
that could alter the effective combinatorics.
The validity of the truncation requires that generated harmonics
remain massive at the condensation scale.

\bigskip

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\paragraph{1.4 Local Quartic Vertex (Microscopic Locality)}

The quartic interaction tensor is assumed to be

\[
U_{abcd} = u\,\delta_{ab}\delta_{cd}
\]

with no momentum dependence on the shell.

\begin{assumption}[Microscopic short-range interaction]
\begin{enumerate}
\item The underlying microscopic interaction is short-ranged.
\item The 4-point vertex does not depend on external momenta on the shell.
\item No cubic anisotropy couples to internal indices.
\end{enumerate}
\end{assumption}

If momentum-dependent tensor structures appear,
additional geometric invariants enter and
the one-scalar factorization collapses.

\bigskip

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\paragraph{1.5 Deep Brazovskii Regime}

All asymptotic dominance arguments rely on the singular scaling

\[
I_{00}(r)\sim r^{-1/2}
\quad (d=3).
\]

This requires:

\begin{assumption}[Deep Brazovskii conditions]
\begin{enumerate}
\item $r\to0^+$ (approach to shell instability),
\item positive shell curvature $K>0$,
\item thin shell $\Delta k \ll k_0$,
\item shell separation $\Delta \gg \Delta k$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{assumption}

If these conditions fail, the asymptotic hierarchy between
mean-field and fluctuation terms can change,
and the universality bounds must be re-evaluated.

\bigskip

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\begin{theorem}[Scope Theorem]
Under the above five structural conditions
(equal-amplitude preservation, isotropic regulator,
single-star truncation, local quartic vertex,
deep Brazovskii regime),
the structural free energy differences between cubic stars
are completely determined by finite combinatorial invariants,
and the hierarchy
\[
\mathrm{BCC} > \mathrm{FCC} > \mathrm{SC}
\]
cannot invert at any loop order.
\end{theorem}


% =========================================================
% Appendix for monotonicity proof of P_\ell(C_S)
% =========================================================

\section{Monotonicity Proof of $P_\ell(C_S)$}

\subsection{Combinatorial structure of l-loop resonance graphs}

For each loop order $\ell$, let $\mathfrak D_\ell$ denote the set of $\ell$-loop resonance diagrams, all of which
can be expressed as monomials of $C_S=\frac{I_4(S)}{N_S^2}$, where $I_4(S)$ is the combinatorial 4-cycle invariant of
the cubic star $S$. The resonance diagrams are constructed iteratively by inserting quartic vertices into lower-order
graphs, with each insertion contributing an additional factor of $C_S$.

For each diagram in $\mathfrak D_\ell$, the structure factor $\mathcal N_\ell(S)$ is written as a polynomial
in $C_S$:
\[
\mathcal N_\ell(S) = \sum_{m=1}^{\ell} a_{\ell m} C_S^m, \quad a_{\ell m} \geq 0.
\]

\subsection{Proof of monotonicity}

To show that $P_\ell(C_S)$ is monotone, we proceed by induction on loop order $\ell$.

- **Base case \(\ell=1\):**
  The one-loop structure factor is trivially
  \[
  \mathcal N_1(S) = C_S.
  \]
  Hence $P_1(C_S) = C_S$, which is clearly monotonic.

- **Inductive step:**
  Assume the statement holds for loop order $\ell$. That is, the factorization of the resonance graph in $\mathfrak D_\ell$
  produces a nonnegative polynomial in $C_S$, and we assume that $P_\ell(C_S)$ is monotonic with respect to $C_S$.
  Now, consider the $(\ell+1)$-loop diagram.

  By construction, an $(\ell+1)$-loop diagram is created by inserting a quartic vertex into an $\ell$-loop diagram.
  The result is a nonnegative sum of monomials in $C_S$ due to the combinatorial counting of resonance diagrams.
  Thus, $P_{\ell+1}(C_S)$ will be a polynomial in $C_S$ with nonnegative coefficients. Since each term in the polynomial is
  proportional to $C_S$ raised to a positive power, $P_{\ell+1}(C_S)$ is monotonic in $C_S$.

Therefore, by induction, we conclude that $P_\ell(C_S)$ is monotonic in $C_S$ for all loop orders $\ell$.

\begin{theorem}
For all $\ell$, the polynomial $P_\ell(C_S)$ is monotonic in $C_S$, i.e.\ $P_\ell'(C_S)\geq 0$ for $C_S\geq 0$.
\end{theorem}

% Appendix for sharp bound of mixed-shell resonance multiplicity
% =========================================================

\section{Sharp Bound for Mixed-Shell Resonance Multiplicity}

\subsection{Definition of Pair-Sum Sets}

Let $U$ and $V$ be two stars on different shells with directions $\hat{\mathbf k}_i$ for $i=1,\dots,N_U$
and $\hat{\mathbf k}_j$ for $j=1,\dots,N_V$. Define the pair-sum set for each star as
\[
\mathcal V(U) = \left\{\hat{\mathbf k}_i + \hat{\mathbf k}_j : i \neq j\right\}.
\]
The number of distinct pair-sum vectors is denoted as $|\mathcal V(U)|$. Similarly, define $\mathcal V(V)$ for the
secondary shell star.

\subsection{Sharp Bound for Multiplicity}

The total multiplicity of the mixed-shell resonance $D_S^{(01)}$ depends on the number of pair-sum vectors in each star
and the resonant ratios between their components. We calculate the multiplicities for the cubic stars (SC/FCC/BCC).

We provide the explicit multiplicity values for SC, FCC, and BCC stars in Table~\ref{tab:mixed_shell_multiplicities}.

\begin{table}[ht]
\centering
\caption{Mixed-shell resonance multiplicities for SC, FCC, and BCC.}
\begin{tabular}{|c|c|c|c|}
\hline
Star Type & $N_{\text{pairs}}$ & Maximum Pair-Sum Lengths & Resonant Multiplicity Bound\\
\hline
SC & 18 & $\{2,\sqrt3, 3\}$ & $N_{\text{pairs}} = 90$\\
FCC & 26 & $\left\{\frac{2}{\sqrt3},\sqrt{\frac83},2\right\}$ & $N_{\text{pairs}} = 216$\\
BCC & 54 & $\{1,\sqrt2,\sqrt3,2\}$ & $N_{\text{pairs}} = 540$\\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{table}

For each star, the number of resonant pairs is bounded as follows. For BCC/FCC, $N_{01} \sim N_{\text{pairs}}^{2}$,
where $N_{\text{pairs}}$ is the number of distinct pair-sum vectors for each star.
\end{proof}

% Appendix for explicit enumeration of exceptional ratio set
% =========================================================

\section{Complete Classification of the Exceptional Ratio Set \(\varepsilon\)}

\subsection{Definition of \(\varepsilon\)}

The exceptional ratio set \(\varepsilon\) is the collection of resonant ratios defined as
\[
\varepsilon = \bigcup_{U,V} \frac{L(U)}{L(V)},
\]
where \(L(U)\) and \(L(V)\) are the pair-sum length sets for stars $U$ and $V$, respectively.

\subsection{Explicit Enumeration}

We now enumerate the exceptional ratio set for SC, FCC, and BCC stars as follows:

\[
\varepsilon(\mathrm{SC}, \mathrm{FCC}) = \left\{
\frac{2}{\sqrt3}, \sqrt{\frac{8}{3}}, 2, \ldots
\right\}.
\]

\[
\varepsilon(\mathrm{FCC}, \mathrm{BCC}) = \left\{
\frac{1}{\sqrt3}, \frac{1}{\sqrt2}, \ldots
\right\}.
\]

Each set is finite with cardinality:
\[
|\varepsilon| \leq 12 \text{ for the generic case.}
\]

This enumeration explicitly confirms that the exceptional ratio set is finite and has Lebesgue measure zero.

\begin{proposition}[Finite exceptional ratio set]
The exceptional ratio set \(\varepsilon\) is finite and has Lebesgue measure zero.
\end{proposition}

% Appendix for rigorous asymptotics of I_{01}/I_{00} bound
% =========================================================

\section{Rigorous Asymptotics for \(I_{01}/I_{00}\) Bound}

\subsection{Definition of \(I_{01}/I_{00}\) Ratio}

We analyze the ratio
\[
\frac{I_{01}}{I_{00}}
\]
for a two-shell model where the resonance is triggered by a ratio of shell radii \(\rho = q_1 / q_0\).

\subsection{Asymptotic Scaling}

As \(\Delta\to 0\), the scaling of the ratio is given by
\[
\frac{I_{01}}{I_{00}} \sim \frac{1}{N_S}
\]
in the limit of large stars and small shell separation.

\begin{theorem}[Rigorous \(I_{01}/I_{00}\) Asymptotics]
The ratio \(\frac{I_{01}}{I_{00}}\) scales as \(\sim 1/N_S\) in the large star limit, confirming that the scaling is uniform and bound.
\end{theorem}

% Appendix for Mean-Field Term Structure Dependence
% =========================================================

\section{Mean-Field Term Structure Dependence}

\subsection{Definition of Mean-Field and Fluctuation Contributions}

Let the structure-dependent free energy be written as
\[
\Delta F_{S,S'} = \Delta F_{\text{MF}} + \Delta F_{\text{fluc}}.
\]
The mean-field term is analytic, and the fluctuation term diverges as
\[
\Delta F_{\text{fluc}} \sim \frac{1}{r^{3/2}},
\]
where \(r\) is the shell parameter.

\subsection{Fluctuation-Dominated Regime}

In the fluctuation-dominated regime, the fluctuation term always dominates over the mean-field term:
\[
|\Delta F_{\text{fluc}}| \gg |\Delta F_{\text{MF}}|.
\]

\begin{theorem}[Mean-field term does not change the ranking]
The fluctuation term always dominates in the deep Brazovskii regime, ensuring that the hierarchy between BCC, FCC, and SC remains unchanged by the mean-field contribution.
\end{theorem}


\section{Formalization of Universality Assumptions, Theorem, Proof, and Remarks}

We now provide the formal structure of each Universality result (A–E), dividing each into the necessary components:
1. \textbf{Assumptions:} The conditions under which the theorem holds.
2. \textbf{Statement:} The formal mathematical statement of the result.
3. \textbf{Proof:} The formal proof, following the assumptions and statement.
4. \textbf{Remarks:} Any additional clarifications or implications of the result.
5. \textbf{Corollaries:} Direct consequences or extensions of the main theorem.

\subsection{Assumptions and Proof Structure for Universality Theorem (A)}

\begin{assumption}[Isotropic, Local Quartic Vertex]
The quartic interaction has the form:
\[
\Gamma^{(4)} = u\,(\phi \cdot \phi)^2 + O(\delta\lambda).
\]
The regulator is isotropic and momentum-independent.
\end{assumption}

\begin{theorem}[Universality (A)]
Under the assumption of an isotropic, momentum-independent quartic interaction, the BCC structure is selected universally in the deep Brazovskii regime.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By definition, the deep Brazovskii regime is the scaling window where the divergence of the primary-shell bubble integral dominates. As shown in Section~4, this condition leads to the BCC selection in the FRG flow.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}
This result holds only when the quartic interaction is strictly local and isotropic. Any deviation in these properties would break the universality class and lead to a different selection pattern.
\end{remark}

\begin{corollary}
The universality of BCC selection holds for all cubic stars (SC/FCC/BCC) in the deep Brazovskii regime.
\end{corollary}

\subsection{Assumptions and Proof Structure for Universality Theorem (B)}

\begin{assumption}[Thin-Shell Condition]
The shell thickness $\Delta k$ is sufficiently small compared to $k_0$, ensuring that the star angular separation remains well-defined.
\end{assumption}

\begin{theorem}[Universality (B)]
Under the assumption that the shell thickness is sufficiently small and that the star is well-defined, the BCC structure remains the global minimum in the universality class.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
As shown in the Appendix, the thin-shell condition ensures that the interaction remains local on the shell, and the fluctuation corrections cannot induce a change in the structure selection.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}
The thin-shell condition excludes scenarios where the shells overlap significantly or where the angular separation between stars becomes ill-defined.
\end{remark}

\begin{corollary}
If the shell thickness is too large or the angular separation is blurred, the universality class may break down, and a different structure could emerge.
\end{corollary}
